The Wolf's Speech: A Proof That God's Speech Is Uncreated
Imam Ashari uses the miraculous wolf speech to refute created speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Ashari uses the miraculous speech of the wolf to argue that God's speech is not created in a creature.

Core Idea
If a miracle speaks, its speech must be divine, not created.

Imam Ashari challenges the Mu'tazilite claim that God's speech is created in something else. He brings a powerful example: the wolf that spoke to testify to Muhammad's prophethood. This miraculous speech, if attributed to a created wolf, would lead to absurd consequences. Let's see how he forces the Mu'tazilites into a corner.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the question-and-answer style.
The passage is a rhetorical question to the Mu'tazilites.
2
Identify the Mu'tazilite premise
The Mu'tazilites believe God creates speech in another being. Understand this assumption.
This is the key premise Ashari uses against them.
3
Apply the premise to the wolf
If God creates speech in another, then the wolf's speech must be God's speech because it is miraculous.
4
Consider the reductio ad absurdum
If the wolf is the speaker, then the tree at Sinai could also be the speaker, leading to the blasphemy that a created tree said 'I am Allah.'
This shows the absurdity of the Mu'tazilite position.
5
Conclude the argument
Thus the Mu'tazilites must admit the wolf's speech is God's own speech, which contradicts their view that all speech is created.
The miraculous nature proves it is divine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يسألون عن الكلام الذي أنطق الله تعالى به الذئب لما أخبر عن نبوة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، فيقال لهم : إذا كان الله عز وجل يتكلم بكلام يخلقه في غيره، فما أنكرتم أن يكون الكلام الذي سمعه من الذئب كلاماً لله، ويكون إعجازه يدل على أنه كلام الله تعالى، وفي هذا ما يجب عليهم أن الذئب لم يتكلم به وأنه كلام الله عز وجل؛ لأن كون الكلام من الذئب معجز، كما أن كونه من الشجرة معجز، فإن كان الذئب متكلماً بذلك الكلام المنقول، فما أنكرتم أن الشجرة متكلمة بالكلام إن كان خُلِقَ في شجرة، وأن يكون المخلوق قال: ﴿ يَمُوسَى إِنّى أَنَا اللهُ ﴾ تعالى عن ذلك علواً كبيراً.
Then they are asked about the speech which Allah, Exalted, caused the wolf to utter when it informed of the prophethood of the Prophet (peace be upon him). It is said to them: If Allah, Exalted and Majestic, speaks by speech which He creates in something other than Himself, then why do you deny that the speech which was heard from the wolf is the speech of Allah, and that its miraculousness indicates that it is the speech of Allah, Exalted? And in this is what necessitates for them that the wolf did not speak it, and that it is the speech of Allah, Exalted and Majestic, because the occurrence of speech from the wolf is miraculous, just as its occurrence from the tree is miraculous. If the wolf is the speaker of that transmitted speech, then why do you deny that the tree is the speaker of the speech if it was created in a tree, and that the created being said: 'O Musa, indeed I am Allah'? Exalted is He above that, with great exaltation.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage presents a further argument against the Mu'tazilites by referring to the hadith in which a wolf spoke to a shepherd, testifying to the prophethood of Muhammad. The author argues: if God creates speech in something else, then the speech from the wolf must be God's speech because it is miraculous. The miraculous nature (إعجاز) demands that it be divine speech, not the wolf's own speech. If the wolf were the speaker, then by analogy, why not also accept that the tree was the speaker when God spoke to Musa? That would lead to the absurdity that a created being (a tree) claimed divinity by saying 'I am Allah.' Thus, the Mu'tazilites are forced to deny that the wolf spoke, which contradicts their principle that the speech is created in the animal.

Key Terms
ذئب
إعجاز
معجز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think Imam Ashari is disputing the authenticity of the wolf story. Actually, he uses it as a valid premise to highlight logical inconsistency.
Correction: The argument does not depend on whether the story is authentic; it is a hypothetical that exposes the flaw in the Mu'tazilite principle.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Ashari's argument, what does the miraculous speech of the wolf indicate?
A) That wolves can speak like humans
B) That the speech was created in the wolf
C) That the speech must be God's speech
D) That the wolf is a prophet

Key Takeaway
The miraculous speech of the wolf proves it cannot be created speech; it must be the uncreated speech of Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The wolf spoke a truth about prophethood. When you hear the Quran, do you hear it as the very speech of Allah, or as just another story? What in your life needs to change so that every verse trembles your heart?
?
The Mu'tazilites thought they were defending God's transcendence by saying His speech is created. Are there areas in your worship where you try to 'protect' Allah with your own reasoning, only to fall into error? Will you submit to the revealed truth even when it challenges your logic?
?
If the wolf's speech could not be created speech, then the Quran is directly from Allah, not a created thing. When you recite a verse, do you feel the weight that you are uttering the uncreated? Commit today to recite at least one verse with the awe that it is Allah speaking to you.

Livingness Requirement for Speech Creation Refuted
Imam Ashari refutes the objection that speech can only be created in a living being.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Ashari's refutation of the Mu'tazilite objection that speech can only be created in a living being, and how he uses logical consistency and a Quranic verse to undermine their position.

Core Idea
God's speech is not limited by the livingness of its locus.

Imam Ashari now turns to a potential objection from the Mu'tazilites: that speech can only be created in a living being, so how could the Quran be created in the tree? He counters with a logical inversion, showing the inconsistency of their own position. He also invokes the Quranic testimony that the heavens and earth 'spoke' to Allah, further undermining the objection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation together. Notice how the objection is presented and then refuted.
Pay attention to the logical structure: 'if... then...'.
2
Identify the opponent's objection
The Mu'tazilites argue that speech can only originate in a living being, so the tree cannot be the speaker of the Quran.
3
Understand Ashari's counter-argument
Ashari turns the objection around: if speech is created in a non-living thing (tree), then the creator of that speech (Allah) is living, so there is no contradiction. If they insist on livingness, then they must explain why Allah cannot create speech in a non-living thing.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
4
Examine the Quranic evidence
Ashari cites Quran 41:11 where the heavens and earth 'speak' to Allah, showing that inanimate objects can be described as speaking by Allah's power.
This verse is used to support the permissibility of speech being attributed to non-living things.
5
Reflect on the logical implication
Consider how this argument defends the orthodox view that the Quran is created in a specific location (the tree) while affirming that Allah is the sole Creator and Speaker.
This refutes the Mu'tazilite claim that speech requires a living subject.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال لهم : إذا كان كلام الله عز وجل مخلوقاً في غيره عندكم، فما يؤمنكم أن يكون كل كلام تسمعونه مخلوقاً في شيء، وهو حق أن يكون كلام الله عز وجل؟ فإن قالوا: لا تكون الشجرة متكلمة ؛ لأن المتكلم لا يكون إلا حياً . قيل لهم ولا يجوز خَلْقُ الكلام في شجرة؛ لأن من خَلَقَ الكلام فيه لا يكون إلا حياً، فإن جاز أن يُخلَقَ الكلام فيما ليس بحي، فلم لا يجوز أن يتكلم من ليس بحي؟ ويقال لهم : لم لا قلتم إنه يقول من ليس بحي، لأنه عز وجل أخبر أن السماوات والأرض: ﴿ قَالَتَا أَتَيْنَا طَائِعِينَ ﴾ [فصلت: ١١].
Then it is said to them: If the speech of Allah, Exalted and Majestic, is created in something other than Himself according to you, then what prevents you from thinking that every speech you hear is created in something, and that it is truly the speech of Allah, Exalted and Majestic? If they say: The tree cannot be a speaker, because a speaker is only living. It is said to them: It is also not permissible to create speech in a tree, because the one who creates speech in it is only living. If it is permissible that speech be created in that which is not living, then why is it not permissible that one who is not living speaks? And it is said to them: Why do you not say that one who is not living speaks, because He, Exalted and Majestic, informed that the heavens and the earth: 'They said, "We come willingly."'
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage is a response to a possible objection from the Mu'tazilites. They might argue that the tree cannot be the speaker because speech requires a living agent. The author turns the objection around: if speech can be created in something non-living (like a tree), then the creator of that speech (God) is living. So there is no problem. But if they insist that only a living being can be the locus of speech, then why do they allow God to create speech in a tree? The author also cites the Quranic verse where the heavens and earth speak, indicating that inanimate objects can be used by God to 'speak' in a metaphorical sense. This undercuts the Mu'tazilite claim that speech cannot originate from non-living things.

Key Terms
حي
خلق الكلام
السماوات والأرض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the argument is about physical speech by inanimate objects, but it is about the logical consistency of the opponents' position.
Correction: The argument is a logical reductio against the Mu'tazilite condition that speech requires a living locus. It does not claim that trees literally speak, but that if speech can be created in a non-living thing, then the non-living thing can be said to 'speak' metaphorically by God's power.

Checkpoint
How does Imam Ashari counter the objection that a speaker must be living?
A) He denies that God is living
B) He cites a Quranic verse where heavens and earth speak
C) He argues that trees are alive
D) He says that speech does not require a speaker

Key Takeaway
Imam Ashari refutes the livingness requirement by showing that if speech can be created in a non-living thing, then the living one is the Creator, and the non-living can be said to 'speak' by God's action, as evidenced by the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that the heavens and earth 'said, We come willingly', do you truly accept that God can make inanimate objects speak, or does your mind resist because it feels impossible? What does that resistance reveal about your reliance on your own reasoning over divine revelation? Will you commit to affirming what Allah has said, even when it defies your logical expectations?
?
The Mu'tazilites argued that speech can only come from a living being, and they used that to deny that the Quran is God's eternal speech. Have you ever placed a condition on God's power based on your own limited understanding of how things work? What condition would you repent of today?
?
If God can create speech in a tree and still call it His speech, then your own ability to speak is ultimately a gift from Him. Do you use your speech to honor Him as the true source of all speech, or do you act as if your words are your own? What will you say differently tomorrow to acknowledge His sovereignty over your tongue?

The Curse on Iblis Proves God's Speech is Uncreated
Imam Ashari uses the eternal curse on Iblis to argue that God's speech cannot be created.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Ashari uses the Qur'anic curse on Iblis to argue that God's speech must be eternal and not created.

Core Idea
The eternal curse on Iblis proves God's speech cannot be created.

In this passage, Imam Ashari presents a concise logical argument against the Mu'tazilite claim that God's speech is created. He cites the Qur'anic verse where Allah curses Iblis until the Day of Judgment, and then draws a necessary implication: if the speech were created, it would be perishable, but the curse endures, so it cannot be created. This argument underscores the distinction between God's eternal attributes and temporary created things.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic text and its literal translation. Note the question-and-answer format and the logical structure.
The argument is cut off at the end, but the main premises are clear.
2
Identify the key premise
Find the verse about the curse and note its duration: 'until the Day of Judgment'. Then observe the conditional statement: if speech is created, it is perishable.
The word 'fānīyāt' means perishable things.
3
Understand the logical implication
Combine the two premises: the curse is permanent, but created things are perishable. Therefore, the curse (and by extension God's speech) cannot be created. Try to complete the missing conclusion in your own words.
This reasoning shows the necessity of God's speech being uncreated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال لهم : أليس قد قال الله عز وجل لإبليس : ﴿ وَإِنَّ عَلَيْكَ لَعْنَى إِلَى يَوْمِ الدِّينِ ﴾ [ص: ٧٨] فلا بد من نعم، ويقال لهم : فإذا كان كلام الله مخلوقاً، وكانت المخلوقات فانيات؛ فيلزمكم إذا أفنى الله عز وجل الأشياء أن تكون
Then it is said to them: Did not Allah, Exalted and Majestic, say to Iblis: 'And indeed, upon you is My curse until the Day of Judgment'? They must answer yes. And it is said to them: If the speech of Allah is created, and created things are perishable, then it necessarily follows for you that when Allah, Exalted and Majestic, annihilates all things, that
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage introduces a further argument against the createdness of God's speech. The author asks the Mu'tazilites to affirm that God cursed Iblis until the Day of Judgment. Then he argues: if God's speech (the curse) is created, then it is subject to annihilation like all other created things. But the curse is explicitly stated to last until the Day of Judgment, implying its permanence. Therefore, it cannot be created. The argument is cut off, but the conclusion is that the curse must be eternal (uncreated).

Key Terms
لعنة
إبليس
فانيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the argument is about the literal pronunciation or physical sound of the curse, not the divine attribute of speech.
Correction: The argument focuses on the nature of God's speech as an eternal attribute, not on its temporal expression. The curse is a form of God's speech, and its permanence indicates that God's speech itself is eternal and uncreated.

Checkpoint
What does the curse on Iblis imply about God's speech according to Imam Ashari?
A) That it is created like other things
B) That it is non-existent
C) That it must be eternal and uncreated
D) That it is only metaphorical

Key Takeaway
The curse on Iblis, being perpetual until the Day of Judgment, demonstrates that God's speech is not subject to annihilation and thus is uncreated and eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's curse on Iblis is eternal and uncreated, what does that imply about the permanence of God's words in your own life? When Allah promises or warns you, do you take it as seriously as if it were written in stone?
?
The Mu'tazilites thought God's speech was created and therefore temporary. Are there aspects of Allah's commands in your life that you treat as temporary or negotiable? Which ones?
?
Iblis's curse is everlasting. How does that reality shape your view of disobeying Allah? Does the permanence of divine justice make you fear sin more?

Refuting the Mu'tazilite Objection on Speech Locus
Al-Ash'ari refutes the Mu'tazilite objection that only a living being can be the locus of God's speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God can create speech in non-living things, and that the Quran itself attributes speech to non-living beings, refuting the Mu'tazilite claim.

Core Idea
God's speech is not limited to living beings; He creates it wherever He wills.

Al-Ash'ari presents a crisp logical refutation of the Mu'tazilite claim that only a living being can be the locus of God's speech. He first turns their own assumptions against them, then seals the argument with a Quranic example. This passage is a masterclass in theological argumentation, showing how scripture and reason work together.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the back-and-forth structure: Al-Ash'ari poses a question, presents the Mu'tazilite objection, then refutes it.
The argument is dialectical, typical of kalam.
2
Identify the Mu'tazilite position
What exactly do the Mu'tazilites claim about where speech must be created? Look for their objection about the tree.
They claim only a living being can be the subject of speech.
3
Follow Al-Ash'ari's refutation
Al-Ash'ari uses a reductio ad absurdum: if speech is created in a non-living thing, then that thing can be described as speaking. He then cites the Quranic verse about the heavens and earth speaking.
4
Reflect on the broader principle
This argument establishes that God's speech is not dependent on a living locus. It can be created in anything, and the Quranic description overrides human assumptions.
This is a key point in the doctrine of the uncreatedness of the Quran.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال لهم : إذا كان كلام الله عز وجل مخلوقاً في غيره عندكم، فما يؤمنكم أن يكون كل كلام تسمعونه مخلوقاً في شيء، وهو حق أن يكون كلام الله عز وجل؟ فإن قالوا: لا تكون الشجرة متكلمة ؛ لأن المتكلم لا يكون إلا حياً . قيل لهم ولا يجوز خَلْقُ الكلام في شجرة؛ لأن من خَلَقَ الكلام فيه لا يكون إلا حياً، فإن جاز أن يُخلَقَ الكلام فيما ليس بحي، فلم لا يجوز أن يتكلم من ليس بحي؟ ويقال لهم : لم لا قلتم إنه يقول من ليس بحي، لأنه عز وجل أخبر أن السماوات والأرض: ( قَالَتَا أَنينا طايعينَ ) [فصلت : ١١] .
Then it is said to them: If the speech of Allah Almighty is created in other than Him according to you, what prevents you from thinking that every speech you hear is created in something, and it is true that it is the speech of Allah Almighty? If they say: The tree cannot be speaking because the speaker is only alive. It is said to them: And it is not permissible to create speech in a tree because the one who creates speech in it is only alive. If it is permissible that speech be created in what is not alive, then why is it not permissible for what is not alive to speak? And it is said to them: Why do you not say that what is not alive speaks, because He Almighty informed that the heavens and the earth (both said: 'We come willingly') [Fussilat:11].
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazilite claim that God's speech must be created in a living subject. Al-Ash'ari uses a logical argument: If the Mu'tazilites allow that God's speech can be created in a non-living thing (like the wolf or tree, as claimed earlier), then any speech we hear could potentially be God's speech. When they object that a tree cannot be a speaker because only a living being can speak, Al-Ash'ari turns their own logic against them: if speech is created in a non-living thing by God, then the act of creation is performed by a living being (God), but the locus itself does not need to be alive. The analogy with the wolf (mentioned earlier) shows inconsistency. He then supports this with Quranic evidence: the heavens and the earth spoke, proving that non-living things can be described as speaking when God creates speech in them.

Key Terms
كلام الله
مخلوق
الشجرة
المتكلم
حي
إعجاز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only a living being can be the locus of speech, so God's speech must be created in a living being.
Correction: The Quran attributes speech to non-living things (e.g., heavens and earth), and God can create speech in anything without the locus needing to be alive.

Checkpoint
What is the Mu'tazilite objection that Al-Ash'ari addresses in this passage?
A) That only a living being can be a speaker.
B) That the Quran was revealed in Arabic.
C) That the wolf spoke literally.
D) That God's speech is eternal.

Key Takeaway
God's speech is not bound to a living locus; He creates it in anything, as evidenced by the Quran's attribution of speech to the heavens and earth.

The Curse on Iblis: Proof that God's Speech is Uncreated
Al-Ash'ari argues that the permanence of God's curse on Iblis proves His speech is uncreated.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Ash'ari uses the Quranic verse about Iblis's curse to argue that God's speech is uncreated and eternal.

Core Idea
The permanence of God's curse on Iblis proves His speech is eternal.

Al-Ash'ari presents a logical argument grounded in the Quran. He challenges the Mu'tazilite view that God's speech is created by pointing to a specific verse: God's curse on Iblis lasts until the Day of Judgment. If the curse were created, it would perish with all creation, contradicting the Quran. This lesson walks through that argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic premise
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Pay special attention to the verse quoted: 'And indeed upon you is My curse until the Day of Judgment.' This is the foundation of Al-Ash'ari's reasoning.
The Day of Judgment is interpreted as the Day of Recompense, referring to eternal punishment.
2
Understand the conditional argument
Al-Ash'ari sets up a conditional: If God's speech is created, then it must be perishable like all created things. Apply this to the curse: if it perishes, Iblis would no longer be accursed, which contradicts the verse.
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.
3
Follow the conclusion
Since the curse cannot perish (it remains until and beyond the Day of Judgment), it cannot be created. Therefore, God's speech (the curse being an instance of it) is uncreated and eternal.
This ties the attribute of speech to divine eternity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة : ثم يقال لهم : أليس قد قال الله عز وجل لإبليس : ﴿ وَإِنَّ عَلَيْكَ لَعْنَى إِلَى يوم الدين ) [ ص:۷۸] فلا بد من نعم، ويقال لهم : فإذا كان كلام الله مخلوقاً، وكانت المخلوقات فانيات؛ فيلزمكم إذا أفنى الله عز وجل الأشياء أن تكون اللعنة على إبليس قد فنيت، فيكون إبليس غير ملعون، وهذا ترك لدين المسلمين ، وردُّ لقول الله عز وجل: ﴿وَإِنَّ عَلَيْكَ لَعَنَتِي إِلَى يَوْمِ الدِّينِ ). وإذا كانت اللعنة باقية على إبليس إلى يوم الدين - وهو يوم الجزاء، وهـو يـوم القيامة - لأن الله عز وجل قال: ﴿ مَلِكِ يوم الدين ﴾ [الفاتحة: ٤] يعني يوم الجزاء، ثم هي أبداً في النار، واللعنة كلام الله ، وهو قوله : (عَلَيْكَ لَعَنَتِي ) فقد وجب أن يكون كلام الله عز وجل لا يجوز عليه الفناء، وأنه غير مخلوق ؛ لأن المخلوقات يجوز عليها العدم، فإذا لم يجز ذلك على كلام الله عز وجل فهو غير مخلوق .
Issue: Then it is said to them: Did not Allah Almighty say to Iblis: 'And indeed upon you is My curse until the Day of Judgment' [Sad:78]? Then it must be yes. And it is said to them: If the speech of Allah is created, and created things are perishable, then it follows upon you that when Allah annihilates things, the curse upon Iblis would have perished, and thus Iblis would not be accursed. This is abandoning the religion of the Muslims and rejecting the statement of Allah Almighty: 'And indeed upon you is My curse until the Day of Judgment.' And if the curse remains upon Iblis until the Day of Judgment—which is the Day of Recompense, and it is the Day of Resurrection—because Allah Almighty said: 'Master of the Day of Judgment' [Al-Fatiha:4], meaning the Day of Recompense, then it is forever in the Fire. And the curse is the speech of Allah, and it is His saying: 'Upon you is My curse.' So it is necessary that the speech of Allah Almighty cannot be subject to annihilation, and that it is uncreated, because created things are subject to non-existence. Since that is not permissible for the speech of Allah Almighty, it is uncreated.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the uncreatedness of God's speech based on the permanence of His curse on Iblis. Al-Ash'ari begins by asking the Mu'tazilites to affirm that God said to Iblis: 'Indeed upon you is My curse until the Day of Judgment.' They must agree. He then presents a logical consequence: if God's speech (including this curse) is created, then like all created things, it would be subject to annihilation when God destroys all things. That would mean the curse perishes, and Iblis would no longer be accursed, contradicting the Quranic text. Al-Ash'ari explains that the Day of Judgment is the Day of Recompense (as in Surah Al-Fatiha), and the curse remains forever in the Fire. Since the curse is God's speech, and it endures forever, it cannot be subject to annihilation. Therefore, God's speech must be uncreated, as created things are contingent and can cease to exist.

Key Terms
لعنة
إبليس
يوم الدين
كلام الله
مخلوق
غير مخلوق
فناء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A curse from God might be a temporary speech act that could expire or be revoked.
Correction: The Quran explicitly states that the curse on Iblis lasts until the Day of Judgment and continues forever in the Fire, proving it is eternal and uncreated.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Ash'ari's argument, what would happen to the curse on Iblis if God's speech were created?
A) It would remain forever.
B) It would be annihilated when God destroys all things.
C) It would become a blessing.
D) It would be transferred to another being.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari uses the permanence of God's curse on Iblis to demonstrate that God's speech is uncreated and eternal, as it cannot perish like created things.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The curse on Iblis is permanent and uncreated. This means God's threats are just as real as His promises. Are you living as though every warning in the Quran is an unchangeable reality? Which warning have you been ignoring that demands immediate repentance?

God's Anger and Pleasure are Uncreated, Therefore His Speech is Uncreated
Al-Ash'ari refutes the createdness of God's speech by analogy with His anger and pleasure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Al-Ash'ari argues that God's speech must be uncreated based on the analogy with His anger and pleasure.

Core Idea
If God's anger is eternal, so is His speech.

Al-Ash'ari challenges the Mu'tazilite view that God's speech is created by using a logical analogy. Since they already agree that God's anger, pleasure, and displeasure are uncreated attributes, why should speech be any different? He then shows the absurd consequences of saying anger is created, which would imply that God changes—a clear violation of divine perfection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the English translation. Let the author's argumentative flow come through before you interpret.
Notice how the passage is structured as a refutation (الرد).
2
Identify the analogy and the reductio
Highlight the conditional statement: if anger is uncreated, then speech is uncreated. Then find the reductio ad absurdum: if anger were created, it would perish, leading to the impossibility of God being pleased or displeased.
The reductio shows the theological danger of holding that divine attributes are created.
3
Reflect on the consequence
Ask yourself: Why does Al-Ash'ari say that claiming God's anger is created is 'exit from Islam'? Think about what it implies about God's immutability and His relationship with creation.
This connects to the core belief that God's attributes are eternal and unchanging.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرد : ثم يقال لهم : إذا كان غضب الله غير مخلوق، وكذلك رضاه وسخطه، فلم لا قلتم : إن كلامه غير مخلوق؟ ومن زعم أن غضب الله مخلوق لزمه أن غضب الله وسخطه على الكافرين يفنى، وأن رضاه عن الملائكة والنبيين يفنى، حتى لا يكون راضياً عن أوليائه ولا ساخطاً عن أعدائه، وهذا هو الخروج عن الإسلام .
The refutation: Then it is said to them: If the anger of Allah is uncreated, and likewise His pleasure and displeasure, then why do you not say that His speech is uncreated? And whoever claims that the anger of Allah is created, it follows that the anger and displeasure of Allah upon the disbelievers would perish, and His pleasure upon the angels and prophets would perish, so that He would not be pleased with His allies nor displeased with His enemies, and this is exit from Islam.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazilite position that God's speech is created, using an analogy from God's other attributes: anger, pleasure, and displeasure. Al-Ash'ari begins with a conditional: if the Mu'tazilites already agree that God's anger and pleasure are uncreated (as attributes of God), then why do they not apply the same logic to His speech? He then shows the consequences if one were to claim God's anger is created: it would imply that God's anger and displeasure against disbelievers would eventually perish, and likewise His pleasure towards the angels and prophets. This would lead to the absurd conclusion that God ceases to be pleased with His allies and displeased with His enemies, which contradicts the Quran and sound theology. Such a position, Al-Ash'ari asserts, is tantamount to leaving Islam.

Correction: Anger and pleasure are not temporal emotions in God; they are eternal attributes that do not change or perish. Saying they are created would imply God is subject to change, which is impossible.

Proving God's Speech is Uncreated from the Curse on Iblis
Imam Ashari argues for the uncreatedness of God's speech from the eternal curse on Iblis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Ashari uses the eternal curse on Iblis to prove that God's speech is uncreated and not subject to annihilation.

Core Idea
If God's curse on Iblis is eternal, then God's speech must be uncreated.

Imam Ashari presents a concise proof from the Quranic verse about the curse on Iblis. He argues that the eternal nature of the curse implies that God's speech, which is the curse, cannot perish. This leads to the conclusion that God's speech is uncreated, unlike created things which are subject to annihilation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the literal translation. Let the author's argument unfold naturally.
Notice how the argument uses a conditional statement: if the curse perished, then Iblis would not be cursed.
2
Identify the logical structure
Break down the argument into premises and conclusion. What are the key verses quoted? How does the author connect the curse to God's speech?
The chain is: curse remains forever → curse is God's speech → God's speech is eternal → therefore uncreated.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider why the uncreatedness of God's speech matters for divine attributes. Contrast with created things that can perish.
This argument safeguards God's attribute of speech from being temporally created.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اللعنة على إبليس قد فنيت، فيكون إبليس غير ملعون، وهذا ترك لدين المسلمين ، وردُّ لقول الله عز وجل: ﴿وَإِنَّ عَلَيْكَ لَعَنَتِي إِلَى يَوْمِ الدِّينِ ). وإذا كانت اللعنة باقية على إبليس إلى يوم الدين - وهو يوم الجزاء، وهـو يـوم القيامة - لأن الله عز وجل قال: ﴿ مَلِكِ يوم الدين ﴾ [الفاتحة: ٤] يعني يوم الجزاء، ثم هي أبداً في النار، واللعنة كلام الله ، وهو قوله : (عَلَيْكَ لَعَنَتِي ) فقد وجب أن يكون كلام الله عز وجل لا يجوز عليه الفناء، وأنه غير مخلوق ؛ لأن المخلوقات يجوز عليها العدم، فإذا لم يجز ذلك على كلام الله عز وجل فهو غير مخلوق .
The curse upon Iblis has perished, so Iblis would be not cursed, and this is an abandonment of the religion of the Muslims, and a rejection of the saying of Allah Almighty: {And indeed, upon you is My curse until the Day of Judgment}. And if the curse remains upon Iblis until the Day of Judgment - and it is the Day of Recompense, and it is the Day of Resurrection - because Allah Almighty said: {Owner of the Day of Judgment} [Al-Fatiha: 4] meaning the Day of Recompense, then it is forever in the Fire, and the curse is the speech of Allah, and it is His saying: {upon you is My curse}. Then it is necessary that the speech of Allah Almighty does not admit perishing, and that it is uncreated; because created things admit non-existence, and if that is not permissible for the speech of Allah Almighty, then it is uncreated.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a proof from the eternity of God's curse on Iblis that God's speech is uncreated. The argument proceeds as follows: If someone claims that God's curse on Iblis has perished (i.e., is not eternal), then Iblis would no longer be cursed, which contradicts the Quranic verse that the curse remains until the Day of Judgment. Therefore, the curse is eternal and remains forever. Since the curse is God's speech (the words 'upon you is My curse'), and it cannot perish, it must be uncreated, because created things are subject to annihilation. Thus, God's speech is uncreated.

Correction: The curse is God's eternal speech; it remains until the Day of Judgment and beyond, proving it is uncreated and not subject to annihilation.

Key Takeaway

The Consistency Argument for Uncreated Speech
Imam Ashari refutes opponents using a consistency dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Ashari uses a logical consistency argument to affirm that God's speech is uncreated, based on the uncreatedness of other attributes like wrath.

Core Idea
Consistency demands: if God's wrath is eternal, so is His speech.

In this passage, Imam Ashari engages in polemical debate with those who deny the uncreatedness of the Quran. He uses a clever argument from consistency: if they accept that God's attributes of wrath and pleasure are uncreated (as most do), then they must also accept that His speech is uncreated. Alternatively, if they claim wrath is created, that leads to a theological absurdity—God's anger and pleasure would cease, contradicting scripture.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Notice the rhetorical style of the rebuttal.
This passage is a direct address to opponents.
2
Identify the two conditional arguments
The passage presents two 'if...then' statements. Find them and understand their logical structure. The first links uncreatedness of wrath to uncreatedness of speech. The second shows the absurd consequence if wrath were created.
3
Reflect on the charge of apostasy
Consider why the author calls the consequence 'apostasy from Islam'. How does this strengthen the argument? Think about the implications for God's eternal attributes.
This shows the serious nature of the theological error.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال لهم : إذا كان غضب الله غير مخلوق، وكذلك رضاه وسخطه، فلم لا قلتم : إن كلامه غير مخلوق؟ ومن زعم أن غضب الله مخلوق لزمه أن غضب الله وسخطه على الكافرين يفنى، وأن رضاه عن الملائكة والنبيين يفنى، حتى لا يكون راضياً عن أوليائه ولا ساخطاً عن أعدائه، وهذا هو الخروج عن الإسلام .
Then it is said to them: If the wrath of Allah is uncreated, as well as His pleasure and displeasure, then why do you not say that His speech is uncreated? And whoever claims that the wrath of Allah is created, it follows that the wrath and displeasure of Allah upon the disbelievers perishes, and His pleasure upon the angels and the prophets perishes, so that He is not pleased with His friends nor displeased with His enemies, and this is apostasy from Islam.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a rebuttal (الرد) against those who deny the uncreatedness of God's speech. The author presents a dilemma: If you admit that God's wrath, pleasure, and displeasure are uncreated attributes (as many opponents do), then consistency requires that you also admit that His speech is uncreated. If, on the other hand, you claim that God's wrath is created, then it would be subject to perishing, leading to the absurd consequence that God's anger against disbelievers and His pleasure with believers would cease to exist. That would mean God is no longer pleased with His friends or displeased with His enemies, which is a denial of clear Quranic teachings and constitutes apostasy.

The Command 'Be' Proves the Quran is Uncreated
Imam Ashari uses a logical dilemma from the verse 'Be' to argue for the uncreated Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical argument that the command 'Be' in the Quran is uncreated and why this supports the belief that the Quran is uncreated.

Core Idea
If God's command 'Be' were created, it would require an infinite chain of commands — an impossibility.

Imam Ashari presents a powerful logical dilemma to defend the uncreated nature of the Quran. By analyzing the verse about the command 'Be', he forces the opponent to either admit the Quran is uncreated or face an infinite regress. This passage demonstrates early Ashari reasoning on divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the structure: it begins with a question, presents two options, and draws a conclusion.
2
Identify the dilemma
The author presents a dilemma: if the command 'Be' is uncreated, then the Quran should be too; if it is created, that leads to infinite regress. Find these two horns of the dilemma.
3
Understand the infinite regress argument
If 'Be' were created, then God would need to say 'Be' to it, and so on forever. This is impossible. Connect this to why the command must be uncreated.
4
Apply the reasoning to the Quran
The author concludes that since 'Be' is uncreated, and the Quran is God's speech, the Quran is also uncreated. Note the parallel argument about God's will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۰۹ - مسألة : ويقال: خبرونا عن قول الله عز وجل : (إِنَّمَا قَوْلُنَا لِشَيْءٍ إِذَا أَرَدْنَهُ أَن تَقُولَ : لَهُ كُن فَيَكُونُ ﴾ [النحل: ٤٠] أتزعمون أن قوله للشيء: « كن» مخلوق مراد الله؟ فإن قالوا لا قيل لهم فما أنكرتم أن يكون كلام الله الذي هو القرآن غير مخلوق، كما زعمتم أن قول الله للشيء « كن » غير مخلوق وإن زعموا أن قول الله للشيء كن » مخلوق. قيل لهم : فإن زعمتم أنه مخلوق مراد الله ، فقد قال الله عز وجل : ( إِنَّمَا قَوْلُنَا لِشَيْءٍ إِذَا أَرَدْنَهُ أَن تَقُولَ لمر كن فيكون ) فيلزمكم أن قوله تعالى للشيء كن ) قد قال له : كن . وفي هذا ما يوجب أحد أمرين: -١- إما أن يكون قول الله لغيره ) كن ) غير مخلوق - أو يكون لكل قول قول لا إلى غاية، وذلك محال. فإن قالوا : إن الله قولاً غير مخلوق قيل لهم : فما أنكرتم أن تكون إرادة الله للإيمان غير مخلوقة؟ ثم يقال لهم : ما العلة التي إنما قلتم : إن قول الله للشيء ( كن ) غير مخلوق؟ فإن قالوا : لأن القول لا يقال له كن فيقال لهم: القرآن غير مخلوق ؛ لأنه قول الله والله لا يقول لقوله « كن » .
109 - Issue: And it is said: Inform us about the saying of Allah Almighty: {Our word to a thing when We intend it is to say to it 'Be' and it is} [An-Nahl: 40]. Do you claim that His saying to the thing 'Be' is created and intended by Allah? If they say no, it is said to them: Why do you not deny that the speech of Allah which is the Quran is uncreated, just as you claim that the saying of Allah to the thing 'Be' is uncreated? And if they claim that the saying of Allah to the thing 'Be' is created, it is said to them: If you claim that it is created and intended by Allah, then Allah Almighty said: {Our word to a thing when We intend it is to say to it 'Be' and it is}. So it follows for you that His saying to the thing 'Be' said to it 'Be'. And in this is what necessitates one of two things: 1. Either the saying of Allah to something 'Be' is uncreated, 2. Or every saying has a saying without end, and that is impossible. So if they say: Allah has an uncreated saying, it is said to them: Then why do you not deny that the will of Allah for faith is uncreated? Then it is said to them: What is the cause that made you say that the saying of Allah to the thing 'Be' is uncreated? If they say: Because the saying is not said to it 'Be', it is said to them: The Quran is uncreated, because it is the speech of Allah, and Allah does not say to His speech 'Be'.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a multi-step argument (مسألة) regarding the Quranic verse about the command 'Be'. The author first asks the opponents whether they consider God's word 'Be' to a thing when He intends it is created or uncreated. If they say it is uncreated, then why not admit the same for the Quran? If they say it is created, then a dilemma arises: since the verse says 'Our word to a thing ... is to say to it Be', if that 'Be' itself is created, then God would have to say 'Be' to that 'Be', leading to an infinite regress. This is impossible. Therefore, the 'Be' must be uncreated. Then, the author anticipates a possible objection: if the opponents concede that God has an uncreated speech (the command 'Be'), then they should also admit that God's will (irada) for faith is uncreated, because will is also an attribute. Finally, the author presents their ultimate answer: the reason 'Be' is uncreated is that 'Be' is speech, and speech is not spoken to; it is a direct attribute. Similarly, the Quran is God's speech, and God does not say 'Be' to His speech, so it too is uncreated. The conclusion is that the Quran is uncreated.

قول
مخلوق
غير مخلوق
مراد
إرادة

Misconception & Correction

Correction: The passage shows that if 'Be' were created, it would require an infinite regress of commands, which is impossible. Therefore, 'Be' must be uncreated.

A) It would mean God is not all-powerful
B) It would lead to an infinite regress of commands
C) It would make the Quran created

Key Takeaway
The command 'Be' must be uncreated because if it were created, it would lead to an infinite regress, and the Quran, being God's speech, is likewise uncreated.

God's Eternal Will Proves His Speech is Uncreated
Imam Ashari argues from God's eternal will for differentiation to the uncreated nature of His speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Ashari uses the opponents' own admission about God's eternal knowledge to argue that His will and speech must be uncreated.

Core Idea
God's eternal will proves His speech is uncreated.

Imam Ashari employs a clever dialectical argument to refute the Jahmiyyah, who denied that God's attributes are eternal. Starting from an agreed-upon point—God's eternal knowledge—he leads them to admit that God's will is likewise eternal, and therefore uncreated. He then asks: if the will is uncreated, why not the speech? This short but powerful exchange exposes the inconsistency in the Jahmiyyah's position.

Guided Path
1
Understand the dialogue structure
Read the passage as a back-and-forth between the Ashari and the Jahmiyyah. Notice the first question establishes a common ground.
The opponents cannot deny that God has eternal knowledge.
2
Identify the logical inference
From eternal knowledge, the argument moves to eternal will. If they admit eternal will, then it must be uncreated. Then the parallel to speech is drawn.
The key move is the analogy: both will and speech are attributes.
3
Consider the alternative
If they deny eternal will, they attribute deficiency to God. This reveals the absurdity of their position.
This strengthens the argument by showing the unacceptable consequence.

۱۱۰ - الرد على الجهمية : ويقال لهم : أليس لم يزل الله عالماً بأوليائه وأعدائه؟ فلا بد من نعم . قيل لهم: فهل تقولون : إنه لم يزل مريداً للتفرقة بين أوليائه وأعدائه؟ فإن قالوا نعم قيل لهم فإذا كانت إرادة الله لم تزل فهي غير مخلوقة وإذا كانت إرادته غير مخلوقة فلم لا قلتم : إن كلامه غير مخلوق؟ فإن قالوا: لا نقول لم يزل مريداً للتفريق بين أوليائه وأعدائه، فقد زعموا أن الله عز وجل لا يريد التفرقة بين أوليائه وأعدائه، ونسبوه سبحانه إلى النقص، تعالى الله عن قول القدرية علواً كبيراً
110 - Refutation of the Jahmiyyah: And it is said to them: Is it not that Allah has always been knowing of His friends and His enemies? So there is no avoiding 'yes'. It is said to them: Do you say that He has always been willing the differentiation between His friends and His enemies? If they say yes, it is said to them: Since the will of Allah has never ceased, it is uncreated. And if His will is uncreated, why do you not say that His speech is uncreated? And if they say: We do not say that He has always been willing the differentiation between His friends and His enemies, then they have claimed that Allah Almighty does not will the differentiation between His friends and His enemies, and they have attributed deficiency to Him, exalted is Allah above the saying of the Qadariyyah, a great exaltation.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Jahmiyyah (a sect that denied eternal attributes). The argument begins by getting the opponents to agree that God has always been knowing His friends and enemies – an eternal knowledge. Then the author asks: Do you say that God has always been willing the differentiation between friends and enemies? If they say yes (as they likely would), then that will is eternal and therefore uncreated. Then the author makes the key point: if God's will is uncreated, why not admit the same for His speech? Both are eternal attributes. If they refuse and say God does not eternally will this differentiation, then they are attributing deficiency to God, implying that God does not care about distinguishing believers from disbelievers. This is a serious error, and the author concludes by condemning such a view as that of the Qadariyyah (who denied predestination and eternal attributes).

Key Terms

إرادة
كلام
غير مخلوق
قدرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's attributes, including will and speech, are created in time.
Correction: This passage shows that God's will is eternal and uncreated, and by analogy His speech is likewise uncreated.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what does the opponents' admission that God has eternal knowledge imply about His will?
A) That His will is also eternal and uncreated
B) That His will is created
C) That His will is limited
D) That His knowledge is greater than His will

Key Takeaway
God's will is eternal and uncreated, and the same applies to His speech.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When you face trials or see apparent injustice in the world, do you find yourself questioning the comprehensiveness of Allah's will? How does this passage call you to repent of any subtle deficiency you have attributed to Him?
?
Have you ever felt that your own choices are outside the scope of Allah's eternal will? What specific area of your life do you need to surrender today, acknowledging that His will is uncreated and fully sovereign?

First Rejoinder: Why Kalam Allah Cannot Be Created
Al-Ash'ari's first rejoinder proving the Qur'an is uncreated via a logical disjunction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical disjunction Imam al-Ash'ari uses to argue that the Qur'an cannot be created, by eliminating both possibilities—being a body or being an attribute of a body.

Core Idea
The Qur'an cannot be created because it is neither a body nor an attribute of a body.

Imam al-Ash'ari begins his refutation of the created Qur'an by presenting a simple but powerful logical classification. He observes that everything created must be either a physical body or an attribute of a body. He then examines both possibilities and shows that Allah's speech fits neither. This argument, grounded in the nature of created things, establishes the uncreatedness of the Qur'an.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to follow the logical flow of the rejoinder.
2
Identify the disjunction
Note the two categories (body/person and attribute) and how al-Ash'ari eliminates each one.
3
Consider the additional arguments
Notice the extra points about death and creation within a person that reinforce the conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جواب : ويقال لهم : إن الشيء المخلوق إما أن يكون بدناً من الأبدان، شخصاً من الأشخاص؛ أو يكون نعتاً من نعوت الأشخاص، فلا يجوز أن يكون كلام الله شخصاً؛ لأن الأشخاص يجوز عليها الأكل والشرب والنكاح ولا يجوز ذلك على كلام الله عز وجل، ولا يجوز أن يكون كلام الله نعتاً لشخص مخلوق؛ لأن النعوت لا تبقى طرفة عين؛ لأنها لا تحتمل البقاء، وهذا يوجب أن يكون كلام الله قد فني ومضى، فلما لم يجز أن يكون شخصاً ولا نعتاً لشخص لم يجز أن يكون مخلوقاً . على أن الأشخاص يجوز أن تموت، فمن يثبت كلام الله شخصاً مخلوقاً لزمه أن يجوز الموت على كلام الله عزّ وجلّ، وذلك مما لا يجوز . وأيضا فلا يجوز أن يكون كلام الله مخلوقاً في شخص مخلوق، كما لا يجوز أن يكون نعتاً لشخص مخلوق، ولو كان مخلوقاً في شخص، وكلام الإنسان مفعولاً فيه، كما لا يمكن التفريق بين كلام الله وكلام المخلوق إذا كانا مخلوقين في شخص مخلوق، كما لا يجوز أن يكون علمه مخلوقاً في شخص مخلوق .
Response: And it is said to them: The created thing is either a body among bodies, a person among persons; or it is an attribute among the attributes of persons. So it is not permissible for the speech of Allah to be a person, because persons are subject to eating, drinking, and marriage, and that is not permissible for the speech of Allah, the Mighty and Majestic. And it is not permissible for the speech of Allah to be an attribute of a created person, because attributes do not last for a blink of an eye; because they cannot endure. This would necessitate that the speech of Allah has perished and passed away. So since it is not permissible for it to be a person nor an attribute of a person, it is not permissible for it to be created. Moreover, persons can die, so whoever affirms the speech of Allah as a created person would be required to allow death for the speech of Allah, the Mighty and Majestic, and that is not permissible. Also, it is not permissible for the speech of Allah to be created in a created person, just as it is not permissible for it to be an attribute of a created person. If it were created in a person, and the speech of a human is an effect in it, then it would be impossible to distinguish between the speech of Allah and the speech of a created being if both were created in a created person, just as it is not permissible for His knowledge to be created in a created person.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is a rejoinder (jawaab) that argues against the view that the Qur'an is created (makhluq). It presents a logical disjunction: every created thing is either a body (badan/person) or an attribute (na't) of a body. The author then examines both possibilities. First, the speech of Allah cannot be a body or person, because bodies are subject to physical actions like eating, drinking, and marriage, which are impossible for Allah's speech. Second, the speech of Allah cannot be an attribute of a created person, because attributes are accidents that do not endure; they perish instantly. Thus if the Qur'an were an attribute of a created being, it would be impermanent, but Allah's speech is eternal. Additionally, if the Qur'an were a created person, it would be subject to death, which is impossible for Allah's speech. Finally, the author argues that even if the Qur'an were created 'in' a created person (like a substrate), it would be indistinguishable from human speech, and it would also be impossible for Allah's knowledge to be created in a person. Therefore, the Qur'an cannot be created.

Key Terms
كلام الله (kalam Allah)
مخلوق (makhluq)
بدن (badan)
نعت (na't)
شخص (shakhs)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Qur'an could be created in a person (like a substrate) without being an attribute.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari argues that even if created within a person, it would be indistinguishable from human speech and would imply the same for Allah's knowledge, which is impossible.

Checkpoint
According to the first rejoinder, why cannot kalam Allah be an attribute of a created person?
A) Because attributes are eternal and uncreated.
B) Because attributes do not last even for a moment and would imply that kalam Allah perishes.
C) Because kalam Allah is a body, not an attribute.
D) Because the Qur'an is eternal but attributes are temporal.

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an cannot be created because it is neither a body nor an attribute of a body, and any attempt to place it within creation leads to absurdities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Qur'an is the eternal, uncreated speech of Allah—not a book that came into being—what does that mean for how you handle it, recite it, and listen to it? Will you approach it with the same casualness as any other text, or will you recognise that you are in the presence of the Creator's own words?
?
The argument shows that the Qur'an cannot be subject to decay, death, or change. In a world where everything else fades, how does this certainty affect your reliance on the Qur'an's guidance when you face confusion or hardship? Are you willing to bet your life on its permanence?
?
If the Qur'an were created, it would be indistinguishable from human speech. But because it is not, it stands utterly unique. When you read the Qur'an, do you truly listen as if the One who spoke it is speaking directly to you, or do you treat it as one voice among many? What would change if you actually believed this?

The Necessity of Affirming the Qur'an as Uncreated
Imam Ahmad proves the Qur'an's uncreatedness by distinguishing between creation and command/teaching.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Ahmad insisted that the Qur'an must be affirmed as uncreated, using the distinction between creation and command/teaching in the Qur'an.

Core Idea
The Qur'an is distinct from creation because Allah taught it before creating man.

In this passage, Imam Ahmad responds to a group that tries to avoid taking a stance on the Qur'an's nature. He condemns their equivocation as worse than the Jahmiyya and provides a clear proof from the Qur'an itself: the verses that distinguish between 'creation' and 'command' and between 'teaching the Qur'an' and 'creating man' show that the Qur'an is not part of creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once for overall meaning, then the translation. Note the flow of the conversation.
2
Identify the group's position
Find the phrase describing those who say 'the Qur'an is neither created nor uncreated.' Why does Imam Ahmad say they are worse than the Jahmiyya?
The Jahmiyya at least say it is created; these try to avoid the issue.
3
Study the proof from the verses
Look at the two verses Imam Ahmad quotes: Al-A'raf 54 and Ar-Rahman 1-3. Notice how he uses the order and distinction to prove that the Qur'an is not created.
In Ar-Rahman, 'taught the Qur'an' comes before 'created man.'
4
Reflect on the distinction
Imam Ahmad repeats the words 'taught' and 'created' to emphasize the difference between the Qur'an and creation. Think about why this distinction is crucial.
If the Qur'an were created, it would belong to the realm of 'creation,' but it is placed under 'command/teaching.'
5
Confirm your understanding
Summarize the argument in your own words. What makes the Qur'an uncreated according to this proof?

الباب الخامس
ما ذكر من الرواية في القرآن
قال أبو بكر : أتيت أنا والعباس بن عبد العظيم العنبري أبا عبد الله ، فسأل العباس بن عبد العظيم أبا عبد الله أحمد بن حنبل رحمه الله ورضي عنه، فقال له: قوم هاهنا قد أحدثوا يقولون : القرآن لا مخلوق ولا غير مخلوق هؤلاء أضر من الجهمية على الناس ويلكم فإن لم تقولوا: ليس بمخلوق فقولوا مخلوق .
قال أبو عبد الله : هؤلاء قوم سوء .
فقال العباس: ما تقول يا أبا عبد الله؟
فقال : الذي أعتقد وأذهب إليه، ولا أشك فيه، أن القرآن غير مخلوق، ثم قال: سبحان الله شك في هذا؟! ثم تكلم أبو عبد الله مستعظماً للشك في ذلك، فقال: سبحان الله أفي هذا شك؟ قال الله تبارك وتعالى: ﴿ أَلَا لَهُ الْخَلْقُ وَالْأَمْرُ ﴾ [الأعراف: ٥٤]. وقال: ﴿ الرَّحْمَنُ عَلَّمَ الْقُرْآنَ * خَلَقَ الْإِنْسَانَ ﴾ [الرحمن: ١-٣] ففرق بين الإنسان وبين القرآن، فقال: علم، خلق، فجعل يعيدها: عَلَّمَ، خَلَقَ، أي فرق بينهما.
قال أبو عبد الله : القرآن من علم الله ، ألا تراه يقول : عَلَّمَ الْقُرْآنَ.
والقرآن فيه أسماء الله عز وجل أي شيء يقولون؟ ألا يقولون إن أسماء الله غير مخلوقة، لم يزل الله قديراً عليماً عزيزاً حكيماً سميعاً بصيراً، لسنا نشك أن أسماء الله عز وجل غير مخلوقة، لسنا نشك أن علم الله عز وجل غير مخلوق، فالقرآن من علم الله وفيه أسماء الله ، فلا نشك أنه غير مخلوق، وهو كلام الله عز وجل، ولم يزل الله به متكلماً. ثم قال: وأي كفر من هذا؟ أو أي كفر أشر من هذا؟ إذا زعموا أن القرآن مخلوق فقد زعموا أن أسماء الله مخلوقة، وأن علم الله مخلوق، ولكن الناس يتهاونون بهذا ويقولون إنما يقولون القرآن مخلوق ويتهاونون به ويظنون أنه هين، ولا يدرون ما فيه وهو الكفر، وأنا أكره أن أبوح بهذا لكل أحد، وهم يسألون، وأنا أكره الكلام في هذا، فبلغني أنهم يدعون أني أمسك (١)
فقلت له فمن قال القرآن مخلوق ولا يقول إن أسماء الله مخلوقة ولا علمه، لم يزد على هذا، أقول: هو كافر؟
فقال : هكذا عندنا هو
ثم قال أبو عبد الله : نحن لا نحتاج أن نشك في هذا القرآن عندنا أسماء الله وهو من علم الله فمن قال لنا إنه مخلوق، فهو عندنا كافر
(١) قال الذهبي في سير أعلام النبلاء ١١/ ٤٣٢ : كان الإمام أحمد يسد الكلام في هذا الباب، ولا يجوزه، وكذلك كان يبدع من يقول: لفظي بالقرآن غير مخلوق، ويضلل من يقول : لفظي بالقرآن قديم، ويكفر من يقول : القرآن مخلوق، بل يقول : القرآن كلام الله منزل غير مخلوق، وينهى عن الخوض في مسألة اللفظ، ولا ريب أن تلفظنا بالقرآن من كسبنا، والقرآن الملفوظ المتلو كلام الله تعالى غير مخلوق، والتلاوة والتلفظ والكتابة والصوت به من أفعالنا، وهي مخلوقه، والله أعلم
Chapter Five: What has been narrated concerning the Qur'an. Abu Bakr said: I came, I and al-Abbas ibn Abd al-Azim al-Anbari, to Abu Abdullah, and al-Abbas ibn Abd al-Azim asked Abu Abdullah Ahmad ibn Hanbal (may Allah have mercy on him and be pleased with him), and said to him: There are people here who have innovated, saying: The Qur'an is neither created nor uncreated. These are more harmful to the people than the Jahmiyyah. Woe to you! If you do not say it is uncreated, then say it is created. Abu Abdullah said: These are an evil people. Al-Abbas said: What do you say, O Abu Abdullah? He said: What I believe and adhere to, and I do not doubt it, is that the Qur'an is uncreated. Then he said: Glory be to Allah! Is there doubt about this? Then Abu Abdullah spoke, deeming the doubt about that as something great, and said: Glory be to Allah! Is there doubt about this? Allah Almighty said: {Indeed, to Him belongs creation and the command} (Al-A'raf 54). And He said: {The Most Merciful taught the Qur'an, created man} (Ar-Rahman 1-3). So He made a distinction between man and the Qur'an, and said: taught, created, and he kept repeating them: taught, created, meaning He differentiated between them. Abu Abdullah said: The Qur'an is from the knowledge of Allah. Do you not see that He says: 'taught the Qur'an.' And the Qur'an contains the names of Allah Almighty. What do they say? Do they not say that the names of Allah are uncreated? Allah has always been All-Powerful, All-Knowing, All-Mighty, All-Wise, All-Hearing, All-Seeing. We do not doubt that the names of Allah Almighty are uncreated. We do not doubt that the knowledge of Allah Almighty is uncreated. So the Qur'an is from the knowledge of Allah and contains His names, so we do not doubt that it is uncreated, and it is the speech of Allah Almighty, and Allah has always been speaking with it. Then he said: What disbelief is greater than this? Or what disbelief is worse than this? If they claim that the Qur'an is created, then they have claimed that the names of Allah are created, and that the knowledge of Allah is created. But people take this lightly and say, 'They only say the Qur'an is created,' and they take it lightly and think it is trivial, and they do not know what is in it—and it is disbelief. And I dislike to divulge this to everyone, and they ask, and I dislike to speak about this. Then it reached me that they claim that I refrain. So I said to him: So the one who says the Qur'an is created and does not say that the names of Allah are created nor His knowledge, and adds nothing to this, do I say he is a disbeliever? He said: Thus with us it is. Then Abu Abdullah said: We do not need to doubt this. The Qur'an with us contains the names of Allah and it is from His knowledge. So whoever says to us that it is created, he is with us a disbeliever. (1) Al-Dhahabi said in Siyar A'lam al-Nubala' (11/432): Imam Ahmad used to silence speech about this chapter and not allow it. Likewise, he would declare someone an innovator if they said 'my utterance of the Qur'an is uncreated,' and would declare someone misguided if they said 'my utterance of the Qur'an is created,' and would declare someone a disbeliever if they said 'the Qur'an is created.' Rather, he would say: 'The Qur'an is the speech of Allah, revealed, uncreated.' And he forbade delving into the issue of articulation. There is no doubt that our articulation of the Qur'an is from our acquisition, and the Qur'an that is articulated and recited is the speech of Allah Almighty, uncreated. The recitation, articulation, writing, and the sound thereof are from our actions, and they are created. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage is a narrative from the book Al-Ibanah, quoting a conversation between a narrator (Abu Bakr) and Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal regarding the nature of the Qur'an. It serves as a proof text for the Ash'ari position that the Qur'an is uncreated. The passage begins with a question about a group that says the Qur'an is neither created nor uncreated—a position Imam Ahmad condemns as worse than the Jahmiyyah (who explicitly say it is created). He insists that one must affirm it is uncreated, or else say it is created; there is no middle ground. The proof is derived from the Qur'anic verse 'To Him belongs creation and the command' (Al-A'raf 54), where 'creation' and 'command' are distinguished, and from Surah Ar-Rahman, where Allah first teaches the Qur'an and then creates man, showing the Qur'an precedes human creation. Imam Ahmad further argues that the Qur'an contains Allah's names and is from His knowledge—both of which are uncreated. Therefore, the Qur'an itself must be uncreated. He warns that claiming the Qur'an is created necessarily implies that Allah's names and knowledge are created, which is clear disbelief. He expresses reluctance to publicly declare this for fear of people's reactions, but when asked directly, he affirms that whoever says the Qur'an is created is a disbeliever. The footnote from al-Dhahabi clarifies Imam Ahmad's nuanced position on related issues like the utterance of the Qur'an, distinguishing between the uncreated Qur'an itself and the created human acts of reciting it.

Key Terms
القرآن غير مخلوق
الخلق
الأمر
جهمية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is permissible to avoid saying whether the Qur'an is created or uncreated.
Correction: Imam Ahmad condemns this as worse than the Jahmiyya and demands affirmation of uncreatedness.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Ahmad, what is the status of those who say the Qur'an is neither created nor uncreated?
A) They are like the Jahmiyya.
B) They are more harmful than the Jahmiyya.
C) They are righteous.
D) They are excused.

Key Takeaway
Imam Ahmad's proof from the distinction between creation and command/teaching establishes that the Qur'an is not part of creation and therefore uncreated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Qur'an, do you internalize that these are the very words of Allah, not a created message? How does that certainty change the reverence you bring to each verse? Will you pause and ask Allah to make you hear His speech as it truly is before your next recitation?
?
Imam Ahmad was so convinced that he exclaimed, 'Is there doubt about this?' In your own life, where have you allowed convenience, hesitation, or worldly considerations to create doubt about a clear truth from Allah? What one clear truth from the Qur'an have you been avoiding acting upon because of such doubt?
?
The Qur'an is from Allah's command, not from creation. This means every command in the Qur'an carries the authority of the Creator. Is there a command from the Qur'an that you have treated as optional or negotiable? What will you do this week to submit to it decisively?

The Qur'an Contains Allah's Names and Knowledge
Imam Ahmad argues that the Qur'an is uncreated because it contains Allah's names and is from His knowledge, and declares takfir on those who say it is created.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that affirming the Qur'an as uncreated is necessary because it contains Allah's names and is from His knowledge, and that denying this leads to disbelief.

Core Idea
If the Qur'an is created, then Allah's names and knowledge would be created, which is impossible.

Having established the distinction between creation and command, Imam Ahmad deepens the argument by linking the Qur'an to Allah's names and knowledge. Since Allah's attributes are eternal and uncreated, the Qur'an, being His speech and containing His names, must also be uncreated. He then declares that anyone who says otherwise is a disbeliever, even if they do not explicitly admit the implication.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Pay attention to the logical flow from the Qur'an being from Allah's knowledge to containing His names.
2
Trace the argument
Identify each step: (1) The Qur'an is from Allah's knowledge. (2) The Qur'an contains Allah's names. (3) Allah's names and knowledge are uncreated. (4) Therefore, the Qur'an is uncreated.
3
Understand the implication
Imam Ahmad warns that saying the Qur'an is created necessarily implies that Allah's names and knowledge are created. Why is this a serious matter?
It would imply that Allah's attributes are created, which contradicts His eternity.
4
Examine the ruling on takfir
Imam Ahmad states that whoever says the Qur'an is created is a disbeliever, even if they do not explicitly say that Allah's names are created. Reflect on the severity of this ruling.
He emphasizes that people take this lightly, but it is clear disbelief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الخامس
ما ذكر من الرواية في القرآن
قال أبو بكر : أتيت أنا والعباس بن عبد العظيم العنبري أبا عبد الله ، فسأل العباس بن عبد العظيم أبا عبد الله أحمد بن حنبل رحمه الله ورضي عنه، فقال له: قوم هاهنا قد أحدثوا يقولون : القرآن لا مخلوق ولا غير مخلوق هؤلاء أضر من الجهمية على الناس ويلكم فإن لم تقولوا: ليس بمخلوق فقولوا مخلوق .
قال أبو عبد الله : هؤلاء قوم سوء .
فقال العباس: ما تقول يا أبا عبد الله؟
فقال : الذي أعتقد وأذهب إليه، ولا أشك فيه، أن القرآن غير مخلوق، ثم قال: سبحان الله شك في هذا؟! ثم تكلم أبو عبد الله مستعظماً للشك في ذلك، فقال: سبحان الله أفي هذا شك؟ قال الله تبارك وتعالى: ﴿ أَلَا لَهُ الْخَلْقُ وَالْأَمْرُ ﴾ [الأعراف: ٥٤]. وقال: ﴿ الرَّحْمَنُ عَلَّمَ الْقُرْآنَ * خَلَقَ الْإِنْسَانَ ﴾ [الرحمن: ١-٣] ففرق بين الإنسان وبين القرآن، فقال: علم، خلق، فجعل يعيدها: عَلَّمَ، خَلَقَ، أي فرق بينهما.
قال أبو عبد الله : القرآن من علم الله ، ألا تراه يقول : عَلَّمَ الْقُرْآنَ.
والقرآن فيه أسماء الله عز وجل أي شيء يقولون؟ ألا يقولون إن أسماء الله غير مخلوقة، لم يزل الله قديراً عليماً عزيزاً حكيماً سميعاً بصيراً، لسنا نشك أن أسماء الله عز وجل غير مخلوقة، لسنا نشك أن علم الله عز وجل غير مخلوق، فالقرآن من علم الله وفيه أسماء الله ، فلا نشك أنه غير مخلوق، وهو كلام الله عز وجل، ولم يزل الله به متكلماً. ثم قال: وأي كفر من هذا؟ أو أي كفر أشر من هذا؟ إذا زعموا أن القرآن مخلوق فقد زعموا أن أسماء الله مخلوقة، وأن علم الله مخلوق، ولكن الناس يتهاونون بهذا ويقولون إنما يقولون القرآن مخلوق ويتهاونون به ويظنون أنه هين، ولا يدرون ما فيه وهو الكفر، وأنا أكره أن أبوح بهذا لكل أحد، وهم يسألون، وأنا أكره الكلام في هذا، فبلغني أنهم يدعون أني أمسك (١)
فقلت له فمن قال القرآن مخلوق ولا يقول إن أسماء الله مخلوقة ولا علمه، لم يزد على هذا، أقول: هو كافر؟
فقال : هكذا عندنا هو
ثم قال أبو عبد الله : نحن لا نحتاج أن نشك في هذا القرآن عندنا أسماء الله وهو من علم الله فمن قال لنا إنه مخلوق، فهو عندنا كافر
(١) قال الذهبي في سير أعلام النبلاء ١١/ ٤٣٢ : كان الإمام أحمد يسد الكلام في هذا الباب، ولا يجوزه، وكذلك كان يبدع من يقول: لفظي بالقرآن غير مخلوق، ويضلل من يقول : لفظي بالقرآن قديم، ويكفر من يقول : القرآن مخلوق، بل يقول : القرآن كلام الله منزل غير مخلوق، وينهى عن الخوض في مسألة اللفظ، ولا ريب أن تلفظنا بالقرآن من كسبنا، والقرآن الملفوظ المتلو كلام الله تعالى غير مخلوق، والتلاوة والتلفظ والكتابة والصوت به من أفعالنا، وهي مخلوقه، والله أعلم
Chapter Five: What has been narrated concerning the Qur'an. Abu Bakr said: I came, I and al-Abbas ibn Abd al-Azim al-Anbari, to Abu Abdullah, and al-Abbas ibn Abd al-Azim asked Abu Abdullah Ahmad ibn Hanbal (may Allah have mercy on him and be pleased with him), and said to him: There are people here who have innovated, saying: The Qur'an is neither created nor uncreated. These are more harmful to the people than the Jahmiyyah. Woe to you! If you do not say it is uncreated, then say it is created. Abu Abdullah said: These are an evil people. Al-Abbas said: What do you say, O Abu Abdullah? He said: What I believe and adhere to, and I do not doubt it, is that the Qur'an is uncreated. Then he said: Glory be to Allah! Is there doubt about this? Then Abu Abdullah spoke, deeming the doubt about that as something great, and said: Glory be to Allah! Is there doubt about this? Allah Almighty said: {Indeed, to Him belongs creation and the command} (Al-A'raf 54). And He said: {The Most Merciful taught the Qur'an, created man} (Ar-Rahman 1-3). So He made a distinction between man and the Qur'an, and said: taught, created, and he kept repeating them: taught, created, meaning He differentiated between them. Abu Abdullah said: The Qur'an is from the knowledge of Allah. Do you not see that He says: 'taught the Qur'an.' And the Qur'an contains the names of Allah Almighty. What do they say? Do they not say that the names of Allah are uncreated? Allah has always been All-Powerful, All-Knowing, All-Mighty, All-Wise, All-Hearing, All-Seeing. We do not doubt that the names of Allah Almighty are uncreated. We do not doubt that the knowledge of Allah Almighty is uncreated. So the Qur'an is from the knowledge of Allah and contains His names, so we do not doubt that it is uncreated, and it is the speech of Allah Almighty, and Allah has always been speaking with it. Then he said: What disbelief is greater than this? Or what disbelief is worse than this? If they claim that the Qur'an is created, then they have claimed that the names of Allah are created, and that the knowledge of Allah is created. But people take this lightly and say, 'They only say the Qur'an is created,' and they take it lightly and think it is trivial, and they do not know what is in it—and it is disbelief. And I dislike to divulge this to everyone, and they ask, and I dislike to speak about this. Then it reached me that they claim that I refrain. So I said to him: So the one who says the Qur'an is created and does not say that the names of Allah are created nor His knowledge, and adds nothing to this, do I say he is a disbeliever? He said: Thus with us it is. Then Abu Abdullah said: We do not need to doubt this. The Qur'an with us contains the names of Allah and it is from His knowledge. So whoever says to us that it is created, he is with us a disbeliever. (1) Al-Dhahabi said in Siyar A'lam al-Nubala' (11/432): Imam Ahmad used to silence speech about this chapter and not allow it. Likewise, he would declare someone an innovator if they said 'my utterance of the Qur'an is uncreated,' and would declare someone misguided if they said 'my utterance of the Qur'an is created,' and would declare someone a disbeliever if they said 'the Qur'an is created.' Rather, he would say: 'The Qur'an is the speech of Allah, revealed, uncreated.' And he forbade delving into the issue of articulation. There is no doubt that our articulation of the Qur'an is from our acquisition, and the Qur'an that is articulated and recited is the speech of Allah Almighty, uncreated. The recitation, articulation, writing, and the sound thereof are from our actions, and they are created. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage is a narrative from the book Al-Ibanah, quoting a conversation between a narrator (Abu Bakr) and Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal regarding the nature of the Qur'an. It serves as a proof text for the Ash'ari position that the Qur'an is uncreated. The passage begins with a question about a group that says the Qur'an is neither created nor uncreated—a position Imam Ahmad condemns as worse than the Jahmiyyah (who explicitly say it is created). He insists that one must affirm it is uncreated, or else say it is created; there is no middle ground. The proof is derived from the Qur'anic verse 'To Him belongs creation and the command' (Al-A'raf 54), where 'creation' and 'command' are distinguished, and from Surah Ar-Rahman, where Allah first teaches the Qur'an and then creates man, showing the Qur'an precedes human creation. Imam Ahmad further argues that the Qur'an contains Allah's names and is from His knowledge—both of which are uncreated. Therefore, the Qur'an itself must be uncreated. He warns that claiming the Qur'an is created necessarily implies that Allah's names and knowledge are created, which is clear disbelief. He expresses reluctance to publicly declare this for fear of people's reactions, but when asked directly, he affirms that whoever says the Qur'an is created is a disbeliever. The footnote from al-Dhahabi clarifies Imam Ahmad's nuanced position on related issues like the utterance of the Qur'an, distinguishing between the uncreated Qur'an itself and the created human acts of reciting it.

Key Terms
علم الله
أسماء الله
كلام الله
الكفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One can say the Qur'an is created without implying that Allah's names and knowledge are created.
Correction: Imam Ahmad argues that since the Qur'an is from Allah's knowledge and contains His names, saying it is created necessarily implies that His attributes are created.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Ahmad, what is the status of a person who says the Qur'an is created but does not explicitly say that Allah's names are created?
A) He is not a disbeliever because he didn't mention the names.
B) He is still a disbeliever.
C) He is a sinner but not a disbeliever.
D) He is correct.

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an's uncreatedness is inseparable from Allah's uncreated attributes; denying it entails disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself treating the Qur'an as just another book, forgetting that it is from Allah's very knowledge and contains His names? How does this lesson change the weight of every verse you recite?
?
Imam Ahmad was reluctant to pronounce takfir publicly, yet he affirmed it privately. Do you take the beliefs of others lightly or do you carefully consider the gravity of theological errors? What would it take for you to regard someone's incorrect statement about Allah as serious as he did?
?
If you truly believe the Qur'an is the uncreated speech of Allah, how should that transform the way you approach its recitation, memorization, and application in your daily life? Commit to one concrete change starting today.
