The Qur'an is Uncreated: Argument from Allah's Names and Knowledge
Proof that the Qur'an is uncreated using the argument from Allah's names and knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument that the Qur'an is uncreated because it contains Allah's names and knowledge, and why claiming the Qur'an is created constitutes disbelief.

Core Idea
The Qur'an's uncreatedness follows logically from the uncreatedness of Allah's names and knowledge.

This passage presents a simple yet powerful proof for the uncreatedness of the Qur'an. It begins by establishing that Allah's names and attributes are uncreated, which is agreed upon by all Muslims. Since the Qur'an contains these names and is from Allah's knowledge, it must also be uncreated. The passage then addresses the severe implications of claiming otherwise, showing how such a statement necessarily leads to disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once through, then the translation. Notice the logical flow from premise to conclusion.
The passage ends with a brief dialogue affirming the ruling.
2
Identify the premises and conclusion
Find where the author states that Allah's names and knowledge are uncreated, and where he concludes that the Qur'an is therefore uncreated.
Also note the implicit premise: whatever contains uncreated things must itself be uncreated.
3
Understand the ruling on the denier
The passage states that merely saying 'the Qur'an is created' makes one a disbeliever, even without explicitly denying the uncreatedness of names and knowledge. Why?
Because the statement entails that what the Qur'an contains is created.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقرآن فيه أسماء الله عز وجل أي شيء يقولون؟ ألا يقولون إن أسماء الله غير مخلوقة، لم يزل الله قديراً عليماً عزيزاً حكيماً سميعاً بصيراً، لسنا نشك أن أسماء الله عز وجل غير مخلوقة، لسنا نشك أن علم الله عز وجل غير مخلوق، فالقرآن من علم الله وفيه أسماء الله ، فلا نشك أنه غير مخلوق، وهو كلام الله عز وجل، ولم يزل الله به متكلماً. ثم قال: وأي كفر من هذا؟ أو أي كفر أشرُّ من هذا؟ إذا زعموا أن القرآن مخلوق فقد زعموا أن أسماء الله مخلوقة، وأن علم الله مخلوق، ولكن الناس يتهاونون بهذا ويقولون إنما يقولون القرآن مخلوق ويتهاونون به ويظنون أنه هين، ولا يدرون ما فيه وهو الكفر، وأنا أكره أن أبوح بهذا لكل أحد، وهم يسألون، وأنا أكره الكلام في هذا، فبلغني أنهم يدعون أني أمسك فقلت له فمن قال القرآن مخلوق ولا يقول إن أسماء الله مخلوقة ولا علمه، لم يزد على هذا، أقول: هو كافر؟ فقال : هكذا عندنا هو ثم قال أبو عبد الله : نحن لا نحتاج أن نشك في هذا القرآن عندنا أسماء الله وهو من علم الله فمن قال لنا إنه مخلوق، فهو عندنا كافر سبحان الله أما فجعلت أردد عليه فقال لي العباس – وهو يسمع - يكفيك دون هذا؟ فقال أبو عبد الله : بلى
And the Qur'an contains the names of Allah, may He be mighty and majestic. What do they say? Do they not say that the names of Allah are uncreated? Allah has never ceased being Powerful, Knowing, Mighty, Wise, Hearing, Seeing. We do not doubt that the names of Allah, may He be mighty and majestic, are uncreated. We do not doubt that the knowledge of Allah, may He be mighty and majestic, is uncreated. So the Qur'an is from the knowledge of Allah and contains His names, so we do not doubt that it is uncreated, and it is the speech of Allah, may He be mighty and majestic, and Allah has never ceased speaking with it. Then he said: And what disbelief is greater than this? Or what disbelief is worse than this? When they claim that the Qur'an is created, they claim that the names of Allah are created, and that the knowledge of Allah is created. But people treat this lightly and say only 'the Qur'an is created' and they treat it lightly and think it is easy, and they do not know what is in it, and it is disbelief. I dislike revealing this to everyone, and they ask, and I dislike speaking about this. Then it reached me that they claim that I refrain. So I said to him: As for the one who says the Qur'an is created and does not say that the names of Allah are created nor His knowledge, and says no more than this, do I say he is a disbeliever? He said: This is our position, he is. Then Abu Abdullah said: We do not need to doubt this. The Qur'an contains the names of Allah and it is from the knowledge of Allah. So whoever says to us that it is created, he is in our view a disbeliever. Glory be to Allah. Then I began to repeat (the question) to him, and Al-Abbas said to me – while he was listening – 'Is this not enough for you?' So Abu Abdullah said: Yes.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage presents a proof for the uncreatedness of the Qur'an based on its content. It begins by noting that the Qur'an contains Allah's names. The speaker then asserts that all Muslims agree Allah's names are uncreated and that Allah has always had His attributes (power, knowledge, etc.). Since the Qur'an contains these uncreated names and is from Allah's knowledge (which is also uncreated), it follows logically that the Qur'an itself is uncreated. Moreover, the Qur'an is Allah's speech, and Allah has never ceased speaking. The passage then condemns those who claim the Qur'an is created: such a claim necessarily implies that Allah's names and knowledge are created, which is blatant disbelief. The speaker expresses concern that people trivialize this statement, not realizing its implications. When asked whether someone who only says 'the Qur'an is created' without explicitly saying names and knowledge are created is still a disbeliever, the answer is affirmative: such a person is still a disbeliever because the Qur'an itself, in their view, would be created, and that entails the createdness of what it contains. The passage concludes with a brief exchange where the speaker's interlocutor affirms that this ruling is sufficient.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that only if one explicitly declares Allah's names or knowledge as created is it kufr.
Correction: The passage clarifies that merely saying 'the Qur'an is created' is sufficient for kufr because the Qur'an contains Allah's names and knowledge, so the statement necessarily implies their createdness.

Checkpoint

B) He is not a disbeliever
C) He is a sinner but not a disbeliever
D) It depends on his intention

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an is uncreated because it contains Allah's uncreated names and knowledge; claiming it is created is clear disbelief because it entails the createdness of Allah's names and knowledge.

?

?

Sulayman ibn Harb: The Quran is Uncreated Like Allah's Sight
Sulayman ibn Harb proves the Quran is uncreated by analogy with Allah's sight.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sulayman ibn Harb used Surah Aal 'Imran 77 to prove that the Quran is uncreated, drawing an analogy between Allah's speech and His sight.

Core Idea
Allah's speech is uncreated, just as His sight is uncreated—both are His eternal attributes.

This lesson presents a concise proof from the early scholar Sulayman ibn Harb for the uncreatedness of the Quran. By citing a verse that pairs Allah's speech and sight, he argues that both share the same divine nature. Understanding this analogy helps clarify the traditional position that divine attributes are eternal and not created.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without overthinking. Then read the literal translation. Let the argument settle in your mind.
Notice how short and direct the proof is.
2
Identify the scriptural basis
Sulayman cites Quran 3:77. Look at the verse: it mentions Allah's speech and His sight together. Why is that significant?
The verse is about punishment, but Sulayman uses it to highlight the attributes.
3
Grasp the analogy
Sulayman argues that since Allah's speech and sight are mentioned together, they share the same nature—both are uncreated attributes of Allah.
This is a simple but powerful argument from linguistic pairing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال سليمان بن حرب القرآن غير مخلوق، وأخذته من كتاب الله تعالى قال الله عز وجل: (وَلَا يُكَلِّمُهُمُ اللَّهُ وَلَا يَنظُرُ إِلَيْهِمْ ) [آل عمران: 77] ، وكلام الله ونظره واحد، يعني غير مخلوق
And Sulayman ibn Harb said: The Quran is uncreated, and I took that from the Book of Allah, the Exalted. Allah Almighty said: 'And Allah will not speak to them nor look at them' [Aal 'Imran: 77]. And the speech of Allah and His sight are one, meaning uncreated.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is a proof from Sulayman ibn Harb that the Quran is uncreated. He cites Quran 3:77, which mentions both Allah's speech (yukallimuhum) and His sight (yanzuru ilayhim). He argues that since both are mentioned together, they share the same nature — both are attributes of Allah, and what is attributed to Allah is uncreated. Therefore, the Quran (Allah's speech) is uncreated, just as His sight is uncreated. This is a simple theological argument from a salafi perspective.

Key Terms
القرآن غير مخلوق
كلام الله
نظر الله
آل عمران 77

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What verse did Sulayman ibn Harb use to prove the Quran is uncreated?
A) Surah Al-Ikhlas
B) Ayat al-Kursi
C) 'Allah will not speak to them nor look at them'
D) 'Say: He is Allah, the One'

Key Takeaway
Sulayman ibn Harb proves the Quran is uncreated by showing that Allah's speech and sight are mentioned together in the same verse, implying they share the same uncreated nature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that every word you recite from the Quran is the uncreated speech of Allah, how would your concentration and reverence change starting from your next recitation? What practical step will you take today to act on this belief?
?
Consider: The same Allah who will not speak to some people on the Day of Judgment (as in the verse) has graced you with His speech in the Quran. How does this motivate you to respond to His speech with obedience and gratitude? What will you change in your attitude toward the Quran right now?
?
Sulayman ibn Harb argues from a single verse that the Quran is uncreated. Do you treat the Quran as merely a historical text or as the eternal word of the Creator addressing you personally? What distractions in your life contradict this belief, and how will you remove them this week?

Proof from Hadith that Quran is Uncreated Speech of Allah
Ashari proves from a hadith and verses that the Quran is uncreated speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Ashari uses a hadith and Quranic verses to establish that the Quran is the uncreated speech of Allah.

Core Idea
The Quran's superiority over all speech proves it is the speech of the Creator, not a creation.

This lesson presents a key proof from the sunna and the Quran that the Quran is the uncreated speech of Allah. Imam Ashari cites a hadith about the superiority of Allah's speech and then reinforces it with Quranic evidence. You will see how the argument unfolds logically.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the overall argument. Notice the structure: a claim, a hadith, and then Quranic citations.
2
Analyze the hadith and its implication
Focus on the Prophet's statement: 'The superiority of Allah's speech over other speech is like the superiority of Allah over His creation.' Ask yourself: what does this comparison imply about the nature of the Quran?
The comparison suggests that just as Allah is not created, His speech is not created.
3
Understand the Quranic support
Examine the verses Ashari quotes: 'Until they hear the speech of Allah' (9:6) and 'Allah spoke to Moses directly' (4:164). How do these verses confirm that the Quran is Allah's speech?
These verses directly attribute speech to Allah, reinforcing that it is His attribute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال سليمان بن حرب القرآن غير مخلوق، وأخذته من كتاب الله تعالى قال الله عز وجل: (وَلَا يُكَلِّمُهُمُ اللَّهُ وَلَا يَنظُرُ إِلَيْهِمْ) [آل عمران: 77] ، وكلام الله ونظره واحد، يعني غير مخلوق. وذكر الحسين بن عبد الأول قال حدثنا محمد بن الحسن بن أبي يزيد الهمداني عن عمرو بن قيس الملائي، عن عطية، عن أبي سعيد الخدري رضي الله عنه قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «فَضْلُ كَلامِ اللهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ على سائر الكَلامِ كَفَضْلِ الله عَلى خَلْقه». فهذا يثبت أن القرآن كلام الله عز وجل، وما كان كلاماً الله لم يكن خلقاً الله، وقد بيّن الله أن القرآن كلامه بقوله عز وجل: (حَتَّى يَسْمَعَ كَلمَ الله) [التوبة: 6] ودل على ذلك في مواضع من كتابه العزيز، وقد قال الله تعالى مخبراً: أن الله كلم موسى تكليماً.
And Sulayman ibn Harb said: The Quran is uncreated, and I took it from the Book of Allah Almighty – Allah Almighty said: 'And Allah will not speak to them nor look at them' [Al 'Imran: 77], and Allah's speech and His look are one, meaning uncreated. And al-Husayn ibn 'Abd al-Awwal mentioned, he said: Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Abi Yazid al-Hamdani narrated to us from 'Amr ibn Qays al-Mula'i, from 'Atiyya, from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, may Allah be pleased with him, he said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'The superiority of the speech of Allah Almighty over other speech is like the superiority of Allah over His creation.' So this proves that the Quran is the speech of Allah Almighty, and whatever is the speech of Allah is not a creation of Allah. And Allah has made clear that the Quran is His speech by His saying Almighty: 'Until they hear the speech of Allah' [Al-Tawba: 6], and He indicated that in places of His noble Book. And Allah Almighty said, informing: that Allah spoke to Moses directly (takliman).
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage presents a proof that the Quran is the uncreated speech of Allah. It begins with a statement from Sulayman ibn Harb who affirms the Quran is uncreated, citing the verse 'Allah will not speak to them nor look at them' – he argues that Allah's speech and His sight are both attributes and are one in being uncreated, meaning not created. Then he reports a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri where the Prophet says the superiority of Allah's speech over other speech is like the superiority of Allah over His creation. The author (Ashari) then provides commentary: this hadith establishes that the Quran is Allah's speech, and whatever is Allah's speech cannot be a creation of Allah. He supports this with Quranic evidence: the verse 'until they hear the speech of Allah' (9:6) and the statement that 'Allah spoke to Moses directly' (4:164). These proofs collectively demonstrate that the Quran is the eternal, uncreated attribute of speech.

Key Terms
غير مخلوق
كلام الله
فضل كلام الله
تكليماً

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the hadith comparing the superiority of Allah's speech to Allah's superiority over creation implies that the Quran is created, because it is being compared to creation.
Correction: Imam Ashari argues the opposite: the comparison shows that just as Allah is not created, His speech is not created. The superiority of Allah's speech over other speech is like the superiority of the Creator over His creation, indicating that Allah's speech shares in the uncreated nature of Allah Himself.

Checkpoint
What proof does Sulayman ibn Harb use from the verse 'Allah will not speak to them nor look at them' for the uncreatedness of the Quran?
A) That speech and sight are both created
B) That speech and sight are one and uncreated
C) That only speech is uncreated
D) That the verse is about the Hereafter

Key Takeaway
The Quran is uncreated because it is the speech of Allah, and both the hadith and the Quran affirm that Allah's speech is an uncreated attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Quran is the uncreated speech of Allah, do you approach it as the very words of the Creator who is infinitely above His creation, or do you treat it as just another book? What would change in your recitation and reflection if you truly internalized this?
?
The hadith says Allah's speech is superior to all speech like Allah is superior to creation. When you hear the Quran, do you sense that infinite superiority, or does it feel ordinary? What barriers in your heart or mind keep you from experiencing that awe?
?
The passage proves the Quran is not created. How does this affect the authority you give to its commands? Are there specific commands in the Quran you have been neglecting or rationalizing away, forgetting they come from the uncreated Lord?

Hadiths on Allah Speaking and the Quran's Superiority
Ashari supplies three hadiths proving Allah speaks and Quran is preeminent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how three prophetic hadiths and narrations affirm that Allah speaks directly and that the Quran is His exalted, uncreated speech.

Core Idea
Allah's speech is proven by direct communication and its unmatched superiority.

Imam al-Ashari now brings forward prophetic hadiths and early narrations that ground the doctrine of Allah's speech in transmitted evidence. These narrations not only confirm that Allah is Mutakallim but also highlight the extraordinary status of His speech, the Quran. This lesson presents three such proofs, showing how they reinforce the Ash'ari position that the Quran is the uncreated attribute of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the three narrations carefully
Read each hadith slowly, paying attention to the chain of transmission and the key statement. Notice that each narration emphasizes a different aspect of Allah's speech.
The first hadith is about direct speech, the second about superiority, the third about learning/teaching.
2
Identify the doctrinal point of each narration
For each narration, ask: what specific attribute or characteristic of Allah's speech does it prove? The first proves direct speech, the second proves superiority, the third implies the esteemed status of the Quran.
These three points together reinforce the uncreatedness and excellence of the Quran.
3
Connect the narrations to the Ash'ari position
Understand how these hadiths support the conclusion that Allah is Mutakallim with an eternal attribute of speech, and that the Quran is not created but is His very speech.
This passage is part of a larger argument against those who deny the attribute of speech.

Source Text

وروى وكيع عن الأعمش، عن خيثمة، عن عدي بن حاتم، قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: (مَا مِنكُمْ مِنْ أَحَدٍ إِلا سَيُكَلِّمُهُ رَبُّهُ لَيْسَ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَهُ تُرْجُمَانٌ). ومما يدل أن الله عز وجل متكلم، وأن له كلاماً، ما رواه عفان، قال: حدثنا حماد بن سلمة: عن الأشعث الحداني عن شهر بن حوشب، قال: فَضلُ كلام الله عَزَّ وَجَلَّ على سَائِرِ الكلام كَفَضْلِ الله عَلَى خَلْقِهِ. وروى يعلى بن المنهال السعدي قال: حدثنا إسحاق بن سليمان الرازي، قال: حدثنا الجراح بن الضحاك الكندي، عن علقمة بن مرثد، عن أبي عبد الرحمن السلمي عن عثمان بن عفان رضي الله عنه قال، قال رسول الله: أَفْضَلُكُم مَنْ تَعَلَّمَ القُرآنَ وعَلَّمَهُ.
And Wakī' narrated from al-A'mash, from Khaythama, from 'Adi ibn Hatim, he said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'There is not one of you who will not have his Lord speak to him with no interpreter between him and Him.' And Ya'la ibn al-Minhāl al-Sa'di narrated, he said: Ishaq ibn Sulayman al-Razi narrated to us, he said: al-Jarrah ibn al-Dahhak al-Kindi narrated to us from 'Alqama ibn Marthad, from Abu 'Abd al-Rahman al-Sulami from 'Uthman ibn 'Affan, may Allah be pleased with him, he said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'The best of you is the one who learns the Quran and teaches it.'
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage provides three additional narrations that support the doctrine that Allah speaks and that His speech (the Quran) is supremely exalted. The first hadith (from 'Adi ibn Hatim) states that every person will have Allah speak to them directly on the Day of Judgment with no interpreter – proving that Allah is Mutakallim (speaking). The second narration (from Shahr ibn Hawshab) reiterates the superiority of Allah's speech over all other speech, emphasizing its exalted and uncreated nature. The third hadith (from 'Uthman ibn 'Affan) declares that the best of people are those who learn and teach the Quran, implying the immense virtue and esteem of Allah's speech. Together, these narrations reinforce the Ash'ari position that the Quran is the uncreated, eternal speech of Allah, an attribute of His essence.

The Superiority Hadith and the Uncreated Quran
Al-Ash'ari presents a hadith and commentary proving the Quran is Allah's uncreated speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Ash'ari uses a hadith about the superiority of Allah's speech to prove that the Quran is uncreated.

Core Idea
The superiority hadith shows the Quran is Allah's speech, which cannot be created.

Al-Ash'ari begins with a prophetic hadith that compares the superiority of Allah's speech over other speech to Allah's superiority over creation. From this analogy, he extracts a decisive theological conclusion: the Quran, being Allah's speech, is not created. He then reinforces this with Quranic verses. Let's examine his argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its placement
First, carefully read the hadith as transmitted by Abu Sa'id al-Khudri. Notice that it states a general principle: the superiority of Allah's speech over all other speech is like Allah's superiority over His creation.
This hadith is the foundation of the argument.
2
Follow the logical deduction
Al-Ash'ari then draws a conclusion: since the Quran is identified as Allah's speech, and the hadith implies that Allah's speech is not like created things (because of the degree of superiority), the Quran cannot be created.
The analogy links superiority to uncreatedness.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
Al-Ash'ari cites the verse 'until they hear the speech of Allah' (9:6) and the general principle that Allah spoke to Moses directly. These confirm that the Quran is Allah's speech.
These verses provide scriptural backing.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this argument matters in Islamic theology. It establishes the Quran as an eternal attribute of Allah, not a created entity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أبي يزيد الهمداني عن عمرو بن قيس الملائي، عن عطية، عن أبي سعيد الخدري رضي الله عنه قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : « فَضْلُ كَلامِ اللهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ على سائر الكَلامِ كَفَضْلِ الله عَلى خَلْقه (۱). فهذا يثبت أن القرآن كلام الله عز وجل، وما كان كلاماً الله عـز وجــل لـم يكن خلقاً الله، وقد بيّن الله أن القرآن كلامه بقوله عز وجل: (حَتَّى يَسْمَعَ كَلمَ الله ﴾ [التوبة : ٦] ودل على ذلك في مواضع من كتابه العزيز، وقد قال الله تعالى مخبراً : أن الله كلم موسى تكليماً .
From Abu Yazid al-Hamdani from Amr bin Qais al-Mala'i from Atiyya from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The superiority of the speech of Allah Almighty over all other speech is like the superiority of Allah over His creation.' This establishes that the Quran is the speech of Allah Almighty, and what is the speech of Allah Almighty cannot be creation of Allah. And Allah has made clear that the Quran is His speech by His statement: 'Until they hear the speech of Allah' [Surah at-Tawbah: 6] and He indicated that in several places of His noble Book. And Allah Almighty said, informing: that Allah spoke to Moses directly.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is a proof combining a hadith with authorial reasoning. Al-Ash'ari first cites a hadith that states the superiority of Allah's speech over all other speech is like Allah's superiority over His creation. The author then draws a logical conclusion: since the Quran is identified as Allah's speech, and Allah's speech is not creation (because it is attributed to Him as a quality), the Quran cannot be created. He reinforces this with Quranic evidence: the verse 'until they hear the speech of Allah' (Surah at-Tawbah: 6) explicitly calls the Quran Allah's speech. He also references the general principle that Allah spoke to Moses directly (Surah an-Nisa: 164), which implies speech is an eternal attribute. Each point follows sequentially: first the hadith, then the deduction, then scriptural confirmation.

Key Terms
كلام الله (speech of Allah)
فضل (superiority)
غير مخلوق (uncreated)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the hadith only praises the Quran's excellence without addressing its createdness.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari shows that the analogy directly implies uncreatedness: if Allah's speech is as superior over other speech as Allah is over creation, then it cannot be part of creation.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Ash'ari, what does the hadith about the superiority of Allah's speech prove?
A) That the Quran is the best of all books
B) That the Quran is the speech of Allah and therefore not created
C) That Allah's speech is similar to human speech
D) That the Quran was revealed gradually

Key Takeaway
The hadith about the superiority of Allah's speech proves that the Quran is uncreated, because the analogy shows that Allah's speech is not like created things.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the superiority of Allah’s speech over all other speech is like His superiority over His creation, how much weight do you give to the words of the Quran compared to the words of people or even your own inner thoughts? When was the last time you felt that awe while reciting or listening to the Quran?
?
The hadith tells us that the Quran is entirely different from creation. Yet, do you sometimes treat it like a book among books—reading it casually, rushing through it, or neglecting its commands? What would change if you truly believed every verse is Allah's eternal, uncreated speech addressing you directly?
?
Allah’s speech is supreme and uncreated. Are there created words (songs, social media, gossip) that you listen to more often than the Quran? Will you make a concrete plan today to tip the scales in favor of hearing Allah's speech more than any other?

Allah Speaks Without an Interpreter
Al-Ash'ari cites a hadith affirming direct divine speech to every individual.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a hadith from the Prophet confirms that Allah's attribute of speech is direct and unmediated, affirming the reality of divine speech.

Core Idea
Allah’s speech is so real that He will address each person directly.

Al-Ash'ari uses a prophetic hadith to defend the doctrine that Allah truly speaks. The hadith vividly depicts the Day of Judgment where every individual is spoken to by Allah without any intermediary. This passage is a key proof for the attribute of divine speech as eternal and essential.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its translation
Read the Arabic text and the literal translation. Notice the chain of narrators and the key phrase 'without an interpreter.'
2
Understand the theological claim
The hadith is presented to prove that Allah is a speaker (mutakallim). The absence of an intermediary shows that Allah's speech is direct and real.
3
Reflect on the significance
Why does Al-Ash'ari emphasize 'no interpreter'? This refutes those who reduce Allah's speech to a created effect or indirect communication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١٢٢ - وروى وكيع عن الأعمش، عن خيثمة، عن عدي بن حاتم، قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: (مَا مِنكُمْ مِنْ أَحَدٍ إِلا سَيُكَلِّمُهُ رَبُّهُ لَيْسَ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَهُ تُرْجُمَانٌ (۲).

Commentary
This passage is a solitary hadith citation serving as evidence for Allah's attribute of speech. Al-Ash'ari presents the hadith as proof that Allah is truly a speaker (mutakallim). The hadith states that on the Day of Judgment (or in the afterlife) every person will be directly addressed by Allah without any intermediary. The absence of an interpreter means the speech is direct and real, not a created voice or representation. This refutes those who deny that speech is an eternal attribute of Allah, claiming it is only a created effect. By emphasizing no interpreter, the hadith upholds that Allah's speech is immediate and unmediated, confirming it is an essential attribute.

Key Takeaway

Another Narration on the Superiority of Allah's Speech
Al-Ash'ari repeats the hadith of superiority with a different chain to reinforce the proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a different chain of transmission strengthens the proof that Allah is a speaker and His speech is uncreated.

Core Idea
Multiple chains strengthen the proof that Allah's speech is divine and uncreated.

Al-Ash'ari has already presented one hadith on this topic. Now he offers the same meaning through a different chain of narrators. This is a standard method in hadith scholarship: when the same meaning is transmitted by multiple reliable chains, the proof becomes stronger. In this lesson, you will see how this second narration reinforces the doctrine that Allah is a speaker and His speech is superior to all created speech.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text aloud or silently. Notice the phrase 'فضل كلام الله على سائر الكلام' (the superiority of Allah's speech over all speech).
The chain begins with 'Affan.'
2
Compare with the previous hadith
Recall the first narration from lesson 1. This second narration says exactly the same thing but with different narrators. Why does Al-Ash'ari include it?
3
Reflect on the implication
The comparison to Allah's superiority over creation implies that Allah's speech is eternal and uncreated, because creation is inferior to the Creator.
This is a key doctrinal point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١٢٣ - ومما يدل أن الله عز وجل متكلم، وأن له كلاماً، ما رواه عفان، قال: حدثنا حماد بن سلمة : عن الأشعث الحداني عن شهر بن حوشب، قال: فَضلُ كلام الله عَزَّ وَجَلَّ على سَائِرِ الكلام كَفَضْلِ الله عَلَى خَلْقِهِ (۳).
123 – And from what indicates that Allah Almighty is a speaker, and that He has speech, is what 'Affan narrated: Hammad bin Salama narrated to us from al-Ash'ath al-Huddani from Shahr bin Hawshab who said: The superiority of the speech of Allah Almighty over all other speech is like the superiority of Allah over His creation.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is another transmitted proof for the same doctrine. Al-Ash'ari introduces it with 'from what indicates that Allah is a speaker and has speech,' showing its purpose. The hadith is identical in meaning to the one in lesson 1 but with a different chain of narrators. The repetition across multiple chains strengthens the reliability of the report and the doctrine it supports. By stating that Allah's speech is superior to all other speech as Allah is superior to creation, the hadith implies that Allah's speech is inherently divine, not a created thing, because creation is inferior to the Creator, just as created speech is inferior to Allah's speech.

Key Terms
متكلم (speaker)
كلام (speech)
فضل (superiority)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A single narration is enough to prove a doctrine.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari provides multiple chains to strengthen the proof and preempt criticism of weakness in transmission.

Key Takeaway
Through multiple chains of transmission, Al-Ash'ari solidifies the proof that Allah's speech is superior and uncreated.

The Virtue and Superiority of the Quran
Al-Ash'ari presents two hadiths and an explanatory note

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Quran is superior to all other speech, based on two hadiths and the theological principle that it is from Allah.

Core Idea
The Quran's unmatched excellence stems from its divine origin.

Al-Ash'ari presents two well-known hadiths to establish the Quran's unique status. The first praises those who learn and teach it; the second declares its superiority over all speech, comparing it to Allah's superiority over creation. The author then adds a crucial note that grounds this superiority in the Quran's source: it is from Allah Himself.

Guided Path
1
Read the two hadiths
Read the Arabic text and translation carefully. Notice that the first hadith is about the best among people, and the second about the Quran's superiority.
The hadiths are transmitted together in a single chain.
2
Reflect on the author's note
After the second hadith, Al-Ash'ari adds: 'And that is because it is from Him.' Think about why he includes this explanation.
This connects the Quran's status directly to its divine origin.
3
Understand the theological implication
The phrase 'it is from Him' implies that the Quran, as Allah's speech, is not created. This was a key point in early Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١٢٤ - وروى يعلى بن المنهال السعدي قال: حدثنا إسحاق بن سليمان الرازي، قال: حدثنا الجراح بن الضحاك الكندي، عن علقمة بن مرثد، عن أبي عبد الرحمن السلمي عن عثمان بن عفان رضي الله عنه قال، قال رسول الله : « أَفْضَلُكُم مَنْ تَعَلَّمَ القُرآنَ وعَلَّمَهُ (٤) ، وقال : « إِنَّ فَضْلَ القُرْآنِ عَلَى سَائِرِ الكَلامِ كَفَضْلِ الله عَلى خَلْقِهِ () ، وذلك أنه منه.
124 – And Ya'la bin al-Minhal as-Sa'di narrated: Ishaq bin Sulayman ar-Razi narrated to us: al-Jarrah bin ad-Dahhak al-Kindi narrated to us from 'Alqama bin Mirthad from Abu 'Abd ar-Rahman as-Sulami from 'Uthman bin 'Affan (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The best among you is the one who learns the Quran and teaches it.' And he said: 'Indeed, the superiority of the Quran over all other speech is like the superiority of Allah over His creation.' And that is because it is from Him.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage contains two hadiths transmitted together. The first praises learning and teaching the Quran. The second repeats the superiority simile. The author adds a brief explanatory note: 'And that is because it is from Him.' This indicates the reason for the Quran's unparalleled excellence: it originates from Allah Himself. Since Allah is not created, His attribute of speech (the Quran) is likewise not created. The phrase 'it is from Him' directly ties the Quran's nature to its divine source, implying that its status is derived from Allah's own status, thus it cannot be created.

Key Terms
فضل القرآن
تعلم القرآن
منه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the second hadith is merely a repetition of the first or a general praise, without theological depth.
Correction: The author's note 'because it is from Him' adds a crucial theological link: the Quran's superiority is due to its divine origin, which implies it is not created.

Checkpoint

A) Because it contains beautiful language
B) Because it is from Allah Himself
C) Because it was revealed in Arabic
D) Because it is the most memorized book

Key Takeaway
The Quran's superiority over all speech is rooted in its being directly from Allah, affirming its uncreated status.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

If you're honest, does your effort match your belief in its superiority? What specific change will you make today to join the ranks of the best?
?
If the Quran's superiority over all speech is like Allah's superiority over His creation, how do you actually treat it? Do you listen to it with the same attention you give to your favorite podcast or conversation? What would it look like if you truly honored it as the speech of your Creator?
?
The author says the Quran's excellence is because it is from Allah. Do you approach the Quran as a divine message meant to transform you, or as a text to be recited without reflection? If you truly believed every word is from Him, what would you do differently in your relationship with it? Will you begin that today?

The Inexhaustibility of Allah's Words: Quranic Proof from Surah Luqman
Al-Ash'ari cites Surah Luqman 31:27 on the inexhaustibility of Allah's words.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Surah Luqman 31:27 demonstrates that Allah's words are infinite, supporting the doctrine that the Quran is uncreated.

Core Idea
Allah's words are limitless, proving they are an eternal attribute, not a created thing.

In this passage, Imam al-Ash'ari presents a powerful Quranic verse to argue that Allah's speech is not created. By citing the infinite nature of Allah's words, he refutes those who claim the Quran is a finite creation. This lesson unpacks the verse and its theological implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and its narration chain
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the chain of transmission (sanad) that Al-Ash'ari provides to authenticate the verse.
The narration chain adds reliability to the citation.
2
Reflect on the imagery of trees and seas
The verse uses vivid imagery: all trees as pens and the sea plus seven more seas as ink. Imagine the vastness this describes to grasp the infinite nature of Allah's words.
The number seven is symbolic of completeness in Arabic rhetoric.
3
Connect to the doctrine of the uncreated Quran
Since Allah's words cannot be exhausted, they are not finite or created. This verse directly challenges the view that the Quran, being Allah's speech, is a created entity.
Created things are limited; the infinite implies eternity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١٢٥ - وذكر سنيد بن داود، قال حدثنا أبو سفيان عن معمر عن قتادة قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَلَوْ أَنَّمَا فِي الْأَرْضِ مِن شَجَرَةٍ أَعْلَمُ وَالْبَحْرُ يَمُدُّهُ مِنْ بَعْدِهِ سَبْعَةُ أَبْحُرٍ مَّا نَفِدَتْ كَلِمَتُ اللهِ ) الآية [لقمان: ۲۷].
125 – And Sunayd bin Dawud mentioned: Abu Sufyan narrated to us from Ma'mar from Qatada regarding His statement: 'And if whatever trees upon the earth were pens and the sea [were ink], replenished thereafter by seven more seas, the words of Allah would not be exhausted' [Surah Luqman: 27].
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is a proof from the Quran itself. Al-Ash'ari presents the verse from Surah Luqman (31:27) which declares that all the trees on earth turned into pens and the entire sea plus seven more seas into ink would not be enough to write the words of Allah. This demonstrates that Allah's words are infinite, which is a property of an eternal attribute, not of a created finite thing. Created things are limited, whereas the attribute of speech belonging to Allah is boundless. The verse implicitly supports the doctrine that the Quran (as part of Allah's speech) is uncreated because it shares in this infinite quality.

Key Terms
كلمات الله
لا تنفد
سبعة أبحر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some argue this verse refers only to the content of Allah's knowledge, not to the Quran.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari uses it to highlight the uncreated nature of divine speech, which includes the Quran as a subset of Allah's words.

Checkpoint

A) By saying the Quran is eternal
B) By showing that Allah's words are infinite and cannot be exhausted
C) By stating the Quran was sent down
D) By comparing it to trees

Key Takeaway
The words of Allah are infinite, showing that they are an eternal attribute and not a created thing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The verse says even if all trees become pens and all seas become ink, the words of Allah would not run out. Yet when you memorize Quran, you may feel you have 'learned' it. What does this say about your attitude? Will you seek to be a student of His words for life, never claiming mastery?

Drawing Near to Allah Through His Speech
Al-Ash'ari cites a narration emphasizing that Allah's speech is the most beloved means of drawing near to Him.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Khabbab's statement implies the Quran is uncreated and most beloved to Allah.

Core Idea
Allah's speech is the most beloved act of worship.

Imam al-Ash'ari presents a narration from the Companion Khabbab to support the doctrine of the uncreated Quran. This hadith emphasizes that nothing draws a person closer to Allah more than His speech, indicating its supreme and uncreated nature.

Guided Path
1
Read the narration carefully
Read the Arabic narration and its translation. Notice the chain of transmission and the direct advice from Khabbab to his neighbor.
The chain shows the narration is well-attested.
2
Identify the key teaching
Khabbab says you will never draw near to Allah with anything more beloved to Him than His speech. Identify what this means for the status of the Quran.
3
Reflect on the theological implication
Consider why this points to the Quran being uncreated. If the Quran were created, it would not be the most beloved thing; only something from Allah's essence holds such rank.
This is the core argument Al-Ash'ari uses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١٢٦ - وذكر هارون بن معروف قال حدثنا جرير عن منصور، عن هلال بن يساف، عن فروة بن نوفل قال: كنت جاراً لخباب بن الأرت، فقال لي : يا هذا تقرب إلى الله عز وجل بما استطعت فإنك لن تتقرب إلى الله بشيء أحب إليه من كلامه (۳).

Commentary

The statement indicates that the most beloved act of worship to Allah is engagement with His speech, i.e., the Quran. The implication for the doctrine of the uncreated Quran is that if the Quran were a created thing, it would not be the most beloved means of drawing near to Allah, because created things are inferior and cannot be the ultimate means of closeness. The fact that it is singled out as the best shows it shares in Allah's uncreated nature. The report thus supports the high status of the Quran as divine speech.

Key Takeaway

Ibn Abbas on the Quran's Perfection as Uncreated
Al-Ash'ari reports Ibn Abbas's interpretation of a Quranic phrase to mean the Quran is uncreated.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Abbas interpreted the Quranic description 'without deviation' as evidence for the Quran being uncreated.

Core Idea
Ibn Abbas saw the Quran's perfection as proof it is uncreated.

Al-Ash'ari reports a key interpretation from Ibn Abbas, a leading Companion, linking the Quran's description as 'without deviation' to its uncreated nature. This short report shows how early scholars used Quranic verses to defend the Quran's eternal attribute. Let's examine the passage.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the chain of narration. The passage is a single report.
The Arabic has an OCR corruption: 'قرة أنا' should be 'قرآنا'.
2
Understand the interpretation
Ibn Abbas interprets 'without deviation' as 'uncreated'. Reflect on why this interpretation matters.
3
Connect to broader doctrine
This interpretation connects the Quran's perfection to its being from Allah's eternal speech, not a created entity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١٢٧ - وروي عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما في قوله عز وجل: قرة أنا عَرَبِيًّا غَيْرَ ذِي عِوَج ﴾ [الزمر: ۲۸] قال: غير مخلوق(۳).
127 – And it is narrated from Ibn 'Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both) regarding His statement: 'An Arabic Quran without any deviance' [Surah az-Zumar: 28] that he said: 'Uncreated.'
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is a tafsir (exegesis) report. Al-Ash'ari transmits from Ibn Abbas, a renowned tafsir authority, that the phrase 'without any deviance' (غَيْرَ ذِي عِوَج) is explained as 'uncreated' (غير مخلوق). This is a direct scriptural argument linking the Quran's description of itself as free from deviation with its nature as uncreated. The interpretation shows that early authorities understood the Quran's perfection as evidence that it is not a created entity, because created things are subject to change and imperfection. The Quran's freedom from error or contradiction indicates it is from Allah's eternal attribute of speech.

Key Terms
غير مخلوق (uncreated)
عربي (Arabic)
غير ذي عوج (without deviation)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some consider Ibn Abbas's interpretation as merely his personal opinion, lacking authoritative weight.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari presents this as an authoritative narration from a Companion, showing early scholarly consensus on the Quran's uncreated nature.

Checkpoint

A) As the Quran being easy to understand
B) As the Quran being uncreated
C) As the Quran having no contradictions
D) As the Quran being in Arabic

Key Takeaway
The report from Ibn Abbas equates the Quran's freedom from deviation with its uncreated status, showing scriptural basis for the doctrine.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you read the Quran as a perfect, uncreated book from Allah, or do you approach it as a human text subject to criticism? How would your daily recitation change if you truly believed every word is free from deviance and from Allah's eternal speech?
?
Ibn Abbas saw the Quran's perfection as proof of its divinity. What imperfections or doubts do you still hold about the Quran that you need to resolve to fully submit to its uncreated authority?
?
If the Quran is uncreated and perfect, then every command within it is from the eternal. Which command have you been neglecting as if it were a created, optional suggestion?

The Quran: Neither Creator Nor Created
Al-Ash'ari reports Ja'far al-Sadiq's famous statement on the Quran's uncreated status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ja'far al-Sadiq's precise formulation that the Quran is neither creator nor created, and why this became a standard Sunni position.

Core Idea
The Quran is neither creator nor created—it is the uncreated attribute of Allah.

Ja'far al-Sadiq, a revered figure from the Ahl al-Bayt, provided a concise formulation that avoids two errors: saying the Quran is created (as the Jahmiyya claimed) or saying it is a creator (as if it were independent of Allah). His statement 'la khaliq wa la makhluq' has become a standard Sunni slogan. In this lesson, you will see how this brief sentence encapsulates the correct stance on the nature of the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Read the source statement
Read the Arabic and translation of Ja'far al-Sadiq's statement. Notice its balanced wording.
2
Understand the two denials
The phrase denies two things: that the Quran is a creator and that it is created. Reflect on why both denials are necessary.
Denying 'creator' prevents elevating the Quran to deity; denying 'created' preserves its eternal attribute status.
3
See how it counters extremes
This formulation opposes both the Jahmiyya (who said the Quran is created) and any view that would make the Quran an independent creator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١٢٩ - وصحت الرواية عن جعفر بن محمد أن القرآن لا خالق ولا مخلوق. وروي ذلك عن عمه زيد بن علي، وعن جده علي بن الحسين رضي الله عنهم أجمعين
129 – And the narration from Ja'far bin Muhammad is authentic that the Quran is neither creator nor created. And that is narrated from his uncle Zayd bin 'Ali, and from his grandfather 'Ali bin al-Husayn, may Allah be pleased with them all.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is a transmission of a key formulation from the Ahl al-Bayt. Ja'far al-Sadiq says the Quran is neither creator nor created. This statement is carefully balanced: it denies that the Quran is a created entity (makhluq) while also denying that it is a creator (khaliq) in the sense of being an independent agent. Rather, the Quran is the uncreated attribute of Allah. Al-Ash'ari notes that this position is also attributed to Zayd bin Ali and Ali bin Husayn (Zayn al-Abidin), showing continuity among early imams. The formula 'la khaliq wa la makhluq' became a standard Sunni slogan against both those who said the Quran is created (Jahmiyya) and those who might elevate it to a co-creator (extreme literalism).

Key Terms
لا خالق ولا مخلوق (neither creator nor created)
جعفر بن محمد (Ja'far bin Muhammad)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'neither creator nor created' means the Quran is nothing or non-existent.
Correction: It means the Quran is the uncreated attribute of Allah, not a separate object. It exists as an attribute, not as an independent substance.

Checkpoint
What is the meaning of Ja'far al-Sadiq's statement that the Quran is 'la khaliq wa la makhluq'?
A) The Quran is a created thing but not a creator
B) The Quran is not a creator and not created, but is Allah's uncreated attribute
C) The Quran is eternal and divine like Allah
D) The Quran does not exist

Key Takeaway
Ja'far al-Sadiq's phrase 'la khaliq wa la makhluq' affirms the Quran is Allah's uncreated attribute, neither a separate creator nor a mere creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you treat the Quran as if it were a creation of your own mind, subject to your interpretation and convenience? This lesson says it is neither created nor a creator. When you read the Quran tonight, will you remember that it is Allah's uncreated speech, demanding submission, not negotiation?
?
Ja'far al-Sadiq's words guard against two extremes: making the Quran a mere book (created) or making it a partner (creator). Which extreme do you lean towards in your heart? Do you sometimes reduce the Quran to a product of history, or do you sometimes elevate your own understanding of it to equal divine command? Commit to opening the Mushaf with the awareness that it is Allah's attribute, not your project.
?
The statement 'neither creator nor created' is not just theology; it determines how you listen to every verse. If the Quran is uncreated, then every command in it has the same authority as if Allah spoke it directly to you now. Does your daily response to the Quran reflect that reality? What will you change today in how you approach its recitation?

The Quran's Excellence and the Verse of Luqman
Al-Ash'ari presents three initial proofs for the uncreated Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari uses the Quran's unparalleled excellence and the verse about its inexhaustibility to argue that the Quran is not created.

Core Idea
The Quran's superiority over all speech proves it is from Allah and not created.

This opening passage from al-Ash'ari draws a powerful analogy to highlight the Quran's divine origin. He then cites a verse that speaks of the inexhaustibility of Allah's words, and a companion's exhortation to draw near to Allah through His speech. Together, these three proofs lay the foundation for the doctrine that the Quran is uncreated.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the flow from a comparison to a verse to a narrative.
The Arabic is concise; each sentence adds a new layer.
2
Examine the opening analogy
Identify how the excellence of the Quran is likened to the excellence of Allah over creation. What does this imply about the Quran's nature?
This analogy sets the tone for the entire argument.
3
Analyze the verse from Luqman (31:27)
The verse states that if all trees were pens and oceans ink, Allah's words would never run out. Consider how this underscores the eternal, uncreated nature of the Quran as part of those words.
The verse is used as scriptural evidence that Allah's speech is infinite.
4
Reflect on Khabbab's advice
Khabbab ibn al-Aratt encourages drawing near to Allah through His speech. What does this say about the Quran's status?
The speech of Allah is the most beloved means of proximity to Him.
5
Synthesize the three proofs
Summarize how these three pieces – analogy, verse, and narration – collectively support the uncreatedness of the Quran.
Each proof reinforces the divine, uncreated origin of the Quran.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ فَضْلَ الْقُرْآنِ عَلَى سَائِرِ الْكَلَامِ كَفَضْلِ اللَّهِ عَلَى خَلْقِهِ، وَذَلِكَ أَنَّهُ مِنْهُ. وَذَكَرَ سُنَيْدُ بْنُ دَاوُدَ قَالَ حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو سُفْيَانَ عَنْ مَعْمَرٍ عَنْ قَتَادَةَ قَوْلَهُ تَعَالَى: {وَلَوْ أَنَّمَا فِي الْأَرْضِ مِنْ شَجَرَةٍ أَقْلَامٌ وَالْبَحْرُ يَمُدُّهُ مِنْ بَعْدِهِ سَبْعَةُ أَبْحُرٍ مَا نَفِدَتْ كَلِمَتُ اللَّهِ} الْآيَةَ [لُقْمَانَ: ٢٧]. وَذَكَرَ هَارُونَ بْنَ مَعْرُوفٍ قَالَ حَدَّثَنَا جَرِيرٌ عَنْ مَنْصُورٍ عَنْ هِلَالِ بْنِ يِسَافٍ عَنْ فَرْوَةَ بْنِ نَوْفَلٍ قَالَ: كُنْتُ جَارًا لِخَبَّابِ بْنِ الْأَرَتِّ، فَقَالَ لِي: يَا هَذَا تَقَرَّبْ إِلَى اللَّهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ بِمَا اسْتَطَعْتَ فَإِنَّكَ لَنْ تَتَقَرَّبَ إِلَى اللَّهِ بِشَيْءٍ أَحَبَّ إِلَيْهِ مِنْ كَلَامِهِ. وَرُوِيَ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا فِي قَوْلِهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ: {قُرْآَنًا عَرَبِيًّا غَيْرَ ذِي عِوَجٍ} [الزَّمَرِ: ٢٨] قَالَ: غَيْرُ مَخْلُوقٍ. وَرَوَى اللَّيْثُ بْنُ يَحْيَى قَالَ: حَدَّثَنِي إِبْرَاهِيمُ بْنُ أَبِي الْأَشْعَثِ قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ مُؤَمَّلَ بْنَ إِسْمَاعِيلَ يُحَدِّثُ عَنِ الثَّوْرِيِّ قَالَ: مَنْ زَعَمَ أَنَّ الْقُرْآنَ مَخْلُوقٌ فَقَدْ كَفَرَ. وَصَحَّتِ الرِّوَايَةُ عَنْ جَعْفَرِ بْنِ مُحَمَّدٍ أَنَّ الْقُرْآنَ لَا خَالِقَ وَلَا مَخْلُوقَ. وَرُوِيَ ذَلِكَ عَنْ عَمِّهِ زَيْدِ بْنِ عَلِيٍّ، وَعَنْ جَدِّهِ عَلِيِّ بْنِ الْحُسَيْنِ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمْ أَجْمَعِينَ.
Indeed, the excellence of the Quran over all other speech is like the excellence of Allah over His creation, and that is because it is from Him. And Sanad ibn Dawud mentioned, he said: Abu Sufyan narrated to us from Ma'mar from Qatada regarding the saying of the Exalted: {And if whatever trees upon the earth were pens and the sea [were ink], replenished thereafter by seven seas, the words of Allah would not be exhausted} the verse [Luqman: 27]. And Harun ibn Ma'ruf mentioned, he said: Jarir narrated to us from Mansur from Hilal ibn Yasaf from Farwa ibn Nawfal who said: I was a neighbor of Khabbab ibn al-Aratt, and he said to me: O this one, draw near to Allah Almighty as much as you are able, for you will never draw near to Allah with anything more beloved to Him than His speech. And it is narrated from Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both, regarding the saying of the Exalted: {An Arabic Quran, without any deviance} [az-Zumar: 28], he said: Uncreated. And al-Layth ibn Yahya narrated, he said: Ibrahim ibn Abi al-Ash'ath narrated to me, he said: I heard Mu'ammal ibn Isma'il narrating from al-Thawri, he said: Whoever claims that the Quran is created has indeed disbelieved. And the narration is authenticated from Ja'far ibn Muhammad that the Quran is neither creator nor created. And that was narrated from his uncle Zayd ibn Ali and from his grandfather Ali ibn al-Husayn, may Allah be pleased with them all.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage presents a series of narrations and scholarly statements establishing that the Quran is not created. The author begins by quoting a hadith-like statement: 'The excellence of the Quran over all other speech is like the excellence of Allah over His creation,' implying the Quran's divine origin and unparalleled status. Then he cites the verse from Surah Luqman about the inexhaustibility of Allah's words, indicating the Quran as part of those words. Next, a narration from Khabbab ibn al-Aratt encourages seeking closeness to Allah through His speech, showing its virtuous nature. The author then quotes Ibn Abbas interpreting 'without deviance' as 'uncreated', directly stating the Quran is not created. Then al-Thawri declares that whoever claims the Quran is created has disbelieved, a strong condemnation. Finally, Ja'far al-Sadiq and his uncle and grandfather affirm that the Quran is neither creator nor created—meaning it is not a creation, nor does it create; it is the uncreated speech of Allah. These sources collectively build the case that the Quran is uncreated, a core tenet of Sunni belief.

Key Terms
كلام الله
غير مخلوق
فضل القرآن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Assuming the Quran is just another created book, like human compositions.
Correction: The passage shows the Quran's excellence is divine, its words are inexhaustible (unlike created things), and it is the most beloved speech to Allah, all pointing to its uncreated nature.

Checkpoint
What does the verse from Luqman (31:27) illustrate about the words of Allah?
A) They are limited and finite.
B) They are inexhaustible and infinite.
C) They are created and temporary.
D) They are only for the prophets.

Key Takeaway
The Quran's excellence, its inexhaustibility, and its being the most beloved speech to Allah all demonstrate it is the uncreated speech of Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Quran is more excellent than all other speech, why do you spend more time listening to podcasts, music, or gossip than reciting it? What would it take for you to prioritize hearing from Allah?
?
Khabbab said you will never draw near to Allah with anything more beloved to Him than His speech. When you stand in prayer, do you truly feel you are drawing near to Allah? If not, what is missing in your heart?
?
The verse of Luqman shows that Allah's words are inexhaustible. How much of that infinite speech have you made an effort to learn and understand? Commit to one action today that shows you value His words above all others.

Ibn Abbas and Early Scholars on the Uncreated Quran
Al-Ash'ari presents three authoritative statements affirming the uncreated Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari uses the interpretation of Ibn Abbas and stark statements from al-Thawri and Ja'far al-Sadiq to affirm that the Quran is uncreated and that opposing this is disbelief.

Core Idea
The Quran is neither creator nor created; it is the eternal speech of Allah.

After presenting earlier proofs, al-Ash'ari now turns to explicit interpretations and declarations. Ibn Abbas interprets 'without deviance' as meaning uncreated. Al-Thawri declares that calling the Quran created is disbelief. Ja'far al-Sadiq articulates the precise formulation: the Quran is neither creator nor created. These statements from authoritative figures leave no doubt about the Sunni position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the chain of narrations and the precise wording of each statement.
Each statement is attributed to a respected scholar or imam.
2
Understand Ibn Abbas's interpretation
Ibn Abbas explains that the Quran being 'without deviance' means it is uncreated. How does this connect to the concept of creation?
Deviance implies created imperfection; its absence indicates divine, uncreated perfection.
3
Analyze al-Thawri's declaration
Al-Thawri explicitly says that claiming the Quran is created is disbelief. Why is this statement so strong?
It categorizes the belief as a matter of faith, not just a minor error.
4
Reflect on Ja'far's formula
Ja'far al-Sadiq states the Quran is 'neither creator nor created'. What does this negate?
It denies both that it is a creator (like Allah) and that it is a creation (like creatures).
5
Synthesize the three authorities
Summarize how these three statements collectively establish the uncreatedness of the Quran as a core doctrine.
They cover interpretation, explicit declaration, and precise theological formulation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ فَضْلَ الْقُرْآنِ عَلَى سَائِرِ الْكَلَامِ كَفَضْلِ اللَّهِ عَلَى خَلْقِهِ، وَذَلِكَ أَنَّهُ مِنْهُ. وَذَكَرَ سُنَيْدُ بْنُ دَاوُدَ قَالَ حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو سُفْيَانَ عَنْ مَعْمَرٍ عَنْ قَتَادَةَ قَوْلَهُ تَعَالَى: {وَلَوْ أَنَّمَا فِي الْأَرْضِ مِنْ شَجَرَةٍ أَقْلَامٌ وَالْبَحْرُ يَمُدُّهُ مِنْ بَعْدِهِ سَبْعَةُ أَبْحُرٍ مَا نَفِدَتْ كَلِمَتُ اللَّهِ} الْآيَةَ [لُقْمَانَ: ٢٧]. وَذَكَرَ هَارُونَ بْنَ مَعْرُوفٍ قَالَ حَدَّثَنَا جَرِيرٌ عَنْ مَنْصُورٍ عَنْ هِلَالِ بْنِ يِسَافٍ عَنْ فَرْوَةَ بْنِ نَوْفَلٍ قَالَ: كُنْتُ جَارًا لِخَبَّابِ بْنِ الْأَرَتِّ، فَقَالَ لِي: يَا هَذَا تَقَرَّبْ إِلَى اللَّهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ بِمَا اسْتَطَعْتَ فَإِنَّكَ لَنْ تَتَقَرَّبَ إِلَى اللَّهِ بِشَيْءٍ أَحَبَّ إِلَيْهِ مِنْ كَلَامِهِ. وَرُوِيَ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا فِي قَوْلِهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ: {قُرْآَنًا عَرَبِيًّا غَيْرَ ذِي عِوَجٍ} [الزَّمَرِ: ٢٨] قَالَ: غَيْرُ مَخْلُوقٍ. وَرَوَى اللَّيْثُ بْنُ يَحْيَى قَالَ: حَدَّثَنِي إِبْرَاهِيمُ بْنُ أَبِي الْأَشْعَثِ قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ مُؤَمَّلَ بْنَ إِسْمَاعِيلَ يُحَدِّثُ عَنِ الثَّوْرِيِّ قَالَ: مَنْ زَعَمَ أَنَّ الْقُرْآنَ مَخْلُوقٌ فَقَدْ كَفَرَ. وَصَحَّتِ الرِّوَايَةُ عَنْ جَعْفَرِ بْنِ مُحَمَّدٍ أَنَّ الْقُرْآنَ لَا خَالِقَ وَلَا مَخْلُوقَ. وَرُوِيَ ذَلِكَ عَنْ عَمِّهِ زَيْدِ بْنِ عَلِيٍّ، وَعَنْ جَدِّهِ عَلِيِّ بْنِ الْحُسَيْنِ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمْ أَجْمَعِينَ.
Indeed, the excellence of the Quran over all other speech is like the excellence of Allah over His creation, and that is because it is from Him. And Sanad ibn Dawud mentioned, he said: Abu Sufyan narrated to us from Ma'mar from Qatada regarding the saying of the Exalted: {And if whatever trees upon the earth were pens and the sea [were ink], replenished thereafter by seven seas, the words of Allah would not be exhausted} the verse [Luqman: 27]. And Harun ibn Ma'ruf mentioned, he said: Jarir narrated to us from Mansur from Hilal ibn Yasaf from Farwa ibn Nawfal who said: I was a neighbor of Khabbab ibn al-Aratt, and he said to me: O this one, draw near to Allah Almighty as much as you are able, for you will never draw near to Allah with anything more beloved to Him than His speech. And it is narrated from Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both, regarding the saying of the Exalted: {An Arabic Quran, without any deviance} [az-Zumar: 28], he said: Uncreated. And al-Layth ibn Yahya narrated, he said: Ibrahim ibn Abi al-Ash'ath narrated to me, he said: I heard Mu'ammal ibn Isma'il narrating from al-Thawri, he said: Whoever claims that the Quran is created has indeed disbelieved. And the narration is authenticated from Ja'far ibn Muhammad that the Quran is neither creator nor created. And that was narrated from his uncle Zayd ibn Ali and from his grandfather Ali ibn al-Husayn, may Allah be pleased with them all.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage presents a series of narrations and scholarly statements establishing that the Quran is not created. The author begins by quoting a hadith-like statement: 'The excellence of the Quran over all other speech is like the excellence of Allah over His creation,' implying the Quran's divine origin and unparalleled status. Then he cites the verse from Surah Luqman about the inexhaustibility of Allah's words, indicating the Quran as part of those words. Next, a narration from Khabbab ibn al-Aratt encourages seeking closeness to Allah through His speech, showing its virtuous nature. The author then quotes Ibn Abbas interpreting 'without deviance' as 'uncreated', directly stating the Quran is not created. Then al-Thawri declares that whoever claims the Quran is created has disbelieved, a strong condemnation. Finally, Ja'far al-Sadiq and his uncle and grandfather affirm that the Quran is neither creator nor created—meaning it is not a creation, nor does it create; it is the uncreated speech of Allah. These sources collectively build the case that the Quran is uncreated, a core tenet of Sunni belief.

Key Terms
غير مخلوق
مخلوق
لا خالق ولا مخلوق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking the Quran is a created entity like other books, or that it was created in time.
Correction: Ibn Abbas interprets 'without deviance' as uncreated, al-Thawri calls such belief disbelief, and Ja'far says it is neither creator nor created—all affirming its eternal, uncreated nature.

Checkpoint
According to al-Thawri, what is the ruling on someone who says the Quran is created?
A) He is a sinner but still a believer.
B) He has disbelieved.
C) He is excused because of ignorance.
D) He must repent but remains Muslim.

Key Takeaway
Authoritative figures from early Islam unequivocally affirm that the Quran is uncreated, and denying this is a grave error.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly honor the Quran as the uncreated speech of Allah, or do you treat it as just another book? How would your life change if you lived with this conviction today?
?
If you heard someone claim the Quran is created, how would you respond based on what you've learned? What responsibility do you have to correct this error?
?
Ibn Abbas saw the Quran's perfection as proof of its uncreatedness. Where in your life do you fail to see the Quran as perfect and uncreated, leading you to doubt or neglect it?

The Consensus of the Salaf on the Uncreated Quran
Ash'ari enumerates many scholars who held the Quran is uncreated.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the belief that the Quran is uncreated was held by a vast majority of early Sunni scholars, including the founders of the four schools of law.

Core Idea
The uncreatedness of the Quran was the consensus of the early imams.

Imam al-Ash'ari presents a long list of renowned scholars from the early generations who affirmed that the Quran is uncreated and that those who claim it is created are disbelievers. This passage demonstrates that this belief was not a fringe position but the mainstream view of Ahl al-Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing it. Then read the translation. Notice the names of the scholars listed.
The list includes the founders of the four Sunni madhhabs.
2
Identify key figures
Find the names of Abu Hanifa, Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad ibn Hanbal in the list. Note that they are all included.
These four imams are explicitly mentioned.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider that Ash'ari cites this extensive list to show that the position is not a minority view but the consensus of the early scholars. Ask yourself: why would he do this?
This was a response to the Mu'tazilite claim that the Quran is created.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ قَالَ: إِنَّ الْقُرْآنَ غَيْرُ مَخْلُوقٍ، وَإِنَّ مَنْ قَالَ بِخَلْقِهِ كَافِرٌ، الْعُلَمَاءُ وَحَمَلَةُ الْآثَارِ وَنَقَلَةُ الْأَخْبَارِ لَا يُحْصَوْنَ كَثْرَةً، مِنْهُمُ: الْحَمَّادَانِ، وَالثَّوْرِيُّ، وَعَبْدُ الْعَزِيزِ بْنُ أَبِي سَلَمَةَ، وَمَالِكُ بْنُ أَنَسٍ، وَالشَّافِعِيُّ وَأَصْحَابُهُ، وَأَبُو حَنِيفَةَ، وَأَحْمَدُ بْنُ حَنْبَلٍ، وَاللَّيْثُ بْنُ سَعْدٍ، وَسُفْيَانُ بْنُ عُيَيْنَةَ، وَهِشَامٌ، وَعِيسَى بْنُ يُونُسَ، وَحَفْصُ بْنُ غِيَاثٍ، وَسَعْدُ بْنُ عَامِرٍ، وَعَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنُ مَهْدِيٍّ، وَأَبُو بَكْرِ بْنُ عَيَّاشٍ، وَوَكِيعٌ، وَأَبُو عَاصِمٍ النَّبِيلُ، وَيَعْلَى بْنُ عُبَيْدٍ، وَمُحَمَّدُ بْنُ يُوسُفَ، وَبِشْرُ بْنُ الْمُفَضَّلِ، وَعَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ دَاوُدَ، وَسَلَّامُ بْنُ أَبِي مُطِيعٍ، وَابْنُ الْمُبَارَكِ، وَعَلِيُّ بْنُ عَاصِمٍ، وَأَحْمَدُ بْنُ يُونُسَ، وَأَبُو نُعَيْمٍ، وَقَبِيصَةُ بْنُ عُقْبَةَ، وَسُلَيْمَانُ بْنُ دَاوُدَ، وَأَبُو عُبَيْدٍ الْقَاسِمُ بْنُ سَلَّامٍ، وَيَزِيدُ بْنُ هَارُونَ، وَغَيْرُهُمْ. وَلَوْ تَتَبَّعْنَا ذِكْرَ مَنْ يَقُولُ بِذَلِكَ لَطَالَ الْكَلَامُ بِذِكْرِهِمْ، وَفِيمَا ذَكَرْنَا مُقْنِعٌ، وَالْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ.
And whoever says that the Quran is uncreated, and that whoever says it is created is a disbeliever—the scholars, bearers of traditions, and transmitters of reports are uncountable in number. Among them are: al-Hammadan, al-Thawri, Abd al-Aziz ibn Abi Salama, Malik ibn Anas, al-Shafi'i and his companions, Abu Hanifa, Ahmad ibn Hanbal, al-Layth ibn Sa'd, Sufyan ibn Uyayna, Hisham, Isa ibn Yunus, Hafs ibn Ghiyath, Sa'd ibn Amir, Abd al-Rahman ibn Mahdi, Abu Bakr ibn Ayyash, Waki', Abu Asim al-Nabil, Ya'la ibn Ubayd, Muhammad ibn Yusuf, Bishr ibn al-Mufaddal, Abd Allah ibn Dawud, Sallam ibn Abi Muti', Ibn al-Mubarak, Ali ibn Asim, Ahmad ibn Yunus, Abu Nu'aym, Qabisa ibn Uqba, Sulayman ibn Dawud, Abu Ubayd al-Qasim ibn Sallam, Yazid ibn Harun, and others. And if we were to pursue mentioning those who say that, the speech would be lengthy in mentioning them, and in what we have mentioned is sufficient, and praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of the scholars who held that the Quran is uncreated and that anyone who claims it is created is a disbeliever. The author begins by stating that such scholars, bearers of traditions, and transmitters of reports are beyond counting. Then he lists many of them by name. They include: 1. al-Hammadan (i.e., Hammad ibn Zaid and Hammad ibn Salamah), 2. al-Thawri (Sufyan al-Thawri), 3. Abd al-Aziz ibn Abi Salama, 4. Malik ibn Anas (founder of the Maliki school), 5. al-Shafi'i and his companions (founder of the Shafi'i school), 6. Abu Hanifa (founder of the Hanafi school), 7. Ahmad ibn Hanbal (founder of the Hanbali school), 8. al-Layth ibn Sa'd, 9. Sufyan ibn Uyayna, 10. Hisham (probably Hisham ibn Urwa or Hisham al-Dastuwai), 11. Isa ibn Yunus, 12. Hafs ibn Ghiyath, 13. Sa'd ibn Amir, 14. Abd al-Rahman ibn Mahdi, 15. Abu Bakr ibn Ayyash, 16. Waki' ibn al-Jarrah, 17. Abu Asim al-Nabil, 18. Ya'la ibn Ubayd, 19. Muhammad ibn Yusuf, 20. Bishr ibn al-Mufaddal, 21. Abd Allah ibn Dawud, 22. Sallam ibn Abi Muti', 23. Ibn al-Mubarak (Abd Allah ibn al-Mubarak), 24. Ali ibn Asim, 25. Ahmad ibn Yunus, 26. Abu Nu'aym al-Fadl ibn Dukayn, 27. Qabisa ibn Uqba, 28. Sulayman ibn Dawud (al-Tayalisi), 29. Abu Ubayd al-Qasim ibn Sallam, 30. Yazid ibn Harun, and others. The author notes that listing everyone would be too lengthy, so the cited names suffice. This demonstrates that the uncreatedness of the Quran was the consensus of the early scholars (salaf).

كافر

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only a few early scholars held that the Quran is uncreated.
Correction: Ash'ari's extensive list shows it was the consensus of the early imams including the founders of the four schools.

The Uncreated Quran: Proof from Revelation
Ash'ari states proof from Quran and dismisses opponents as ignorant.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ash'ari grounds the doctrine of the uncreated Quran in the Quran itself and dismisses opposing views as lacking scholarly authority.

Core Idea
The Quran proves its own uncreatedness; opponents are ignorant outsiders.

In this concluding passage, Ash'ari reinforces his position on the Quran's uncreatedness by pointing to divine proof within the Quran itself. He then dismisses those who claim otherwise as being outside the scholarly tradition. This lesson helps you see how early Sunni theology combined scriptural argument with a strong sense of communal authority.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Notice the confident tone and the key terms like احتجاج and برهان.
The passage is a single rhetorical unit.
2
Identify the source of proof
Ash'ari says he argued from the Book of Allah (القرآن). Underline that phrase. The proof is not from reason or tradition but from the Quran itself.
This is central to his method.
3
Analyze the dismissal of opponents
Notice how Ash'ari characterizes opponents: 'rabble' (رعاع) and 'ignorant' (جهال). He denies that any reliable scholar held the created Quran view.
This is a strong rhetorical move.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
He says his previous argument suffices to refute falsehood. Consider how this passage ties the whole discussion together.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَدِ احْتَجَجْنَا لِصِحَّةِ قَوْلِنَا: إِنَّ الْقُرْآنَ غَيْرُ مَخْلُوقٍ مِنْ كِتَابِ اللَّهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ، وَمَا تَضَمَّنَهُ مِنَ الْبُرْهَانِ، وَأَوْضَحَهُ مِنَ الْبَيَانِ، وَلَمْ نَجِدْ أَحَدًا مِمَّنْ تُحْمَلُ عَنْهُ الْآثَارُ، وَتُنْقَلُ عَنْهُ الْأَخْبَارُ، وَيَأْتَمُ بِهِ الْمُؤْتَمُونَ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْعِلْمِ، يَقُولُ بِخَلْقِ الْقُرْآنِ، وَإِنَّمَا قَالَ ذَلِكَ رَعَاعُ النَّاسِ، وَجُهَّالٌ مِنْ جُهَّالِهِمْ لَا مَوْقِعَ لِقَوْلِهِمْ. وَالْحَجَاجُ الَّذِي قَدَّمْنَاهُ فِي ذَلِكَ يَأْتِي عَلَى كَثِيرٍ مِنْ قَوْلِهِمْ وَدَفْعِ بَاطِلِهِمْ، وَالْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ عَلَى قُوَّةِ الْحَقِّ حَمْدًا كَثِيرًا.
And we have argued for the correctness of our statement: that the Quran is uncreated, from the Book of Allah Almighty, and what it contains of proof, and what it clarifies of explanation. And we have not found anyone among those from whom traditions are carried, from whom reports are transmitted, and whom the followers follow among the people of knowledge, who says that the Quran is created. Only the rabble of the people said that, and the ignorant among their ignorant ones, whose saying carries no weight. And the argument that we presented in that matter covers much of their saying and refutes their falsehood. And praise be to Allah for the strength of truth, abundant praise.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage concludes the discussion by stating that the author and his school have argued for the uncreatedness of the Quran using the Quran itself as proof. They claim that no reliable scholar holding authoritative traditions and followed by the community ever said the Quran is created; rather, only the ignorant and insignificant people say so. The argument already presented (in previous sections) suffices to refute their falsehood. This is a strong rhetorical stance, asserting consensus among the Ahl al-Sunnah and dismissing the opposing view as baseless.

Key Terms
احتجاج
برهان
بيان
رعاع الناس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The view that the Quran is created was held by some early scholars and is a legitimate theological opinion.
Correction: Ash'ari claims that no reliable scholar (those from whom traditions are taken and who are followed by the community) ever held that the Quran is created. The created Quran view is attributed only to the ignorant rabble.

Checkpoint
According to Ash'ari, where did he derive the proof that the Quran is uncreated?
A) From the sayings of scholars
B) From the Book of Allah
C) From reason alone
D) From the consensus of the community

Key Takeaway
Ash'ari grounds the uncreatedness of the Quran in the Quran itself and denies that any authoritative scholar ever held the created view.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Ash‘ari labels those who say the Quran is created as 'rabble' and 'ignorant'. Reflect on your own life: are there any Islamic beliefs you hold simply because they are popular or convenient, rather than because they are proven from the Quran and Sunnah? What will you do today to ensure you are following the path of the 'people of knowledge'?
?
The passage claims that no true scholar ever held the created view. Who are the scholars you rely on for your Islamic knowledge? Are they people who carry traditions, transmit reports, and are followed by the community? If not, what step will you take to connect with reliable teachers?
?
Ash‘ari asserts that the Quran itself contains the proof of its uncreatedness. When was the last time you felt the Quran convincing you of a truth so deeply that you could not deny it? How can you make the Quran your primary source of evidence in matters of faith, especially when others offer conflicting opinions?

Ashari's Proof and Dismissal on the Quran's Uncreatedness
Imam Ashari claims scriptural proof and dismisses opponents as rabble.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Ashari's claim of scriptural proof for the uncreatedness of the Quran and his dismissal of opposing views as lacking scholarly authority.

Core Idea
Imam Ashari grounds the Quran's uncreatedness in scripture and dismisses opponents as ignoramuses.

In this passage, Imam Ashari confidently states that he has already provided proof from the Quran itself that the Quran is uncreated. He then makes a sociological argument: no reliable scholar holds the view that it is created; only ignorant people do. This sets the stage for a polemical defense of a core Sunni doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to absorb its rhythm, then read the literal translation. Notice the confident tone and the structure: claim of proof, then dismissal of opponents, then praise.
The passage is short but packs a strong assertion.
2
Identify the two main claims
Ashari makes two moves: (1) he says he has argued from the Quran that the Quran is uncreated; (2) he says only rabble and ignorant people say it is created, not reliable scholars. Locate these in the text.
3
Examine the dismissal
Observe how Ashari characterizes his opponents: 'rabble' (رعاع) and 'ignorant among their ignorant.' He denies their statement any weight. Why would he use such strong language?
This reflects the high stakes of the debate.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Ashari ends with praise of Allah for the strength of truth. Consider how this serves both as a theological affirmation and a rhetorical closure.
It reinforces his confidence in his position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد احتججنا لصحة قولنا : ( إن القرآن غير مخلوق » من كتاب الله عز وجل، وما تضمنه من البرهان، وأوضحه من البيان، ولم نجد أحداً ممن تُحمل عنه الآثار، وتنقل عنه الأخبار، ويأتم به المؤتمون من أهل العلم، يقول بخلق القرآن، وإنما قال ذلك رعاع الناس، وجهال من جهالهم لا موقع لقولهم . والحجاج الذي قدمناه في ذلك يأتي على كثير من قولهم ودفع باطلهم، والحمد لله على قوة الحق حمداً كثيراً .
And we have argued for the correctness of our statement that 'the Quran is uncreated' from the Book of Allah, mighty and majestic, and what it contains of proof and clarifies of explanation. And we did not find anyone among those from whom reports are conveyed and narrations are transmitted and whom the leaders among the people of knowledge follow, who says that the Quran is created. Only the rabble of the people and the ignorant among their ignorant say that, whose statement has no weight. And the arguments we have presented in that regard cover much of their statement and refute their falsehood. And praise be to Allah for the strength of truth, abundant praise.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a claim of proof and a dismissal of opponents. Imam Ashari states that he has argued from the Quran itself that the Quran is uncreated. He then asserts that no reliable scholar (those from whom knowledge is transmitted and who are followed) says it is created. Only ignorant people and rabble make that claim, and their statement is worthless. The arguments he has presented suffice to refute them. He ends with praise. The passage is confident and polemical.
