The Hadith of Descent: Proof That Allah is Above His Throne
Imam Ash'ari cites the hadith of descent as proof for Allah being above the Throne.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Ash'ari uses the hadith of descent as a transmitted proof for Allah being above His Throne specifically, not everywhere.

Core Idea
The Prophet's hadith of descent affirms that Allah is above His Throne.

Imam Ash'ari now turns to transmitted evidence (naql) to support his position that Allah is istawa upon His Throne specifically. He cites a well-known hadith about Allah's descent to the lowest heaven. This hadith, understood literally in a way befitting Allah, confirms that Allah is above the heavens, i.e., above the Throne, not diffused in creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the fully provided Arabic text and its literal translation. Notice that the author includes a chain of narrators (isnad) and the text of the hadith (matn).
The chain: 'Affan → Hammad bin Salama → 'Amr bin Dinar → Nafi' bin Jubayr → his father (Jubayr bin Mut'im).
2
Understand the argument from this hadith
Imam Ash'ari argues that the hadith proves Allah is above the Throne. Why? Because Allah descends to the lowest heaven; that implies He is above it. If He were everywhere or not specifically above, the descent would be meaningless.
This is a transmitted proof (dalil naqli) supporting the rational proofs already given.
3
Reflect on the principle of affirming attributes
The author affirms the attribute of descent (nuzul) without comparing it to creation (tashbih) or denying it (ta'til). The descent is real but in a manner befitting Allah.
The common misunderstanding is to interpret descent metaphorically to avoid anthropomorphism.
4
Answer the checkpoint question
Test your understanding by answering the MCQ about what this hadith proves according to the author.
The correct answer is B: That Allah is specifically upon His Throne and not everywhere.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومما يؤكد أن الله عزّ وجل مستو على عرشه دون الأشياء كلها، ما نقله أهل الرواية عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم. روى عفان قال: ثنا حماد بن سلمة قال حدثنا عمرو بن دينار عن نافع بن جبير، عن أبيه، أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : ( ينزل ربنا عز وجل كل ليلة إلى السماء الدنيا، فيقول: هل من سائل فأعطيه، هل من مستغفر فأغفر له، حتى يطلع الفجر )
And among what confirms that Allah Almighty is istawa upon His Throne and not upon all things is what the people of narration have transmitted from the Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم. 'Affan narrated: Hammad bin Salama narrated to us: 'Amr bin Dinar narrated to us from Nafi' bin Jubayr, from his father, that the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم said: 'Our Lord, mighty and majestic, descends every night to the lowest heaven and says: Is there anyone asking so that I may give him? Is there anyone seeking forgiveness so that I may forgive him? until the dawn breaks.'
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a proof (daleel) that Allah is specifically istawa upon His Throne and not equally present in all things. Imam Ash'ari cites a hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that is well-known: the hadith of the descent of Allah to the lowest heaven during the last third of the night. The chain of narration is given: 'Affan from Hammad bin Salama from 'Amr bin Dinar from Nafi' bin Jubayr from his father (Jubayr bin Mut'im). The hadith states that Allah 'descends' to the lowest heaven, which implies that He is above that heaven (i.e., above the Throne) and that His descent is a real act. This supports the Ash'ari position that Allah is above His Throne in a manner befitting His majesty, and that He is not everywhere or merely abstractly present. The proof is from transmitted tradition (naql).

Key Terms
النزول (descent/nuzul)
السماء الدنيا (lowest heaven)
أهل الرواية (people of narration)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some interpret the descent of Allah as purely metaphorical (e.g., descent of mercy) to avoid anthropomorphism.
Correction: Imam Ash'ari uses the hadith to prove that Allah is above the Throne in a real sense, affirming the attribute without comparing it to creation.

Checkpoint
What does the hadith of descent prove according to Imam Ash'ari?
A) That Allah changes location
B) That Allah is specifically upon His Throne and not everywhere
C) That Allah descends into the earth
D) That Allah is physically close to people

Key Takeaway
The hadith of descent shows that Allah is above the lowest heaven, thus above His Throne, affirming His highness without comparison.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Every night, Allah descends and asks if anyone is seeking forgiveness. Have you ever woken up in the last part of the night and responded to that call? What is holding you back from seeking His forgiveness right now, tonight?
?
You believe Allah is above His Throne—does this reality make you feel closer to Him or more distant? When you raise your hands to pray, do you truly sense that you are supplicating to the One who is above, who hears and responds?
?
The hadith mentions both asking and seeking forgiveness. Which of these two are you most in need of right now? Will you take a moment after this lesson to actually ask Allah for it, or will you let this reminder slip away?

Hadith Evidence for Allah's Descent
Al-Ash'ari cites three hadiths on Allah's descent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Ash'ari uses multiple hadith chains to support the doctrine of Allah's descent to the lowest heaven, affirming His transcendence above creation.

Core Idea
Hadiths of Allah's descent prove His highness, not His omnipresence.

Al-Ash'ari has just established from reason and scripture that Allah is above His Throne, distinct from creation. Now he reinforces this with a series of prophetic hadiths that describe Allah descending to the lowest heaven. These reports, transmitted through multiple chains, are not to be interpreted metaphorically; they affirm a real attribute of Allah without modality or comparison. As you read, notice how each hadith emphasizes the time and purpose of the descent.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening statement
Understand how the introductory sentence connects the hadiths to the doctrine of Allah's istiwa' (establishment) on the Throne.
Al-Ash'ari states that these hadiths confirm what was previously argued from reason.
2
Examine the first hadith
Read the hadith from Nafi' ibn Jubayr and note its chain and content: Allah descends every night to the lowest heaven.
Notice the repetition of the phrase 'until dawn breaks.'
3
Compare all three hadiths
Identify the common elements: descent during the last third of the night, the call for supplicants, seekers of forgiveness, and those asking for provision.
Each hadith has a slightly different wording but the same core message.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومما يؤكد أن الله عزّ وجل مستو على عرشه دون الأشياء كلها، ما نقله أهل الرواية عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم.
روى عفان قال: ثنا حماد بن سلمة قال حدثنا عمرو بن دينار عن نافع بن جبير، عن أبيه، أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : ( يَنزِلُ رَبُّنَا عَزَّ وَجَلَّ كُلٌّ لَيْلَةٍ إِلَى السَّمَاءِ الدُّنْيَا، فَيَقُولُ: هَلْ مِنْ سَائِلِ فَأَعْطِيَهُ، هَلْ مِنْ مُسْتَغْفِرٍ فَأَغْفِرَ لَهُ، حَتَّى يَطْلُعَ الفجرُ )
وروى عبد الله بن بكر قال حدثنا هشام بن أبي عبد الله ، عن يحيى ابن أبي كثير ، عن أبي جعفر ، أنه سمع أبا هريرة قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: (إِذَا بَقِيَ ثُلث يَنْزِلُ الله تبارك وتعالى، فَيَقُولُ: مَنْ ذَا الَّذِي يَدْعُونِي فَأَسْتَجِيبَ لَهُ؟ مَنْ ذَا الَّذِي يَسْتَكْشِفَ الضُّرَّ فَأَكْشِفَهُ عَنْهُ؟ مَنْ ذَا الَّذِي يَسْتَرْزِقُنِي فَأَرْزَقَهُ حَتَّى يَنْفَجِرَ الْفَجْرُ .
وروى عبد الله بن بكر السهمي قال: حدثنا هشام بن أبي عبد الله عن يحيى بن كثير ، عن هلال بن أبي ميمونة، قال: حدثنا عطاء بن يسار، أن رفاعة الجهني حدثه، قال: فكنا مع رسول الله حتى إذا كنا بالكديد - أو قال بقديد - حمد الله وأثنى عليه، ثم قال : ( إِذَا مَضَى ثُلُثُ اللَّيْلِ - أَوْ قَالَ ثُلنَا اللَّيْلِ - نَزَلَ الله عَزَّ وَجَلَّ إِلَى السَّمَاءِ، فَيَقُولُ: مَنْ الَّذِي يَدْعُونِي أَسْتَجِبْ لَهُ؟ مَنْ ذَا الَّذِي يَسْتَغْفِرُنِي أَغْفِرَ لَهُ؟ مَنْ ذَا الَّذِي يَسْأَلُنِي أَعْطِهِ، حَتَّى يَنْفَجِرَ الْفَجْرُ )
And what confirms that Allah Almighty is established on His Throne (mustawin 'ala 'arshihi) apart from all things is what the transmitters have narrated from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace.
'Affan narrated: Hammad ibn Salama told us: 'Amr ibn Dinar told us from Nafi' ibn Jubayr, from his father, that the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: "Our Lord, Almighty and Exalted, descends every night to the lowest heaven and says: Is there anyone asking so that I may give him? Is there anyone seeking forgiveness so that I may forgive him? until dawn breaks."
And 'Abdullah ibn Bakr narrated: Hisham ibn Abi 'Abdullah told us from Yahya ibn Abi Kathir, from Abi Ja'far, that he heard Abu Hurayra say: The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: "When a third of the night remains, Allah, Blessed and Exalted, descends and says: Who is calling upon Me so that I may respond to him? Who is seeking the removal of harm so that I may remove it from him? Who is asking Me for provision so that I may provide for him? until dawn breaks."
And 'Abdullah ibn Bakr al-Sahmi narrated: Hisham ibn Abi 'Abdullah told us from Yahya ibn Kathir, from Hilal ibn Abi Maymuna, who said: 'Ata' ibn Yasar told us that Rifa'a al-Juhani told him: We were with the Messenger of Allah until we were at al-Kadid—or he said at Qadid—he praised Allah and extolled Him, then said: "When a third of the night has passed—or he said a third of the night—Allah Almighty descends to the heaven and says: Who is calling upon Me so that I may respond to him? Who is seeking My forgiveness so that I may forgive him? Who is asking Me so that I may give him? until dawn breaks."
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage provides hadith evidence for Allah's being established on the Throne. Al-Ash'ari begins by stating that the transmitted reports from the Prophet confirm that Allah is established on His Throne, distinct from all other things. He then records three hadiths on the authority of various companions, all describing Allah's descent to the lowest heaven during the last third of the night. These hadiths are used to support the doctrine that Allah is above the heavens, not everywhere, because descent implies a direction and a location from which one descends. The repetition of the same theme in multiple chains strengthens the argument.

Key Terms
نزول
السماء الدنيا
الحديث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith of descent is metaphorical and does not affirm a real attribute of Allah.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari presents these hadiths as literal evidence for Allah's descent without modality or comparison, affirming that He is above His Throne.

Checkpoint
What do the three hadiths cited in this lesson have in common?
A) They all describe Allah's descent to the lowest heaven during the night.
B) They all mention the Throne as the place of Allah.
C) They all deny that Allah is in every place.
D) They all contain a supplication to Allah.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari uses multiple hadith chains to prove that Allah descends to the lowest heaven during the last third of the night, affirming His transcendence above creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The hadiths describe Allah descending and asking, 'Is there anyone seeking forgiveness?' During the last third of the night, do you consistently wake up to seek His forgiveness, or do you prioritize sleep over this divine invitation? What is stopping you from responding tonight?
?
If you truly believed that Allah descends to the lowest heaven each night and personally calls to you—'Who is calling upon Me so that I may respond?'—would you still find it burdensome to make du'a in the depths of the night? Examine your heart: is your reluctance due to lack of conviction or lack of love?
?
Al-Ash'ari insists that the descent is a real attribute, not a metaphor. When you recite these hadiths, do you feel the weight of His nearness and respond with awe and action, or do you rationalize them away as mere stories? What would change in your worship if you lived with the certainty that He is truly close at that moment?

Allah's Descent: Affirming the Attribute
Imam al-Ashari cites a hadith on Allah’s descent and His response to supplicants.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ashari uses a hadith about Allah’s descent to affirm a divine attribute without ta’wil or tashbih.

Core Idea
Allah’s descent is real but not like any creature’s movement.

Imam al-Ashari opens his discussion of divine attributes with a well-known hadith that describes Allah descending to the lowest heaven. This is not a metaphor—for Ashari, it is a real act of Allah, but its modality is unknown. The hadith teaches us how to speak of Allah’s actions: affirm what He says about Himself, and stop where He stops.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Read the Arabic text and translation, noting the isnad (chain) and the content of Allah’s speech. The hadith has three rhetorical questions.
Pay attention to the wording of the questions.
2
Identify the key teachings
The hadith teaches that Allah descends, that He responds to supplication, removes harm, and provides. Note the timescale: until dawn breaks.
Three specific actions are mentioned.
3
Connect to Ashari methodology
Reflect on why al-Ashari chose this hadith: it affirms an attribute (nuzul) without explaining how. That is the Salaf way.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وروى عبد الله بن بكر قال حدثنا هشام بن أبي عبد الله ، عن يحيى ابن أبي كثير ، عن أبي جعفر ، أنه سمع أبا هريرة قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: (إِذَا بَقِيَ ثُلث يَنْزِلُ الله تبارك وتعالى، فَيَقُولُ: مَنْ ذَا الَّذِي يَدْعُونِي فَأَسْتَجِيبَ لَهُ؟ مَنْ ذَا الَّذِي يَسْتَكْشِفَ الضُّرَّ فَأَكْشِفَهُ عَنْهُ؟ مَنْ ذَا الَّذِي يَسْتَرْزِقُنِي فَأَرْزَقَهُ حَتَّى يَنْفَجِرَ الْفَجْرُ .
And Abdullah ibn Bakr narrated, saying: Hisham ibn Abi Abdullah narrated to us from Yahya ibn Abi Kathir from Abi Ja'far that he heard Abu Hurairah say: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'When one third remains, Allah, blessed and exalted, descends and says: Who is calling upon Me that I may respond to him? Who is seeking the removal of harm that I may remove it from him? Who is asking for provision that I may provide him? until dawn breaks.'
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a Prophetic hadith cited by Imam al-Ashari as evidence for the reality of Allah's attribute of descent (nuzul). The hadith explicitly states that Allah descends during the last third of the night and makes a series of rhetorical questions inviting supplication and need. Imam al-Ashari includes this to affirm the attribute without delving into how (bilā kayf), following the Salaf methodology. The isnad is sound, and the hadith is well-known. The phrase 'when one third remains' indicates a specific time, and the descent is a true action of Allah, not metaphorical. The questions emphasize Allah's responsiveness to those who call upon Him, seek relief, or ask for provision. The hadith reinforces the belief that Allah is above His creation and actively engages with it in a manner befitting His majesty.

Key Terms
نزول (nuzul)
دعاء (du'a)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah's descent is a physical movement like a creature moving from one place to another.
Correction: Asharis affirm the descent as a true attribute of Allah without modality (bilā kayf), avoiding both ta‘tīl (denial of the attribute) and tashbīh (likening to creation).

Checkpoint
What does the hadith indicate about Allah's attribute?
A) Allah changes location.
B) Allah descends in a manner known only to Him.
C) Allah descends physically.
D) The hadith is metaphorical.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Ashari uses the hadith of descent to affirm a divine attribute without explaining how, following the Salaf methodology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The hadith teaches that Allah descends specifically in the last third of the night and calls out for supplicants. Do you truly believe this happens every single night? Consider your own prayer habits: does your conviction in this hadith move you to wake up for qiyam, or do you treat it as a distant, theological fact that doesn't change your daily routine? What would it cost you to take the descent as a literal invitation tonight?
?
When you read the phrase 'ينزل' in the Arabic, your mind may want to rationalize it to make it less challenging. Are you uncomfortable with a descent that doesn't fit into your mental framework of space and time? What would it mean for your relationship with Allah if you simply accepted the hadith as it is, without trying to explain it away? Will you let this attribute of Allah—real descent—draw you to seek Him more intensely, or will you keep Him at a safe intellectual distance?

Second Hadith on Allah's Descent
Imam al-Ashari cites another hadith on Allah's descent with slight variation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the content and significance of another hadith on Allah's descent, including its chain and additional details.

Core Idea
Allah's descent is affirmed through multiple reliable narrations.

Imam al-Ashari now presents a second hadith on the same subject—Allah's descent in the last third of the night—with a different chain and slight wording variations. This repetition strengthens the evidence and helps address any doubts about the hadith's authenticity or interpretation. Pay attention to the added phrase about seeking forgiveness.

Guided Path
1
Read the Hadith Text
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the chain of narrators and the core message.
The hadith mentions two possible locations: al-Kadid or Qadid.
2
Identify the Additional Element
Compare this hadith with the first one (if known) or note that it includes the phrase 'who is seeking forgiveness from Me that I may forgive him'.
This adds the concept of seeking forgiveness (istighfar).
3
Reflect on the Meaning of 'Descent'
Think about what it means for Allah to descend without being contained in space. The commentary explains the Ashari position.
The descent is real but not physical—it is an act of Allah known only to Him.
4
Consider the Hadith's Purpose
Why did the Prophet mention this during a journey? It shows the importance of praying and seeking forgiveness in the last third of the night.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وروى عبد الله بن بكر السهمي قال: حدثنا هشام بن أبي عبد الله عن يحيى بن كثير ، عن هلال بن أبي ميمونة، قال: حدثنا عطاء بن يسار، أن رفاعة الجهني حدثه، قال: فكنا مع رسول الله حتى إذا كنا بالكديد - أو قال بقديد - حمد الله وأثنى عليه، ثم قال : ( إِذَا مَضَى ثُلُثُ اللَّيْلِ - أَوْ قَالَ ثُلنَا اللَّيْلِ - نَزَلَ الله عَزَّ وَجَلَّ إِلَى السَّمَاءِ، فَيَقُولُ: مَنْ الَّذِي يَدْعُونِي أَسْتَجِبْ لَهُ؟ مَنْ ذَا الَّذِي يَسْتَغْفِرُنِي أَغْفِرَ لَهُ؟ مَنْ ذَا الَّذِي يَسْأَلُنِي أَعْطِهِ، حَتَّى يَنْفَجِرَ الْفَجْرُه
And Abdullah ibn Bakr as-Sahmi narrated, saying: Hisham ibn Abi Abdullah narrated to us from Yahya ibn Kathir from Hilal ibn Abi Maimuna, who said: Ata ibn Yasar narrated to us that Rifa'a al-Juhani narrated to him, who said: We were with the Messenger of Allah until when we were at al-Kadid - or he said Qadid - he praised Allah and extolled Him, then said: 'When one third of the night has passed - or he said one third of the night - Allah, Almighty and Majestic, descends to the heaven and says: Who is calling upon Me that I may respond to him? Who is seeking forgiveness from Me that I may forgive him? Who is asking Me that I may give him? until dawn breaks.'
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This is another hadith, with a different chain and slight wording variation, affirming the same event: Allah's descent to the lowest heaven in the last third of the night. The narrator Rifa'a al-Juhani recalls the Prophet's words during a journey. The phrases 'إلى السماء' (to the heaven) and the inclusion of 'يستغفرني' (seeks forgiveness) add further detail. Imam al-Ashari likely includes multiple narrations to strengthen the evidence and address any doubts about the hadith's authenticity or meaning. The Ashari position is to accept the literal meaning as true while affirming Allah's transcendence above any likeness to creation. The descent is not a spatial movement from above to below in a physical sense, but a real act of Allah known only to Him.

Key Terms

سماء (sama')
استغفار (istighfar)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception: The phrase 'to the heaven' means Allah was elsewhere, implying a physical movement from a higher place to a lower place.
Correction: Ash'ari scholars interpret the descent as a true act of Allah that does not involve spatial transition as humans understand it. Allah is not confined to a place; His descent is a real event known only to Him.

Proof from Quran: Allah is Above His Creation
Imam al-Ashari cites multiple Quranic verses to prove Allah is above the heavens.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ashari uses Quranic verses to establish that Allah is above His creation, established on His Throne, while negating indwelling and union.

Core Idea
Allah is above His creation in a manner befitting His majesty.

In this passage, Imam al-Ashari presents a cumulative Quranic argument to affirm Allah's transcendence. He cites five verses that collectively indicate that Allah is above the heavens and established on His Throne. This lesson will guide you through these proofs and their theological significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation to get a sense of the flow.
The passage uses multiple verses connected by 'And He said'.
2
Identify each verse's key term
For each of the five verses, find the key Arabic word that indicates direction or position relative to Allah.
For example, 'min fawqihim' (above them) and 'ilayhi' (to Him).
3
Understand the conclusion
After listing the verses, Imam al-Ashari states that all this indicates Allah is 'in the heaven' and 'established on His Throne'. Reflect on what this means.
4
Grasp the negations
Notice that the passage ends by saying Allah's istiwa is free from indwelling (hulul) and union (ittihad). This guards against misunderstanding.
This shows the Ashari commitment to tanzih (transcendence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دليل آخر :
قال الله عز وجل : ﴿ يَخَافُونَ رَبَّهُم مِّن فَوقِهِمْ ﴾ [النحل:٥٠] وقال تعالى: ﴿ تَعْرُجُ الْمَلَيْكَةُ وَالرُّوحُ إِلَيْهِ ﴾ [المعارج : ٤] وقال تعالى: ﴿ ثُمَّ اسْتَوَى إِلَى السَّمَاء وَهيَ دخان) [فصلت: ۱۱] وقال تعالى: ﴿ثُمَّ اسْتَوَى عَلَى الْعَرْشِ الرَّحْمَنُ فَشَلُ بِهِ خَبِيرًا ) [الفرقان: ٥٩] وقال تعالى: ﴿ ثُمَّ اسْتَوَى عَلَى الْعَرْشِ مَا لَكُم مِّن دُونِهِ مِن وَلِيَ وَلَا شَفِيع ) [السجدة: ٤] فكل ذلك يدل على أنه تعالى في السماء مستو على عرشه، والسماء بإجماع الناس ليست الأرض، فدل على أنه تعالى منفرد بوحدانيته، مستو علـى عرشه استواء منزهاً عن الحلول والاتحاد
Another proof: Allah Almighty said: 'They fear their Lord above them' [al-Nahl: 50]. And He said: 'The angels and the Spirit ascend to Him' [al-Ma'arij: 4]. And He said: 'Then He turned to the heaven while it was smoke' [Fussilat: 11]. And He said: 'Then He established Himself on the Throne, the Most Gracious, so ask about Him the All-Knowing' [al-Furqan: 59]. And He said: 'Then He established Himself on the Throne; you have not besides Him any protector or intercessor' [al-Sajda: 4]. All of that indicates that He, exalted, is in the heaven, established on His Throne, and the heaven, by consensus of people, is not the earth. Thus it indicates that He is unique in His oneness, established on His Throne with an establishment free from indwelling and union.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a cumulative Quranic proof presented by Imam al-Ashari to demonstrate that Allah is above His creation, specifically in the heaven and established on His Throne. He cites five verses: First, angels fear their Lord 'above them' (min fawqihim) indicating a direction of above. Second, angels and the Spirit (Jibril) ascend 'to Him' (ilayhi), implying a destination above. Third, Allah turned to the heaven when it was smoke, showing His action towards the heaven. Fourth and fifth, Allah established Himself on the Throne (istawa 'ala al-arsh). Imam al-Ashari then concludes: all this indicates that Allah is in the heaven, established on His Throne, and the heaven is not the earth by consensus. Therefore, Allah is unique in His oneness and His istiwa is free from indwelling (hulul) and union (ittihad), refuting anthropomorphism and pantheism. The Ashari doctrine affirms the reality of Allah's attributes while negating any similarity to creation.

Key Terms
فوق (fawq)
استوى (istawa)
عرش (arsh)
سماء (sama')
حلول (hulul)
اتحاد (ittihad)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'in the heaven' means Allah is contained within the physical sky.
Correction: The Ashari view is that Allah is above the heaven in a manner befitting His majesty, not spatially confined. The phrase indicates His highness, not location.

Checkpoint
According to the verses cited, what do angels do that indicates Allah is above?
A) They descend from Him.
B) They fear their Lord above them.
C) They are with Him everywhere.
D) They are in the Throne.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Ashari uses five Quranic verses to establish that Allah is above His creation, established on His Throne, without indwelling or union.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You read that the angels fear their Lord above them. Do you have that same awe of Allah's majesty in your daily life, or do you often act as if He is not watching from above? What will you change today to cultivate that fear?
?
Imam al-Ashari concludes that Allah's establishment on the Throne is free from indwelling and union. Yet do you sometimes think of Allah as present in a place or limited by space? How can you train your heart to constantly remember His transcendence?
?
The verses collectively point to Allah's elevated status. When you supplicate, do you genuinely feel you are raising your hands and heart to the Most High, or is it a mechanical action? What step can you take to make your next dua more conscious of His loftiness?

Proofs from Quran and Consensus: Allah's Transcendence
Imam al-Ashari cites verses on Allah's coming and Jesus' raising to heaven.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ashari uses Quranic verses, consensus, and Muslim supplication to establish that Allah is above His creation, not mixed with it.

Core Idea
Quranic verses and Muslim consensus confirm Allah's transcendence above the heavens.

Imam al-Ashari presents a series of proofs from the Quran and from the practice of the Muslim community to affirm that Allah is above His creation, not mixed with it. The verses include the coming of Allah on the Day of Judgment, the Prophet's vision near the Lote Tree, and the raising of Jesus to heaven. These texts are understood literally in a manner befitting Allah, without anthropomorphism.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without interruption, then read the full translation. Notice the sequence of verses and the final dua.
The passage is dense with scriptural references.
2
Identify the three categories of proof
Look for the three main groups: verses about Allah's coming (al-Fajr 22, al-Baqara 210), the Prophet's vision (al-Najm 8-18), and Jesus' raising (Al Imran 55, al-Nisa 157-158).
3
Notice the consensus and dua evidence
Imam al-Ashari then cites the unanimous agreement of the ummah on Jesus' ascension, and the common practice of Muslims calling upon 'O Dweller of the heaven' in supplication.
This shows that the belief in Allah's transcendence is rooted in communal practice.
4
Reflect on the cumulative argument
Consider how these multiple lines of evidence (Quran, consensus, practice) reinforce the Ashari position that Allah is above His creation in a manner befitting His majesty.
The goal is to affirm the literal meanings while negating anthropomorphism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دليل آخر : قال الله تعالى: ﴿ وَجَاءَ رَبُّكَ والمَلَيكُ صَفًّا صَفًّا ﴾ [الفجر: ۲۲] وقال تعالى: ﴿ هَلْ يَنظُرُونَ إِلا أَن يَأْتِيَهُمُ اللَّهُ فِي ظُلَلٍ مِنَ الْغَمَاءِ وَالْمَلَيْكَةُ ﴾ [البقرة: ۲۱۰] وقال : ﴿ ثُمَّ دَنَا فَتَدَلَّى * فَكَانَ قَابَ قَوْسَيْنِ أَوْ أَدْنَى * فَأَوْحَى إِلَى عَبْدِهِ مَا أَوْحَى * مَا كَذَبَ الْفُؤَادُ مَا رَأَى * أَفَتُمَارُونَهُ عَلَى مَا يَرَى * وَلَقَدْ رَآهُ نَزْلَةً أُخْرَى * عِندَ سِدْرَةِ الْمُنتَهَى * عِندَهَا جَنَّةُ الْمَأْوَى * إِذْ يَغْشَى السِّدْرَةَ مَا يَغْشَى * مَا زَاغَ الْبَصَرُ وَمَا طَغَى * لَقَدْ رَأَى مِنْ آيَاتِ رَبِّهِ الْكُبْرَى ﴾ [النجم: ٨-١٨] . وقال عز وجل لعيسى بن مريم عليه السلام ﴿ إِنِّي مُتَوَفِّيكَ وَرَافِعُكَ إِلَيَّ ﴾ [آل عمران: ٥٥] وقال تعالى: ﴿ وَمَا قَتَلُوهُ يَقِينًا * بَل رَّفَعَهُ اللَّهُ إِلَيْهِ ﴾ [النساء: ١٥٧-١٥٨] وأجمعت الأمة على أن الله عز وجل رفع عيسى إلى السماء. ومن دعاء أهل الإسلام جميعاً إذا هم رغبوا إلى الله عز وجل في الأمر النازل بهم يقولون جميعاً: يا ساكن السماء، ومن خلفهم جميعاً: لا والذي احتجب بسبع سماوات.
Another proof: Allah Almighty said: 'And your Lord comes, and the angels, rank upon rank' [al-Fajr: 22]. And He said: 'Do they await but that Allah should come to them in the shadows of clouds and the angels?' [al-Baqara: 210]. And He said: 'Then he approached and descended, and was at a distance of two bow-lengths or nearer. And He revealed to His servant what He revealed. The heart did not lie about what it saw. So do you dispute with him about what he saw? And he certainly saw him in another descent, at the Lote Tree of the Utmost Boundary, near which is the Garden of Refuge, when there covered the Lote Tree that which covered. The sight did not swerve, nor did it transgress. Indeed, he saw of the greatest signs of his Lord' [al-Najm: 8-18]. And He said to Jesus son of Mary, peace be upon him: 'Indeed, I am going to take you and raise you to Myself' [Al Imran: 55]. And He said: 'And they did not kill him, definitely, but Allah raised him to Himself' [al-Nisa: 157-158]. And the ummah unanimously agrees that Allah raised Jesus to the heaven. And from the supplication of all the people of Islam, when they earnestly turn to Allah in a matter that has befallen them, they all say: 'O Dweller of the heaven,' and from behind them all: 'No, by the One who has screened Himself with seven heavens.'
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage presents a series of Quranic proofs and a consensus argument to affirm that Allah is above His creation. The verses include: Allah's coming (maji') on the Day of Judgment, which indicates His power and presence; the Prophet's ascent and seeing the angel Jibril in his true form near the Lote Tree, showing the reality of the heavenly realm; and the explicit raising of Jesus to Allah, confirming that Allah is above the heavens. Imam al-Ashari then adds that the Muslim ummah is unanimous that Jesus was raised to the heaven. He also cites the common practice of Muslims in supplication: they call upon Allah as 'O Dweller of the heaven,' and swear by Allah who has screened Himself with seven heavens, indicating their belief that Allah is above. These cumulative evidences establish that Allah is transcendent, above His creation, without being contained or mixed with it. The Ashari position is to affirm the literal meanings of these texts while negating anthropomorphism.

Key Terms
مجيء (maji')
رفع (raf')
دعاء (du'a)
احتجب (ihtajaba)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'Your Lord comes' implies physical movement or change in location for Allah.
Correction: Ash'ari scholars affirm the verse's literal meaning in a manner befitting Allah, without movement or change, as a manifestation of His sovereignty.

Checkpoint
What additional evidence does Imam al-Ashari provide from Muslim practice?
A) They pray facing the Qibla.
B) They raise their hands in supplication.
C) They say 'O Dweller of the heaven' in supplication.
D) They fast during Ramadan.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Ashari uses multiple Quranic verses, consensus, and Muslim practice to affirm that Allah is above His creation without physical limitation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you raise your hands in du'a, do you truly feel that you are calling upon the 'Dweller of the heaven' who is above all, or are your words just a habit? What would change in your prayer if you genuinely internalized this lesson's truth that Allah is above, yet close?

?
The Prophet saw the greatest signs of his Lord during the mi'raj. Have you ever had a moment where the unseen became so real to you that it changed your priorities? If not, what is holding you back from seeking that certainty through the Quran and sunnah?

Allah Speaks Only from Behind a Veil: The Logic of Specification
Ashar argues from verse wording for distinct divine communication modes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ashari uses the specific wording of a Qur'anic verse to argue that Allah's mode of speech differs between humans and other beings.

Core Idea
The Qur'an distinguishes human communication from divine speech to other beings.

Imam al-Ashari presents a nuanced argument from Qur'an 42:51. He points out that the verse specifies 'human' (bashar), not a general term, which subtly indicates that Allah's communication with angels or jinn may be different. This passage sharpens our understanding of divine transcendence and the unique nature of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then the English translation. Notice the precise wording: 'ليس لبشر' (it is not for any human).
2
Identify the key word: 'bashar'
The verse says 'basar' meaning human, not a general term like 'anyone'. Imam al-Ashari focuses on this specificity.
Why does he insist on this word?
3
Follow the logical deduction
Ashari argues: if the verse were general, it would cause doubt about other beings. By specifying humans, the doubt is removed because it is clear that this rule applies only to humans.
This is a subtle but powerful argument.
4
Reflect on theological implications
Consider how this supports the Ashari view that Allah's speech is an eternal attribute and that He can speak to angels directly, while humans have limited modes.
This relates to divine transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دليل آخر :
وقال الله عز وجل: ﴿ وَمَا كَانَ لِبَشَرٍ أَن يُكَلِّمَهُ اللهُ إِلَّا وَحْياً أَوْ مِن وَرَاءٍ حِجَابٍ أَوْ يُرْسِلَ رَسُولاً فَيُوحِيَ بِإِذْنِهِ مَا يَشَاءُ ﴾ [الشورى: ٥١] وقد خصت الآية البشر دون غيرهم ممن ليس من جنس البشر، ولو كانت الآية عامة للبشر وغيرهم كان أبعد من الشبهة، وإدخال الشك على من يسمع الآية أن يقول: ما كان لأحد أن يكلمه الله إلا وحياً أو من وراء حجاب أو يرسل رسولاً، فيرتفع الشك والحيرة من أن يقول : ما كان لجنس من الأجناس أن أكلمه إلا وحياً أو من وراء حجاب أو أرسل رسولاً ترك أجناساً لم يعمهم بالآية، فدل ما ذكرنا على أنه خص البشر دون غيرهم.
Another proof: And Allah Almighty said: 'And it is not for any human that Allah should speak to him except by revelation or from behind a veil or that He sends a messenger to reveal by His permission what He wills' [al-Shura: 51]. And the verse specifically mentions humans (bashar) to the exclusion of others who are not of the human kind. If the verse were general for humans and others, it would be more removed from doubt but would introduce uncertainty to the listener, who might say: 'No one can be spoken to by Allah except by revelation or from behind a veil or by sending a messenger.' Then the doubt and confusion would be removed by saying: 'No kind of beings can I speak to except by revelation or from behind a veil or by sending a messenger,' leaving out kinds not covered by the verse. Thus what we have mentioned indicates that He specified humans to the exclusion of others.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
In this passage, Imam al-Ashari offers a logical argument based on Quranic wording. The verse states that Allah does not speak to any human (bashar) except in three ways: revelation, behind a veil, or through a messenger. The key point is that the verse specifically says 'human' (bashar), not 'any being' or 'anyone'. Imam al-Ashari argues that if the verse had been general for all beings, it would have been more straightforward but could raise doubt: the listener might ask whether Allah speaks to jinn or angels in the same way. By specifying humans, the verse eliminates that doubt because it explicitly restricts the modes of divine speech to humans. This suggests that other beings (like angels) may be spoken to in a different manner, which is consistent with Islamic teachings. The argument also implicitly supports the Ashari view that Allah's speech is an eternal attribute, and He speaks to angels without the veil and to prophets in specific ways. The verse thus affirms divine transcendence: Allah is not in direct physical contact with humans; His communication is mediated appropriately.

Key Terms
تكليم (taklim)
بشر (bashar)
وحي (wahy)
حجاب (hijab)
رسول (rasul)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the verse implies Allah cannot speak directly to humans at all.
Correction: The Ashari view is that Allah can speak directly, but He chooses these modes to maintain transcendence. The verse does not deny direct speech; it lists ways He does speak to humans.

Checkpoint
Why does Imam al-Ashari emphasize that the verse specifies 'human' (bashar)?
A) To show that angels also hear Allah directly.
B) To eliminate doubt about other kinds of beings.
C) To prove that humans are superior to angels.
D) To indicate that Allah never speaks to humans.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Ashari uses the specific wording of the Qur'an to argue that the modes of divine speech are unique to humans, supporting the Ashari understanding of Allah's transcendence.

?

Proof from Ash-Shura: Divine Speech Specifies Humans
Al-Ash'ari argues that the verse on divine speech specifies humans, not other beings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Ash'ari uses the verse from Surah Ash-Shura to argue that Allah's speech is specifically to humans, and the logical implications of this specification.

Core Idea
The verse specifies 'human' to avoid doubt about who receives direct revelation.

Al-Ash'ari presents another proof from the Quran, drawing on a key verse about the modes of divine communication. He argues that the verse is deliberately restricted to humans, and if it were general, it would create confusion. This lesson unpacks his reasoning and its theological significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation to understand the plain meaning.
Notice the verse from Surah Ash-Shura (42:51) is quoted in full.
2
Identify the key terms and the verse
Locate the word 'bashar' (human) and the three modes of revelation: revelation, behind a veil, or sending a messenger. Notice how Al-Ash'ari focuses on the specification of 'human'.
The key terms are: تكليم الله, وحي, حجاب, رسول, تخصيص.
3
Understand Al-Ash'ari's argument about specification
Al-Ash'ari argues that the verse specifically says 'human' (bashar) to the exclusion of other kinds. He reasons that if it were general (including angels or jinn), it would cause doubt and confusion. The specification removes that doubt.
Think about why a general statement would be more ambiguous.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دليل آخر : وقال الله عز وجل: وَمَا كَانَ لِبَشَرٍ أَن يُكَلِّمَهُ اللَّهُ إِلَّا وَحْيًا أَوْ مِن وَرَاءِ حِجَابٍ أَوْ يُرْسِلَ رَسُولًا فَيُوحِيَ بِإِذْنِهِ مَا يَشَاءُ ) [الشورى: ٥١] وَقَدْ خَصَّتِ الآيَةُ الْبَشَرَ دُونَ غَيْرِهِمْ مِمَّنْ لَيْسَ مِنْ جِنْسِ الْبَشَرِ، وَلَوْ كَانَتِ الآيَةُ عَامَّةً لِلْبَشَرِ وَغَيْرِهِمْ كَانَ أَبْعَدَ مِنَ الشُّبْهَةِ، وَإِدْخَالُ الشَّكِّ عَلَى مَنْ يَسْمَعُ الآيَةَ أَنْ يَقُولَ: مَا كَانَ لِجِنْسٍ مِنَ الْأَجْنَاسِ أَنْ يُكَلِّمَهُ اللَّهُ إِلَّا وَحْيًا أَوْ مِن وَرَاءِ حِجَابٍ أَوْ يُرْسِلَ رَسُولًا فَيَرْتَفِعَ الشَّكُّ وَالْحَيْرَةُ، فَدَلَّ مَا ذَكَرْنَا عَلَى أَنَّهُ خَصَّ الْبَشَرَ دُونَ غَيْرِهِمْ.
Another proof: And Allah, Mighty and Majestic, said: 'And it is not for any human that Allah should speak to him except by revelation or from behind a veil or by sending a messenger to reveal by His permission what He wills.' [Ash-Shura 51]. The verse specified humans to the exclusion of others who are not of the human kind. Had the verse been general to humans and others, it would have been further from ambiguity, and would have introduced doubt in the mind of the hearer, who might say: 'It was not for any kind of being that Allah should speak to it except by revelation or from behind a veil or by sending a messenger.' Then doubt and confusion would have been removed. Thus, what we have mentioned indicates that He specified humans to the exclusion of others.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is another proof focusing on a verse about divine speech. Al-Ash'ari argues that the verse from Surah Ash-Shura (42:51) specifically mentions 'human' (bashar), thereby limiting direct revelation to human beings. He reasons that if the verse were general (including angels or other creatures), it would be less ambiguous, but the fact that it is restricted to humans indicates that other beings are not addressed in this manner. The author emphasizes that the specification removes doubt and confusion, because a general statement would leave open the possibility that other kinds of beings could also be addressed directly. By making it particular to humans, the verse clarifies that only humans receive revelation in these three ways, while other beings (like angels) are not included. This supports the Ash'ari position that Allah's speech is a specific attribute and that He reveals only to humans.

Correction: The verse only specifies the ways in which humans receive revelation; it does not address how other beings might be addressed by Allah.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari uses the specific mention of 'bashar' in the verse to argue that Allah's speech is exclusively to humans, eliminating any ambiguity about other beings.

Allah as Light and the Vision of Him
Al-Ash'ari uses the Light verse and a hadith to argue that Allah can be seen.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Ash'ari uses the verse 'Allah is the Light of the heavens and the earth' and a hadith to argue that Allah can be seen on the Day of Judgment.

Core Idea
If Allah is Light, and light can be seen, then Allah can be seen.

In this passage, Al-Ash'ari presents a proof for the vision of Allah (ru'ya) on the Day of Judgment. He draws on the Qur'anic verse that calls Allah 'Light' and analyzes its possible meanings, concluding that one meaning implies visibility. This argument shows how early Sunni scholars used linguistic and rational reasoning to affirm divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to get the overall argument.
Pay attention to the two meanings of 'nur' mentioned.
2
Identify the two meanings of light
Al-Ash'ari states that light can be either a light by which one is guided or a light that is seen. Note how he uses this disjunction.
3
Understand the conclusion
Since Allah calls Himself Light, and one meaning is 'seen', Al-Ash'ari argues that denying the vision of Allah contradicts the Book and the Prophet.
4
Examine the supporting hadith
The narration from Ibn Abbas warns against reflecting on Allah's essence but mentions immense lights, reinforcing that Allah is above creation and can be seen.
This hadith supports the possibility of vision without speculating on the 'how'.
5
Reflect on the doctrine
Consider why the vision of Allah is an important article of faith in Sunni Islam and how this proof fits with other scriptural evidence.
This lesson establishes a rational argument for ru'ya based on the attribute of light.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دليل آخر : قال الله عز وجل : اللَّهُ نُورُ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ ) [النور:٣٥] فَسَمَّى نَفْسَهُ نُورًا، وَالنُّورُ عِنْدَ الْأُمَّةِ لَا يَخْلُو مِنْ أَنْ يَكُونَ أَحَدَ مَعْنَيَيْنِ إِمَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ نُورًا يُهْتَدَى بِهِ أَوْ نُورًا يُرَى، فَمَنْ زَعَمَ أَنَّ اللَّهَ يُسْمَعُ وَلَا يُرَى فَقَدْ أَخْطَأَ فِي نَفْيِهِ رُؤْيَةَ رَبِّهِ، وَتَكْذِيبِهِ بِكِتَابِهِ، وَقَوْلِ نَبِيِّهِ . وَرَوَتِ الْعُلَمَاءُ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَبَّاسٍ أَنَّهُ قَالَ : تَفَكَّرُوا فِي كُلِّ شَيْءٍ، وَلَا تَفَكَّرُوا فِي ذَاتِ اللَّهِ، فَإِنَّ بَيْنَ السَّمَاءِ السَّابِعَةِ إِلَى كُرْسِيِّهِ سَبْعَةَ آلَافِ نُورٍ، وَهُوَ فَوْقَ ذَلِكَ .
Another proof: Allah, Mighty and Majestic, said: 'Allah is the Light of the heavens and the earth.' [An-Nur 35]. So He called Himself a light. And light, according to the nation (Ummah), can only be either a light by which one is guided or a light that is seen. Thus, whoever claims that Allah is heard and not seen has erred in his denial of seeing his Lord, and in his belittlement of His Book and the statement of His Prophet. And the scholars narrated from 'Abdullah ibn 'Abbas that he said: 'Reflect upon everything, but do not reflect upon the essence of Allah, for between the seventh heaven and His Footstool are seven thousand lights, and He is above that.'
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is a proof that Allah will be seen on the Day of Judgment. Al-Ash'ari uses the verse 'Allah is the Light of the heavens and the earth' (An-Nur 35). He explains that 'light' (nur) can mean either guidance (nuur yuhda bihi) or a visible light (nuur yura). Since Allah is called Light, and one possible meaning is that He is a visible light, it implies that He can be seen. The author then argues that those who deny the vision (ru'ya) of Allah are mistaken, because they contradict the Book and the Sunnah. He supports this with a narration from Ibn 'Abbas that warns against speculating about Allah's essence, but also indicates that Allah is above His creation, which aligns with the possibility of seeing Him. The narration describes immense lights between the seventh heaven and the Footstool, emphasizing Allah's transcendence. Thus, the proof affirms both that Allah is transcendent and that He will be seen by the believers in the afterlife.

Key Terms
نور
رؤية الله
ذات الله
كرسي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Calling Allah 'Light' means He is a physical light or that He is identical to created light.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari does not say Allah is physical light; rather, He has an attribute of light that is real and implies visibility without corporeality.

Checkpoint

A) A light that guides and a light that burns.
B) A light that is seen and a light that is known.
C) A light by which one is guided and a light that is seen.
D) A light of the sun and a light of the moon.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari argues that since Allah is called Light, and light can be seen, it is necessary that Allah can be seen, and denying this contradicts the Qur'an and Sunnah.

Proof from the Verse of Light for Seeing Allah
Al-Ash'ari argues from the verse of light for seeing Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari uses the Quranic verse 'Allah is the light of the heavens and the earth' to demonstrate that Allah can be seen in the afterlife.

Core Idea
Allah calls Himself Light, and light must be seen—so Allah must be visible.

Imam al-Ash'ari presents a scriptural proof for the visibility of Allah based on the Quranic attribute 'Nur'. He argues that the term 'light' necessarily implies visibility, thus those who deny ru'yat Allah contradict the Quran. This lesson unpacks his reasoning and the supporting narration from Ibn 'Abbas.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the structure: verse, analysis, conclusion, and supporting hadith.
2
Examine the key premise about light
Al-Ash'ari asserts that light is either 'seen' or 'sees'. Consider why this is an exhaustive division and how it applies to Allah.
The Arabic uses the same word 'يرى' but context distinguishes the two meanings.
3
Trace the argument to its conclusion
Since Allah is Light, He must be seen. Denying ru'yat Allah thus contradicts the Quran and the Prophet's teaching. Note the supporting narration from Ibn Abbas about lights and transcendence.
The hadith discourages reflection on Allah's essence but implies His greatness and the possibility of vision.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الله عز وجل : اللَّهُ نُورُ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ ﴾ [النور:٣٥] فسمى نفسه نوراً، والنور عند الأمة لا يخلو من أن يكون أحد معنيين إما أن يكون نوراً يرى أو نوراً يرى فمن زعم أن الله يسمع ولا يرى فقد أخطأ في نفيه رؤية ربه، وتكذيبه بكتابه، وقول نبيه . وروت العلماء عن عبد الله بن عباس أنه قال : ( تفكروا في كل شيء، ولا تفكروا في ذات الله ، فإن بين السماء السابعة إلى كرسيه سبعة آلاف نور، وهو فوق ذلك (١) . (۱) رواه أبو نعيم في ( الحلية ) ، والبيهقي في ( الأسماء والصفات ( ص (٤۲۰) من طريق عاصم بن علي: ثنا أبي عن عطاء بن السائب عن سعيد بن جبير عن ابن عباس موقوفاً عليه. وهذا إسناد ضعيف، عطاء كان قد اختلط، وعاصم بن علي و أبوه فيهما ضعف وابنه خير منه. انظر ( الأحاديث الصحيحة رقم (۱۷۸۸). ويغني عنه حديث عبد الله بن سلام مرفوعاً : ( لا تفكروا في الله ، و تفكروا في خلق الله .... وهو حديث حسن في الشواهد
Allah, the Mighty and Majestic, said: 'Allah is the light of the heavens and the earth' [24:35]. So He named Himself Light. And light according to the community (al-ummah) is not free from being one of two meanings: either it is a light that is seen or it is a light that sees. So whoever claims that Allah hears but is not seen has erred in his denial of seeing his Lord, and in his belittling of His Book and the saying of His Prophet. And the scholars have narrated from 'Abdullah ibn 'Abbas that he said: 'Reflect on everything, but do not reflect on the essence of Allah, for between the seventh heaven and His Kursi are seven thousand lights, and He is above that.' (1) (1) Narrated by Abu Nu'aym in al-Hilyah, and al-Bayhaqi in al-Asma' wa al-Sifat, from the path of 'Asim ibn 'Ali: my father narrated from 'Ata' ibn al-Sa'ib from Sa'id ibn Jubayr from Ibn 'Abbas as a mauquf narration. This is a weak chain, for 'Ata' had become confused, and 'Asim ibn 'Ali and his father have weakness, though his son is better than him. See al-Ahadith al-Sahihah no. 1788. And the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn Salam in marfu' form suffices: 'Do not reflect on Allah, but reflect on His creation...' and it is a hasan hadith as a witness.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the visibility of Allah in the afterlife, based on the Quranic verse 'Allah is the light of the heavens and the earth.' The author, al-Ash'ari, begins by citing the verse where Allah calls Himself 'Nur' (Light). He then notes that light, as understood by the Muslim community, necessarily falls into one of two categories: either it is a light that is seen (i.e., visible) or a light that sees (i.e., illuminating). Since Allah is Light, He must be visible—otherwise the name would be meaningless. Therefore, those who claim that Allah hears but cannot be seen (i.e., deny ru'yat Allah) are wrong; they contradict the Quran and the Prophet. The author then supports this with a report from Ibn 'Abbas, who forbids reflecting on Allah's essence but mentions that between the seventh heaven and the Kursi are seven thousand lights, and Allah is above that—implying His transcendence and the possibility of vision. The footnote that follows is an editor's addition, assessing the chain of this report as weak but noting a supporting hadith.

Affirming Allah's Face, Eyes, and Sight
Imam Ash'ari quotes verses affirming Allah's face, eyes, hearing, and sight.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Ash'ari uses Qur'anic verses to affirm divine attributes while rejecting anthropomorphism through the principle of 'without modality and without limitation'.

Core Idea
Allah's attributes are real yet beyond human comprehension.

Imam Ash'ari begins a new chapter on divine attributes by grounding them directly in revelation. He cites clear Qur'anic verses that mention Allah's face, eyes, hearing, and sight, and then immediately adds that these are to be affirmed without asking 'how' or imposing limitations. This approach preserves both the literal meaning of scripture and the transcendence of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the pattern: each attribute is first mentioned in a verse, then affirmed by the Imam.
2
Identify the attributes
List the divine attributes mentioned: face (وجه), eyes (عين), hearing (سمع), sight (بصر). Also note the phrase 'without modality and without limitation' (لا يُكيف ولا يُحد).
This phrase is key to the Ash'ari methodology.
3
Understand the proof method
See how Imam Ash'ari uses the Qur'an as direct evidence. He does not use philosophical reasoning but relies on revealed texts to establish the attributes.
4
Grasp the boundary
Recognize the balance: affirming the attributes as true while denying any similarity to creation. The phrase 'لا يُكيف ولا يُحد' sets the boundary of theological discourse.
This prevents anthropomorphism (tashbih) and nullification (ta'til).
5
Reflect on the lesson
Consider why this approach is important for Sunni theology. It upholds both the literal meaning of the Qur'an and Allah's transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثامن: الكلام في الوجه والعينين والبصر واليدين. قال الله تبارك وتعالى: ﴿ كُلُّ شَيْءٍ هَالِكُ إِلَّا وَجْهَهُ ﴾ [القصص: ۸۸] ، وقال عز وجل: ﴿وَيَبْقَى وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو الْجَلَالِ وَالْإِكْرَامِ ﴾ [الرحمن: ۲۷] ، فأخبر أن له سبحانه وجهاً لا يفنى، ولا يلحقه الهلاك. وقال عز وجل: ﴿تَجْرِي بِأَعْيُنِنَا ﴾ [ القمر : ١٤]، وقال تعالى : ﴿ وَأَصْنَعِ الْفُلْكَ بِأَعْيُنِنَا وَوَحْيِنَا ﴾ [هود: ۳۷]، فأخبر عز وجل أن له وجهاً وعيناً ولا يُكيف ولا يُحد. وقال عز وجل: ﴿وَاصْبِرْ لِحُكْمِ رَبِّكَ فَإِنَّكَ بِأَعْيُنِنَا ﴾ [ الطور : ٤٨]، وقال تعالى: ﴿وَلِتُصْنَعَ عَلَى عَيْنِي ﴾ [طه:۳۹] وقال تعالى: ﴿وَكَانَ اللهُ سَمِيعًا بَصِيرًا ﴾ [النساء: ١٣٤] وقال لموسى وهارون عليهما أفضل الصلاة والسلام: ﴿إِنَّنِي مَعَكُمَا أَسْمَعُ وَأَرَى ﴾ [ طه :٤٦] فأخبر تعالى عن سمعه وبصره ورؤيته.
Chapter Eight: Speech about the Face, the Two Eyes, the Sight, and the Hands. Allah, Blessed and Exalted, said: 'Everything is perishing except His Face' [Al-Qasas: 88], and He, Mighty and Majestic, said: 'And there will remain the Face of your Lord, Possessor of Majesty and Honor' [Ar-Rahman: 27]. So He informed that He, exalted, has a face that does not perish and to which destruction does not come. And He, Mighty and Majestic, said: 'Sailing under Our eyes' [Al-Qamar: 14], and He, Exalted, said: 'And construct the ship under Our eyes and Our revelation' [Hud: 37]. So He, Mighty and Majestic, informed that He has a face and an eye, and it is not to be asked how nor is it to be limited. And He, Mighty and Majestic, said: 'And be patient for the judgment of your Lord, for indeed you are under Our eyes' [At-Tur: 48], and He, Exalted, said: 'And that you be brought up under My eye' [Ta-Ha: 39], and He, Exalted, said: 'And Allah is All-Hearing, All-Seeing' [An-Nisa: 134], and He said to Musa and Harun, upon them be the best blessings and peace: 'Indeed, I am with you, hearing and seeing' [Ta-Ha: 46]. So He, Exalted, informed about His hearing, His sight, and His seeing.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a chapter heading followed by a collection of Qur'anic proof texts. The chapter is titled 'Speech about the Face, the Two Eyes, the Sight, and the Hands.' The author first cites two verses that explicitly mention Allah's face (wajh), concluding that Allah has a face that is eternal and not subject to destruction. Then he cites three verses mentioning 'eyes' (a'yun) or 'eye' (ayn), and comments that Allah has a face and an eye, but these are to be affirmed 'without modality and without delimitation' (لا يُكيف ولا يُحد). Finally, he cites verses on hearing and sight, including the verse from An-Nisa and the direct statement to Musa and Harun, concluding that Allah informed about His hearing, sight, and seeing. The structure is straightforward: each attribute is supported by scriptural evidence, and the author emphasizes that they are to be accepted as they are without philosophical interpretation.

العين
البصر
السمع
لا يُكيف
لا يُحد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Affirming attributes like face and eyes means believing Allah has a physical body like humans.
Correction: Imam Ash'ari explicitly adds 'without modality and without limitation' (لا يُكيف ولا يُحد), meaning these attributes are affirmed but their true nature is unknown and unlike creation.

Checkpoint
What does Imam Ash'ari say about the attributes of face and eye mentioned in the Qur'an?
A) They are metaphorical
B) They are to be affirmed without asking how and without limitation
C) They are only for prophets
D) They are negated by reason

Key Takeaway
Allah's attributes of face, eyes, hearing, and sight are affirmed from the Qur'an without modality or limitation, preserving both revelation and transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that Allah's face remains while everything else perishes, what specific worldly attachment came to your heart? Name it honestly—what is it about that attachment that you find hard to let go of, knowing it will perish?
?
The passage says of Allah's attributes: 'it is not to be asked how nor is it to be limited.' Which attribute of Allah do you find yourself most tempted to imagine or define? What will you do today to replace that imagining with silent acceptance (tafwid)?
?
Allah says to Musa and Harun: 'Indeed, I am with you, hearing and seeing.' Right now, in your current situation, Allah hears every word you speak and sees every action. What one word or action today will you change because you know He hears and sees you?

Quranic Proofs for Allah's Face, Eyes, Hearing, and Sight
Al-Ash'ari cites Quranic verses to prove Allah has a Face, Eyes, Hearing, and Sight.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari uses Quranic verses to affirm that Allah possesses real attributes of Face, Eyes, Hearing, and Sight, without modality or limitation.

Core Idea
Allah's attributes are real, not metaphors – the Quran proves it.

Imam al-Ash'ari opens the eighth chapter of al-Ibanah by presenting direct Quranic evidence for Allah's attributes. He does not argue through reason but lets the divine text speak. This passage establishes that Allah has a Face, Eyes, Hearing, and Sight as real attributes, while affirming that they are beyond human comprehension (لا يُكيف ولا يُحد). Let's examine the verses and the conclusions drawn.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once. Notice the pattern: each verse is followed by a doctrinal conclusion.
Pay attention to the phrase 'لا يُكيف ولا يُحد' – it is key to the Ash'ari approach.
2
Identify the attributes
List the four attributes al-Ash'ari proves: Face, Eyes, Hearing, Sight. For each, note which verses are cited.
The attribute 'Seeing' appears alongside 'Hearing' in the verses.
3
Understand the principle of tafwid
After the Eye verses, al-Ash'ari adds 'without modality or limitation'. This means we affirm the attribute without asking how.
This guards against anthropomorphism (tashbih) and negation (ta'til).
4
Reflect on the method
Contrast this approach with those who interpret these verses metaphorically. Why does al-Ash'ari insist on literal affirmation?
For al-Ash'ari, the Quran's apparent meaning is the true meaning unless reason necessitates otherwise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثامن
الكلام في الوجه والعينين والبصر واليدين
قال الله تبارك وتعالى: ﴿ كُلُّ شَيْءٍ هَالِكُ إِلَّا وَجْهَهُ ﴾ [القصص: ۸۸]، وقال عز وجل: ﴿وَيَبْقَى وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو الْجَلَالِ وَالْإِكْرَامِ ﴾ [الرحمن: ۲۷]، فأخبر أن له سبحانه وجهاً لا يفنى، ولا يلحقه الهلاك
وقال عز وجل: ﴿ تَجْرِي بِأَعْيُنِنَا ﴾ [القمر: ١٤]، وقال تعالى: ﴿ وَأَصْنَعِ الْفُلْكَ بِأَعْيُنِنَا وَوَحْيِنَا ﴾ [هود: ۳۷]، فأخبر عز وجل أن له وجهاً وعيناً ولا يُكيف ولا يُحد. وقال عز وجل: ﴿ وَاصْبِرْ لِحُكْمِ رَبِّكَ فَإِنَّكَ بِأَعْيُنِنَا ﴾ [الطور: ٤٨]، وقال تعالى: ﴿ وَلِتُصْنَعَ عَلَىٰ عَيْنِي ﴾ [طه:۳۹] وقال تعالى: ﴿ وَكَانَ اللَّهُ سَمِيعًا بَصِيرًا ﴾ [النساء: ١٣٤] وقال لموسى وهارون عليهما أفضل الصلاة والسلام: ﴿ إِنَّنِي مَعَكُمَا أَسْمَعُ وَأَرَى ﴾ [طه:٤٦] فأخبر تعالى عن سمعه وبصره ورؤيته
The eighth chapter: Speech concerning the Face, the Eyes, Sight, and the Hands. Allah, Blessed and Exalted, says: "Everything is perishing except His Face" (al-Qasas 88). And He, Mighty and Majestic, says: "And there will remain the Face of your Lord, Owner of Majesty and Honor" (al-Rahman 27). So He informed that He, glorified, has a Face that does not perish and is not overtaken by destruction. And He, Mighty and Majestic, says: "Sailing under Our Eyes" (al-Qamar 14). And He, Exalted, says: "And construct the ark under Our Eyes and Our revelation" (Hud 37). So He, Mighty and Majestic, informed that He has a Face and an Eye, without modality or limitation. And He, Mighty and Majestic, says: "And be patient for the judgment of your Lord, for indeed you are under Our Eyes" (al-Tur 48). And He, Exalted, says: "And that you might be formed under My Eye" (Taha 39). And He, Exalted, says: "And Allah is Hearing, Seeing" (al-Nisa' 134). And He said to Musa and Harun, upon them be the best prayers and peace: "Indeed, I am with you; I hear and I see" (Taha 46). So He, Exalted, informed about His Hearing, His Sight, and His Seeing.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a proof-text compilation. Al-Ash'ari opens Chapter Eight with Quranic verses to affirm that Allah has a Face, Eyes, Hearing, and Sight. He first cites two verses about the Face: one states that everything perishes except Allah's Face, and the other says the Face of the Lord remains. The conclusion: Allah has a Face that does not perish. Then he cites verses about Eyes: the ark sailed under Allah's Eyes, and He said to construct it under His Eyes and revelation. Al-Ash'ari concludes that Allah has a Face and an Eye, but without modality or limitation ( لا يُكيف ولا يُحد ). Next, he cites verses about Hearing and Sight: Allah is Hearing, Seeing; and He said to Musa and Harun, "I hear and I see." The final conclusion: Allah informed about His Hearing, Sight, and Seeing. The passage establishes these attributes from the Quran, rejecting any metaphorical interpretation (ta'wil).

Correction: Al-Ash'ari insists these are real attributes affirmed by the apparent meaning of the Quran, while denying any likeness to creation.

D) ﴿ وَكَانَ اللَّهُ سَمِيعًا بَصِيرًا ﴾

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari grounds divine attributes in Quranic texts, affirming their reality while denying any anthropomorphism or limitation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Al-Ash'ari did not shy away from affirming what the Quran says, even when it seems difficult. Are there attributes of Allah that you are tempted to explain away? Will you accept them now without modality or limitation, as the salaf did?

Affirming Allah's Face: The Correct Response
Al-Ash'ari answers a question affirming Allah's Face with a Quranic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Ash'ari defends the attribute of the Face for Allah using a direct Quranic proof, distinguishing the Sunni position from innovators.

Core Idea
Allah has a Face, as the Quran says, without ta'til or takyif.

In this brief but powerful exchange, Al-Ash'ari confronts a hypothetical questioner who challenges the belief that Allah has a Face. He responds with a clear affirmation, explicitly rejecting the innovators who deny this attribute. The proof is a simple yet decisive Quranic verse, demonstrating that the Sunni approach is to take Allah's attributes literally while avoiding any speculation about modality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the question-answer format.
Notice the opening supplication and then the direct issue.
2
Identify the parties
Who is the questioner? How does Al-Ash'ari characterize the opponents?
The opponents are 'al-mubtadi'un' (innovators).
3
Examine the proof
What evidence does Al-Ash'ari provide for his affirmation? It is a Quranic verse. Reflect on its meaning.
The verse is from Surah al-Rahman, which speaks of the eternal Face of Allah.
4
Understand the theological significance
Why is this issue important? Affirming the Face is part of affirming Allah's attributes without nullification or anthropomorphism.
This aligns with the principle of 'bilâ kayf' (without asking how).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشيخ أبو الحسن علي بن إسماعيل الأشعري رحمه الله ورضي عنه : بالله نستهدي وإياه نستكفي ولا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله العلي العظيم، وهو المستعان أما بعد :
مسألة :
فمن سألنا فقال: أتقولون إن الله سبحانه وجهاً؟
قيل له : نقول ذلك، خلافاً لما يقوله المبتدعون، وقد دل على ذلك قوله عز وجل: ﴿ وَيَبْقَى وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو الْجَلَالِ وَالْإِكْرَامِ ﴾ [الرحمن: ۲۷] .
Shaykh Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Isma'il al-Ash'ari, may Allah have mercy on him and be pleased with him, said: From Allah we seek guidance, and Him we ask for sufficiency, and there is no power or strength except by Allah, the High, the Great. He is the one whose help is sought. To proceed: Issue: If someone asks us: 'Do you say that Allah, glorified, has a Face?' We say to him: 'We say that, contrary to what the innovators say. And that is indicated by the saying of Allah, Mighty and Majestic: "And there will remain the Face of your Lord, Owner of Majesty and Honor" (al-Rahman 27).'
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a short question-answer format. Al-Ash'ari begins with a formula of reliance on Allah and then addresses an issue. A hypothetical questioner asks: 'Do you say that Allah has a Face?' The answer is affirmative: 'We say that, contrary to what the innovators (al-mubtadi'un) say.' The proof is the Quranic verse from Surah al-Rahman: 'And there will remain the Face of your Lord, Owner of Majesty and Honor.' This is a direct refutation of those who deny the attribute of the Face.

وجه
مبتدعون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim that affirming a 'face' for Allah is anthropomorphism.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari affirms the Face while rejecting modality (as per earlier context), so it is not anthropomorphism but literal affirmation without how.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari affirms Allah's Face based on Quranic evidence, rejecting the innovators' denial while avoiding speculative interpretation.

Affirmation of God's Face
Al-Ash'ari affirms God's face via Quranic verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Ash'ari affirms the divine attribute of face for Allah using a Quranic verse, and why this opposes the innovators.

Core Idea
God's face is affirmed by the Quran, without modality.

In this lesson, we encounter Al-Ash'ari's concise affirmation of a key attribute: the face of Allah. He presents a direct question-and-answer format, immediately distancing himself from those who deny this attribute. The proof is a clear Quranic verse from Surah Ar-Rahman.

Guided Path
1
Read the question-and-answer format
Notice that Al-Ash'ari sets up a hypothetical question: 'Do you say that Allah has a face?' The answer is a clear 'Yes.' This format highlights that the issue is debated, and he takes a firm stance.
The phrase 'خلافاً لما يقوله المبتدعون' explicitly contrasts with the innovators.
2
Examine the Quranic proof
Read the verse from Surah Ar-Rahman: 'وَيَبْقَى وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو الجلال والإكرام'. Reflect on how it directly mentions 'وجه' (face) as belonging to Allah. This is the textual evidence.
Al-Ash'ari takes the verse literally, without explaining how, consistent with the principle of bila kayf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة : فمن سألنا فقال: أتقولون إن الله سبحانه وجهاً؟ قيل له : نقول ذلك، خلافاً لما يقوله المبتدعون، وقد دل على ذلك قوله عز وجل: وَيَبْقَى وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو الجلال والإكرام ﴾ [الرحمن: ۲۷] .

Commentary
This passage is a question-and-answer format affirming that God has a face. Al-Ash'ari states that Ahl al-Sunnah affirms God's face, in opposition to the innovators (المبتدعون) who deny it. The proof is the Quranic verse from Surah Ar-Rahman: 'وَيَبْقَى وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو الجلال والإكرام' (And there will remain the Face of your Lord, Owner of Majesty and Honor). The verse explicitly mentions 'وجهه' (His face), so it is taken literally while accepting that it is without modality (as understood from the broader context of Al-Ash'ari's methodology).

Affirmation of God's Hands without Modality
Al-Ash'ari affirms two hands for God via proofs, without how.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Al-Ash'ari affirms the attribute of two hands for Allah based on scriptural evidence while strictly avoiding any modality or anthropomorphism.

Core Idea
Allah has hands — but we ask not how.

Al-Ash'ari addresses a common challenge: how can we speak of God's hands without imagining a body? He answers by citing the Quran and Hadith, affirming the attribute literally but without modality. This lesson unpacks his proof and his repeated emphasis on 'bila kayf.'

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the question-and-answer format at the beginning.
2
Identify the scriptural proofs
The passage cites four Quranic verses and two hadiths. List each one and note why it is relevant to the affirmation of God's hands.
3
Observe the recurring phrase 'bila kayf'
The author explicitly says 'without how' twice. Reflect on why this qualification is crucial — it prevents anthropomorphism while affirming the attribute literally.
4
Consider the last sentence
The final phrase 'وليس يجوز في لسان يَمِينٌ' is somewhat unclear. It seems to argue that the word 'yamin' (right hand) is linguistically permissible for God. Ponder how this supports the overall argument.
This part is marked for review, so treat it as tentative.
5
Connect to the broader principle
Reflect on how this passage exemplifies the broader Sunni approach to divine attributes: affirm what is revealed, without asking how, and without denying the attribute.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة : فإن سئلنا أتقولون إن الله يَدَيْن؟ قيل نقول ذلك بلا كيف وقد دل عليه قوله عز وجل: يَدُ اللهِ فَوْقَ أيديهم ﴾ [الفتح: ١٠] وقوله عز وجل: لِمَا خَلَقْتُ بِيَدَيَّ ) [ ص: ٧٥] . وروي عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال : « خَلَقَ اللهُ آدَمَ بِيَدِهِ ، فَمَسَحَ فَاسْتَخْرَجَ مِنْهُ ذُرِّيَّتَهُ) ، فثبتت أن له يَدَيْن بلا كيف. وجاء في الخبر المأثور عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: ( إن الله تعالى خَلَقَ آدَمَ بِيَدِهِ، وَخَلَقَ جَنَّةَ عَدن بيده ، وكَتَبَ التَّوْرَاةَ بِيَدِهِ، وَغَرَسَ شَجَرَةَ طُوبَى بِيَدِهِ »، وقال عز وجل: بَل يَدَاهُ مَبْسُوطَتَانِ ﴾ [المائدة:٦٤] . وجاء عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: «كلْتَا يَدَيْه ) . وقال عز وجل: لَأَخَذْنَا مِنْهُ بِالْيَمِينِ ﴾ [الحاقة : ٤٥] وليس يجوز في لسان يَمِينٌ .
Question: If we are asked, 'Do you say that Allah has two hands?' It is said: We say that, without how. And it is indicated by the saying of Allah, Mighty and Majestic: 'The hand of Allah is above their hands' [Surah Al-Fath, 10], and His saying: 'For what I created with My two hands' [Surah Sad, 75]. And it is narrated from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he said: 'Allah created Adam with His hand, then He wiped [his back] and extracted from him his progeny.' So it is established that He has two hands without how. And there came in the transmitted report from the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'Indeed Allah, Exalted is He, created Adam with His hand, and created the Garden of Eden with His hand, and wrote the Torah with His hand, and planted the Tree of Tubā with His hand.' And Allah, Mighty and Majestic, said: 'Nay, both His hands are outstretched' [Surah Al-Ma'idah, 64]. And it came from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he said: 'Both of His hands are right [hands].' And Allah, Mighty and Majestic, said: 'We would have seized him by the right hand' [Surah Al-Haqqah, 45]. And it is not permissible in the language [to say?] 'yamin' [right hand?].
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is a question-and-answer that affirms God's hands (yadān) as a real attribute, but without modality (bilā kayf). Al-Ash'ari cites multiple scriptural proofs: 1) Quran 48:10: 'يَدُ اللهِ فَوْقَ أيديهم' (The hand of Allah is above their hands). 2) Quran 38:75: 'لِمَا خَلَقْتُ بِيَدَيَّ' (For what I created with My two hands). 3) A hadith about Adam: 'خلق الله آدم بيده' (Allah created Adam with His hand) then extracted his progeny. From these, it is established that God has two hands, but without asking how. 4) Another hadith listing things created with God's hand: Adam, Garden of Eden, Torah, and the Tree of Tubā. 5) Quran 5:64: 'بَل يَدَاهُ مَبْسُوطَتَانِ' (Nay, both His hands are outstretched). 6) Hadith: 'كلتا يديه يمين' (Both of His hands are right [i.e., fully generous]). 7) Quran 69:45: 'لَأَخَذْنَا مِنْهُ بِالْيَمِينِ' (We would have seized him by the right hand). The passage ends with a phrase that seems to address linguistic permissibility: 'وليس يجوز في لسان يَمِينٌ' which may argue that the word 'yamin' is used in the language and is permissible for God, though the exact meaning is unclear. The central point: these attributes are affirmed literally but without modality, avoiding anthropomorphism.

Key Terms
يد
يدان
بلا كيف
يمين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That affirming God's hands implies a physical, human-like body.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari affirms God's hands literally but insists on 'bila kayf' (without how), which means we affirm the attribute without speculating about its modality, thus avoiding anthropomorphism.

Checkpoint
What phrase does Al-Ash'ari repeatedly use to qualify the affirmation of God's hands?
A) بالتأويل
B) بلا كيف
C) على الحقيقة
D) بالمشاهدة

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari affirms God's hands as a real attribute, supported by multiple scriptures, but insists on accepting it without asking how, thereby preserving transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that Allah created Adam, the Garden, and the Torah 'with His hand,' does your mind automatically try to picture a hand? What does 'without how' force you to do with that impulse?
?
Have you ever felt uncomfortable with the literal affirmation of God's hands, fearing it makes Him too 'human'? How does this lesson's insistence on 'bila kayf' challenge you to submit to revelation over your own reasoning?
?
The proof from Quran 5:64 says 'both His hands are outstretched'—connecting the attribute to generosity. In what area of your life are you doubting that Allah's hand is open toward you? What would change if you truly believed that His hands are real and generous?
