Affirmation of Allah's Two Hands Without Modality
Imam Ashari affirms Allah's two hands using Quran and hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Ashari affirms the attribute of two hands for Allah using scriptural proof texts without falling into anthropomorphism.

Core Idea
Allah's hands are affirmed by Quran and hadith — without asking how.

This lesson presents Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari's approach to the divine attribute of hands (yadayn). He begins with a clear statement of the Ahl al-Sunnah position: affirmation without modality. Then he marshals multiple Quranic verses and prophetic hadith that explicitly mention Allah's hand or hands. The goal is to establish the attribute textually while avoiding any corporeal interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the main claim
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice that the author starts with a rhetorical question and gives a direct answer: we affirm two hands without modality.
The phrase 'bila kayf' is key.
2
Understand 'bila kayf'
Reflect on the term 'bila kayf' (without modality). It means we affirm the attribute without asking how, avoiding both literal anthropomorphism and metaphorical denial.
This is the hallmark of the Salaf approach.
3
List the Quranic verses cited
Identify each verse: al-Fath 10, Sad 75, al-Ma'ida 64, al-Haqqa 45. Note what each contributes to the proof.
Some verses mention 'hand' singular, others 'two hands'.
4
Examine the hadith proofs
Find the hadith about Adam's creation, the Garden of Eden, the Torah, and the tree of Tubā, plus the saying 'both of His hands are right.' See how they reinforce the attribute.
These hadith are from authentic sources.
5
Reflect on the author's method
Consider that Imam Ashari does not resort to metaphorical interpretation (ta'wil). He simply cites texts and says 'bila kayf'. This is the method of Ahl al-Sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن سئلنا أتقولون إن الله يَدَيْن؟ قيل نقول ذلك بلا كيف وقد دل عليه قوله عز وجل: يَدُ اللهِ فَوْقَ أَيْدِيهِمْ [الفتح: ١٠] وقوله عز وجل: لِمَا خَلَقْتُ بِيَدَيَّ [ص: ٧٥]. وروي عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: «خَلَقَ اللهُ آدَمَ بِيَدِهِ، فَمَسَحَ فَاسْتَخْرَجَ مِنْهُ ذُرِّيَّتَهُ»، فثبتت أن له يَدَيْن بلا كيف. وجاء في الخبر المأثور عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: «إن الله تعالى خَلَقَ آدَمَ بِيَدِهِ، وَخَلَقَ جَنَّةَ عَدْنٍ بِيَدِهِ، وَكَتَبَ التَّوْرَاةَ بِيَدِهِ، وَغَرَسَ شَجَرَةَ طُوبَى بِيَدِهِ»، وقال عز وجل: بَلْ يَدَاهُ مَبْسُوطَتَانِ [المائدة:٦٤]. وجاء عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: «كِلْتَا يَدَيْهِ يَمِينٌ». وقال عز وجل: لَأَخَذْنَا مِنْهُ بِالْيَمِينِ [الحاقة:٤٥].
If we are asked: Do you say that Allah has two hands? We say: We say that without modality, and that is indicated by His saying, Mighty and Majestic: "The hand of Allah is above their hands" [al-Fath:10] and His saying: "for what I created with My two hands" [Sad:75]. And it is narrated from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he said: "Allah created Adam with His hand, then He wiped and brought forth from him his offspring." So it is established that He has two hands without modality. And it came in the transmitted report from the Prophet, peace be upon him: "Indeed Allah the Exalted created Adam with His hand, and created the Garden of Eden with His hand, and wrote the Torah with His hand, and planted the tree of Tubā with His hand." And He said, Mighty and Majestic: "Nay, both His hands are outstretched" [al-Ma'ida:64]. And it came from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he said: "Both of His hands are right [hands]." And He said, Mighty and Majestic: "We would have seized him by the right hand" [al-Haqqa:45].
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is a proof-text accumulation affirming the attribute of two hands (yadayn) for Allah without modality (bila kayf). The author begins with a rhetorical question and answer, presenting the stance of Ahl al-Sunnah: affirmation without asking how. He then adduces multiple Quranic verses and prophetic hadith. The first verse from al-Fath indicates a single hand, but combined with others it confirms two hands. The second verse from Sad explicitly says 'bi-yadayya' (with My two hands). The hadith about Adam is a well-known proof. Additional reports about creating Paradise, writing the Torah, and planting the tree of Tubā reinforce the two-handedness, as does the verse 'both His hands are outstretched' and the hadith 'both of His hands are right hands.' The verse from al-Haqqa mentioning 'by the right hand' is also cited. The key point is that these texts are taken literally without asking how; the author does not resort to metaphorical interpretation. The phrase 'bila kayf' guards against anthropomorphism while preserving the attribute.

Key Terms
يدين (yadayn)
بلا كيف (bila kayf)
يد الله (yad Allah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Affirming that Allah has hands means He has physical limbs like humans.
Correction: The author affirms hands without modality (bila kayf), meaning we accept the attribute without asking how, thus avoiding anthropomorphism.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Ashari, what is the correct stance regarding Allah's two hands?
A) They are to be affirmed without modality.
B) They are metaphorical for power.
C) They are to be negated.
D) They are literal but we must explain how.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Ash'ari affirms Allah's two hands through multiple texts, insisting on affirmation without modality to preserve transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the verses 'with My two hands' and 'both His hands are outstretched,' does your heart accept them literally, or does your mind try to explain them away? What is preventing you from full acceptance?
?
Imagine you are asked by a friend: 'How can Allah have hands?' Would you reply 'I do not know how, but I affirm it'? If your answer would be different, why does your soul shy away from simple submission to the text?
?
Is there any part of your life where you resist submitting to clear textual truths because they seem intellectually uncomfortable? How does this lesson's 'bila kayf' challenge your need to fully understand before you believe?

Why 'Yad' Cannot Mean 'Blessing': A Linguistic Refutation
Imam Ashari refutes the ta'wil of yad as ni'mah using Arabic usage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Ashari's linguistic argument that the Quranic expression 'bi-yadayya' (with My two hands) cannot be interpreted as 'by My blessing' based on Arabic usage and the impossibility of proving otherwise.

Core Idea
Arabic usage does not allow 'bi-yadayya' to mean 'by My blessing'.

When theologians claim that 'yad' in the Quran means 'blessing,' they rely on a supposed linguistic meaning. Imam Ashari challenges this by examining actual Arabic usage. He forces them to choose: either rely on language or consensus—and both fail. This lesson walks through his decisive refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the structure: first the linguistic rule, then its application to the Quran, then the dilemma for opponents.
2
Identify the key claim
Highlight the sentence where Ashari states that Arabic speakers do not use 'bi-yadayya' to mean 'by my blessing'. This is the core of the refutation.
The claim is about a specific construction, not the word 'yad' in isolation.
3
Understand the dilemma
Ashari presents two possible proofs for the opponent: language or consensus. See why both are impossible. Then reflect on the rhetorical challenge: ask for a third way.
This shows Ashari's method of refutation by exhausting possibilities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس يجوز في لسان العرب ولا في عادة أهل الخطاب أن يقول القائل: عملت كذا بِيَدَيَّ، ويعني به النعمة، وإذا كان الله عز وجل إنما خاطب العرب بلغتها وما يجري مفهوماً في كلامها ومعقولاً في خطابها، وكان لا يجوز في لسان أهل البيان أن يقول القائل: فعلتُ بِيَدَيَّ، ويعني النعمة، فبطل أن يكون معنى قوله عز وجل: بِيَدَيَّ النعمة. وذلك أنه لا يجوز أن يقول القائل: لي عليه يد بمعنى: لي عليه نعمة، ومن دافعنا عن استعمال اللغة ولم يرجع إلى أهل اللسان فيها دفع عن أن تكون اليد النعمة، إذ كان لا يمكنه أن يتعلق في أن اليد النعمة إلا من جهة اللغة فإذا دفع اللغة لزمه أن لا يفسر القرآن من جهتها، وأن لا يثبت اليد نعمة من قبلها؛ لأنه إن رجع في تفسير قوله عز وجل يدي نعمتي إلى الإجماع، فليس المسلمون على ما ادعى متفقين، وإن رجع إلى اللغة فليس في اللغة أن يقول القائل: بيدي – يعني نعمتي – وإن لجأ إلى وجه ثالث سألناه عنه، ولن يجد له سبيلاً.
And it is not permissible in the language of the Arabs nor in the customary usage of speakers that one says: 'I did such-and-such with my two hands' meaning thereby 'blessing.' And since Allah the Exalted addressed the Arabs in their language and what is understood in their speech and comprehended in their discourse, and it was not permissible in the speech of eloquent people that one says: 'I did with my two hands' meaning 'blessing,' then it is invalid that the meaning of His saying 'bi-yadayya' be 'blessing.' That is because it is not permissible that one says: 'I have a hand over him' meaning 'I have a blessing over him.' And whoever argues with us about the usage of the language and does not refer to the people of the language in it, he repudiates that 'hand' be 'blessing,' because it is not possible for him to affirm that 'hand' means 'blessing' except through language. So if he repudiates language, it necessarily follows that he should not interpret the Quran from it, and that he should not affirm 'hand' as 'blessing' from it. Because if he relies in interpreting His saying 'yadi' as 'my blessing' on consensus, then the Muslims are not agreed on what he claims. And if he relies on language, then it is not in the language that one says 'bi-yadayya' meaning 'my blessing.' And if he resorts to a third way, we ask him about it, and he will find no way to it.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is a linguistic refutation of the metaphorical interpretation that 'yad' in the Quran means 'ni'mah' (blessing). The author argues that Arabic usage does not allow the expression 'bi-yadayya' (with my two hands) to mean 'by my blessing.' He points out that since the Quran is in Arabic, the interpretation must be consistent with Arabic speech. The argument then examines the evidential basis of the opponents: either consensus or language. Both are untenable. There is no consensus among Muslims that 'yad' means 'ni'mah' in these verses, and the language does not support it. The author challenges them to produce a third proof, which they cannot.

Key Terms
يد (yad)
نعمة (ni'mah)
لسان العرب (lisan al-ʿArab)
إجماع (ijmaʿ)
بيان (bayan)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Ashari denies that the word 'yad' ever means 'blessing' in Arabic.
Correction: In fact, Ashari's argument is specific to the construction 'bi-yadayya' (with my two hands) and the expression 'yad' used for 'blessing' in other contexts might be acceptable, but not in the Quranic verses in question.

Checkpoint
What is the main linguistic argument against interpreting 'bi-yadayya' as 'ni'mah'?
A) The word 'yad' never means blessing in Arabic.
B) The construction 'bi-yadayya' cannot mean 'by my blessing' in Arabic usage.
C) There is a consensus that it means hand.
D) The Quran says so.

Key Takeaway
Imam Ashari demonstrates that the interpretation of 'yad' as 'ni'mah' in the Quranic verses is linguistically unsupported and the opponents have no valid proof from language or consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Quran, do you trust that its words carry the meanings that Allah intended, or do you sometimes find yourself imposing your own interpretations to avoid what seems difficult? This lesson shows that Imam Ashari refused to twist the meaning of 'hand' despite the theological discomfort. Are you willing to accept the apparent meaning of Allah's attributes, even when your intellect struggles?
?
Imam Ashari challenges the opponent to produce a third way, knowing they cannot. Is there an area in your own faith where you rely on shaky reasoning or 'third ways' to avoid submitting to the plain truth of revelation? What is that area, and what would it cost you to surrender it?
?
The argument here rests on the integrity of the Arabic language. If you are not an Arabic speaker, how seriously do you take learning the language of revelation? Do you depend on translations and scholars' opinions alone, or do you strive to encounter Allah's words as they were revealed? What step will you take this week to connect more directly with the Quran in Arabic?

Challenging Ta'wil: Consensus or Language?
Imam Ashari challenges innovators to prove their ta'wil by consensus or language.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Ashari demands consensus or linguistic evidence for interpreting divine attributes and why analogy is insufficient.

Core Idea
Divine attribute interpretation must be based on consensus or Arabic language, not personal reasoning.

Imam Ashari directly challenges the innovators who reinterpret 'bi-yadayya' as meaning 'my blessing'. He asks them to provide either consensus or linguistic proof for their claim. When they might resort to analogy, he refutes that by emphasizing that the Quran is a clear Arabic text whose meanings are fixed by language, not human reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the interrogative tone and the structure of the argument.
The passage is a direct challenge to the innovators.
2
Identify the two sources demanded
The author asks if their claim is based on consensus (إجماع) or language (لغة). Highlight these terms.
These are the only acceptable bases for interpretation in this context.
3
Understand the refutation of analogy
Read the verses cited (Ibrahim 4, al-Nahl 103, al-Zukhruf 3, Muhammad 24). See how they prove that the Quran is Arabic and must be understood through language, not analogy.
The verses emphasize the Arabic nature of the Quran and the command to ponder it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقال لأهل البدع ولم زعمتم أن معنى قوله: بِيَدَيَّ نعمتي، أزعمتم ذلك إجماعاً أو لغة؟ فلا يجدون ذلك إجماعاً ولا في اللغة. وإن قالوا: قلنا ذلك من القياس. قيل لهم: ومن أين وجدتم في القياس أن قوله تعالى: بِيَدَيَّ لا يكون معناه إلا نعمتي؟ ومن أين يمكن أن يعلم بالعقل أن تفسير كذا وكذا، مع أنا رأينا الله عز وجل قد قال في كتابه العزيز الناطق على لسان نبيه الصادق: وَمَا أَرْسَلْنَا مِنْ رَسُولٍ إِلَّا بِلِسَانِ قَوْمِهِ [إبراهيم: ٤] وقال: لِسَانُ الَّذِي يُلْحِدُونَ إِلَيْهِ أَعْجَمِيٌّ وَهَذَا لِسَانٌ عَرَبِيٌّ مُبِينٌ [النحل: ١٠٣] وقال تعالى: إِنَّا جَعَلْنَاهُ قُرْآنًا عَرَبِيًّا [الزخرف: ٣] وقال تعالى: أَفَلَا يَتَدَبَّرُونَ الْقُرْآنَ [محمد: ٢٤].
And it is said to the people of innovation: Why do you claim that the meaning of His saying 'bi-yadayya' is 'my blessing'? Do you claim that by consensus or by language? They will not find that by consensus nor in the language. And if they say: We said that by analogy. It is said to them: From where did you find in analogy that His saying 'bi-yadayya' cannot mean anything but 'my blessing'? And how can it be known by reason that the interpretation is such-and-such, seeing that we see that Allah the Exalted has said in His noble Book, speaking on the tongue of His truthful Prophet: 'And We did not send any messenger except with the language of his people' [Ibrahim:4] and He said: 'The language of those they incline to is foreign, and this is a clear Arabic language' [al-Nahl:103] and He said: 'Indeed We have made it an Arabic Quran' [al-Zukhruf:3] and He said: 'Do they not then ponder the Quran?' [Muhammad:24].
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is a direct interrogation of the opponents (ahl al-bid'a) demanding justification for their ta'wil. The author asks whether their claim is based on consensus or linguistic evidence, and then shows neither supports them. When they might fall back on qiyas (analogical reasoning), he refutes that as well, because the meanings of Quranic words are not determined by reason but by the Arabic language as revealed. The verses quoted emphasize that the Quran is in clear Arabic and its interpretation must come from understanding that language, not from abstract reasoning. The implication is that the innovators have no valid basis for their interpretation.

Key Terms
أهل البدع (ahl al-bidʿa)
قياس (qiyas)
لسان (lisan)
إجماع (ijmaʿ)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One can use analogical reasoning (qiyas) to reinterpret divine attributes like 'yaday' as meaning 'blessing'.
Correction: The author argues that analogy is not a valid source for interpreting Quranic words because meanings are fixed by the Arabic language and consensus, not by human reasoning.

Checkpoint
What two possible sources of evidence does Imam Ashari ask the innovators to provide for their interpretation?
A) Consensus and language.
B) Reason and revelation.
C) Analogy and tradition.
D) Philosophy and mysticism.

Key Takeaway
Imam Ashari establishes that interpretation of divine attributes must be grounded in either consensus or the Arabic language, not in subjective analogy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a difficult verse about Allah's attributes, do you first turn to what scholars have agreed upon and what the Arabic language indicates, or do you rush to interpret it based on your own reasoning? Be honest: where does your mind instinctively go? Write a concrete action you will take next time to base your understanding on solid foundations.
?
Imam Ashari challenges the innovators to prove their interpretation by consensus or language. In your own life, when you make claims about Allah or His religion, are you careful to base them on these same solid foundations, or do you sometimes rely on 'it seems logical to me'? What would change if you held yourself to the same standard? Commit to investigating one belief you hold and verifying its source.
?
The Quran is in clear Arabic and we are commanded to ponder it. But if we bypass the language and use analogy to fit the text to our expectations, are we truly pondering the Quran, or are we making it say what we want? What is one attribute of Allah that you have been tempted to reinterpret to make it more 'comfortable' for you? How does this lesson challenge that tendency? Will you accept the apparent meaning or still try to rationalize it?

The Linguistic Argument: 'Yad' Cannot Mean Grace
Refuting the linguistic plausibility of interpreting 'yad' as 'ni'mah'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why interpreting 'yad' in 'bi-yadayya' as 'grace' contradicts Arabic linguistic custom and why rejecting language undermines Quranic interpretation.

Core Idea
Arabic usage never allows 'yad' to mean grace in this context.

Imam al-Ash'ari begins his refutation by grounding the interpretation in the language of the Arabs. Since the Quran was revealed in Arabic, its meanings must conform to how Arabs actually speak. This lesson examines the linguistic principle that invalidates the sectarian claim and the logical consequence of abandoning language.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how the author establishes the custom of the Arabs and then applies it to the verse.
Pay attention to the phrase 'لا يجوز' (it is not permissible).
2
Identify the custom
The author claims that in Arabic custom, one does not say 'I did with my two hands' to mean grace. Understand that this is a linguistic observation.
This is not a theological claim but a factual one about language.
3
Understand the consequence
The author argues that if someone rejects this linguistic usage, they cannot then use language to interpret the Quran. This is a logical trap for the opponent.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider the broader principle: the Quran's meanings are tied to Arabic. Rejecting Arabic custom leads to inability to interpret the Quran at all.
This sets up the next lesson's examination of alternative bases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العرب ولا في عادة أهل الخطاب أن يقول القائل: عملت كذا ( بِيَدَيَّ )، ويعني به النعمة، وإذا كان الله عز وجل إنما خاطب العرب بلغتها وما يجري مفهوماً في كلامها ومعقولاً في خطابها، وكان لا يجوز في لسان أهل البيان أن يقول القائل: فعلتُ بِيَدَيَّ، ويعني النعمة، فبطل أن يكون معنى قوله عز وجل : ( بِيَدَيَّ ) النعمة . وذلك أنه لا يجوز أن يقول القائل : لي عليه يد بمعنى: لي عليه نعمة، ومن دافعنا عن استعمال اللغة ولم يرجع إلى أهل اللسان فيها دفع عن أن تكون اليد النعمة، إذ كان لا يمكنه أن يتعلق في أن اليد النعمة إلا من جهة اللغة فإذا دفع اللغة لزمه أن لا يفسر القرآن من جهتها، وأن لا يثبت اليد نعمة من قبلها ؛ لأنه إن رجع في تفسير قوله عز وجل يدي نعمتي إلى الإجماع، فليس المسلمون على ما ادعى متفقين وإن رجع إلى اللغة فليس في اللغة أن يقول القائل : بيدي – يعني نعمتي – وإن لجأ إلى وجه ثالث سألناه عنه، ولن يجد له سبيلاً . سؤال : ويقال لأهل البدع ولم زعمتم أن معنى قوله : ( بِيَدَيَّ ) نعمتي، أزعمتم ذلك إجماعاً أو لغة؟ فلا يجدون ذلك إجماعاً ولا في اللغة . وإن قالوا : قلنا ذلك من القياس قيل لهم: ومن أين وجدتم في القياس أن قوله تعالى: (بِيَدَيَّ ) لا يكون معناه إلا نعمتي؟ ومن أين يمكن أن يعلم بالعقل أن تفسير كذا وكذا، مع أنا رأينا الله عز وجل قد قال في كتابه العزيز الناطق على لسان نبيه الصادق : وَمَا اَرْسَلْنَا مِن رَّسُولٍ إِلَّا بِلِسَانِ قَوْمِهِ ﴾ [إبراهيم: ٤] وقال: ﴿لِسَانُ الَّذِي يُلْحِدُونَ إِلَيْهِ أَعْجَمِيٌّ وَهَذَا لِسَانُ عَرَبِيٌّ مُّبِينٌ ﴾ [النحل: ١٠٣] وقال تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّا جَعَلْتَهُ قُرْءَانَا عَرَبِيًّا ﴾ [الزخرف : ٣] وقال تعالى: ﴿ أَفَلَا يَتَدَبَّرُونَ الْقُرْءَانَ ﴾ [محمد : ٢٤] . ولو كان القرآن بلسان غير العرب لما أمكن أن نتدبره، ولا أن نعرف معانيه إذا سمعناه، فلما كان من لا يحسن لسان العرب لا يحسنه وإنما يعرفه العرب إذا سمعوه، علم أنهم علموه ؛ لأنه بلسانهم نزل وليس في لسانهم ما ادعوه .
And it is not in the custom of the Arabs nor in the practice of the people of address that a speaker says: 'I did such-and-such with My two hands' and means by it grace. And since Allah, mighty and majestic, only addressed the Arabs in their language and what is understood in their speech and comprehended in their address, and it is not permissible in the tongue of the eloquent that a speaker says 'I did with My two hands' and means grace, it is invalidated that the meaning of His statement (bi-yadayya) is grace. And that because it is not permissible for a speaker to say: 'I have a hand over him' meaning 'I have grace over him.' And whoever argues with us about the use of language and does not refer to the people of the tongue concerning it, argues against that the hand (yad) is grace, since he cannot rely on that the hand is grace except from the aspect of language. So if he refutes language, it necessitates that he does not interpret the Quran from its aspect, and that he does not affirm the hand as grace from that direction. Because if he refers in interpreting His statement 'yadi' as 'ni'mati' to consensus, the Muslims are not as he claims agreed. And if he refers to language, it is not in the language that a speaker says 'bi-yadayya' meaning 'my grace'. And if he resorts to a third way, we ask him about it, and he will not find a way. Question: And it is said to the people of innovation: Why do you claim that the meaning of His statement (bi-yadayya) is 'my grace'? Do you claim that by consensus or by language? They will not find that by consensus nor in language. And if they say: We said that by analogy, it is said to them: From where did you find in analogy that His statement (bi-yadayya) has no meaning except 'my grace'? And from where can it be known by reason that such-and-such interpretation? While we see that Allah, mighty and majestic, has said in His noble Book speaking on the tongue of His truthful Prophet: 'And We sent no messenger except with the language of his people' (Ibrahim 4) and said: 'The language of those they incline to is foreign, and this is a clear Arabic tongue' (an-Nahl 103) and said: 'Indeed, We have made it an Arabic Quran' (az-Zukhruf 3) and said: 'Then do they not ponder the Quran?' (Muhammad 24). And if the Quran were in the language of other than Arabs, it would not be possible for us to ponder it, nor to know its meanings when we hear it. So when one who does not know the language of the Arabs does not know it, and only the Arabs know it when they hear it, it is known that they know it because it was revealed in their language, and in their language there is not what they claim.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage refutes the interpretation that 'yad' in 'bi-yadayya' (with My two hands) means 'ni'mah' (grace/benefit). The author gives a linguistic argument: in Arabic custom, it is not said 'I did with My two hands' to mean grace. He then questions the opponents: on what basis do they claim this meaning—consensus or language? He shows neither supports them. Consensus is not established, and language does not permit it. If they claim analogy, he replies that reason cannot determine scriptural interpretation without language. He then cites Quranic verses affirming that the Quran is in Arabic, so the interpretation must follow Arabic usage. The passage concludes that since the Quran was revealed in Arabic and the Arabs do not use 'yad' for grace in this context, the interpretation is invalid.

Key Terms
يد (yad)
نعمة (ni'mah)
لغة (language)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'yad' in Arabic can idiomatically mean 'grace' in the context of 'bi-yadayya'.
Correction: Arabic custom does not permit this usage; one does not say 'I did with my two hands' to mean grace.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the primary reason that 'bi-yadayya' cannot mean 'my grace'?
A) Because all Muslims agree it is not grace.
B) Because the Arabic language does not allow that usage.
C) Because reason dictates otherwise.
D) Because the verse is unclear.

Key Takeaway
The interpretation of Quranic words must conform to Arabic linguistic custom; 'yad' cannot mean 'grace' because Arabs do not use it that way.

Refuting the Three Bases: Consensus, Language, and Analogy
Examining and rejecting the three potential bases for the allegorical interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari refutes the three potential foundations (consensus, language, analogy) for interpreting 'yad' as grace, and how Quranic verses confirm the Arabic nature of the Quran.

Core Idea
Neither consensus, language, nor analogy support the allegorical interpretation of 'yad'.

Having established the linguistic custom, Imam al-Ash'ari now challenges the proponents to show their basis. He systematically examines and rejects consensus, language, and analogy as grounds for their claim, and concludes with Quranic evidence that the Quran is Arabic, thereby closing any possible support for their interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the rhetorical structure: a question followed by refutation of each possible basis.
The author uses a question-and-answer format.
2
Identify the three bases
The author considers three ways the opponents might justify their interpretation: consensus (ijma'), language (lugha), and analogy (qiyas).
These are standard sources of Islamic law and theology.
3
Examine each refutation
For consensus: the Muslims are not agreed. For language: Arabic does not permit it. For analogy: reason cannot determine interpretation without language. Note how each is dismissed.
4
Relate the Quranic verses
The author cites four verses showing the Quran is in Arabic. Connect this to the argument: since it is Arabic, interpretation must follow Arabic usage, which does not support their claim.
The verses reinforce the earlier linguistic argument.
5
Conclude the lesson
Understand that the opponents are left without any valid basis. The only consistent method is to take the apparent meaning of 'yad' as a real hand, not metaphorical.
This is the wider theological point of the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العرب ولا في عادة أهل الخطاب أن يقول القائل: عملت كذا ( بِيَدَيَّ )، ويعني به النعمة، وإذا كان الله عز وجل إنما خاطب العرب بلغتها وما يجري مفهوماً في كلامها ومعقولاً في خطابها، وكان لا يجوز في لسان أهل البيان أن يقول القائل: فعلتُ بِيَدَيَّ، ويعني النعمة، فبطل أن يكون معنى قوله عز وجل : ( بِيَدَيَّ ) النعمة . وذلك أنه لا يجوز أن يقول القائل : لي عليه يد بمعنى: لي عليه نعمة، ومن دافعنا عن استعمال اللغة ولم يرجع إلى أهل اللسان فيها دفع عن أن تكون اليد النعمة، إذ كان لا يمكنه أن يتعلق في أن اليد النعمة إلا من جهة اللغة فإذا دفع اللغة لزمه أن لا يفسر القرآن من جهتها، وأن لا يثبت اليد نعمة من قبلها ؛ لأنه إن رجع في تفسير قوله عز وجل يدي نعمتي إلى الإجماع، فليس المسلمون على ما ادعى متفقين وإن رجع إلى اللغة فليس في اللغة أن يقول القائل : بيدي – يعني نعمتي – وإن لجأ إلى وجه ثالث سألناه عنه، ولن يجد له سبيلاً . سؤال : ويقال لأهل البدع ولم زعمتم أن معنى قوله : ( بِيَدَيَّ ) نعمتي، أزعمتم ذلك إجماعاً أو لغة؟ فلا يجدون ذلك إجماعاً ولا في اللغة . وإن قالوا : قلنا ذلك من القياس قيل لهم: ومن أين وجدتم في القياس أن قوله تعالى: (بِيَدَيَّ ) لا يكون معناه إلا نعمتي؟ ومن أين يمكن أن يعلم بالعقل أن تفسير كذا وكذا، مع أنا رأينا الله عز وجل قد قال في كتابه العزيز الناطق على لسان نبيه الصادق : وَمَا اَرْسَلْنَا مِن رَّسُولٍ إِلَّا بِلِسَانِ قَوْمِهِ ﴾ [إبراهيم: ٤] وقال: ﴿لِسَانُ الَّذِي يُلْحِدُونَ إِلَيْهِ أَعْجَمِيٌّ وَهَذَا لِسَانُ عَرَبِيٌّ مُّبِينٌ ﴾ [النحل: ١٠٣] وقال تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّا جَعَلْتَهُ قُرْءَانَا عَرَبِيًّا ﴾ [الزخرف : ٣] وقال تعالى: ﴿ أَفَلَا يَتَدَبَّرُونَ الْقُرْءَانَ ﴾ [محمد : ٢٤] . ولو كان القرآن بلسان غير العرب لما أمكن أن نتدبره، ولا أن نعرف معانيه إذا سمعناه، فلما كان من لا يحسن لسان العرب لا يحسنه وإنما يعرفه العرب إذا سمعوه، علم أنهم علموه ؛ لأنه بلسانهم نزل وليس في لسانهم ما ادعوه .

Misconception: That there is consensus among Muslims that 'yad' in 'bi-yadayya' means grace.
Correction: The author states that the Muslims are not agreed on this interpretation.

No valid basis—consensus, language, or analogy—supports interpreting 'yad' as grace, and the Quran's Arabic nature confirms this.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read a verse like 'bi-yadayya', do you find yourself tempted to rationalize it with your own mind rather than accepting it as Allah's true speech? What does this lesson reveal about the danger of relying on your own reasoning over the clear language of the Quran? Commit to memorizing one of the Arabic verses cited here so that you can guard your heart against such doubts.
?
The author argues that the Quran is in Arabic so that we can ponder it. When was the last time you pondered a Quranic verse in its original Arabic, trusting that its literal meaning is the truth? If you have never done so, what is stopping you from starting today? Make a plan to learn the meaning of just one verse this week.
?
You have heard that some people interpret 'yad' as 'grace'—did you ever wonder why? This lesson exposes that such interpretations have no basis in consensus, language, or logic. How does this challenge you to be more cautious about accepting allegorical interpretations you hear? Are there any beliefs you hold about Allah's attributes that you have not verified from the Quran and the understanding of the early Muslims? Resolve to examine one such belief this week.

Refuting 'Yad' as Power: Three Arguments
Refuting the claim that 'yad' means power with three arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three key arguments refuting the interpretation that 'yad' in 'bi-yadayya' means power, based on linguistics, theology, and context.

Core Idea
The meaning of Allah's 'two hands' cannot be reduced to 'power' because language, theology, and scripture all refute it.

In this passage, Imam al-Ash'ari refutes the Mu'tazilite claim that the 'two hands' of Allah mentioned in the Qur'an refer to His power. He provides three decisive arguments: a linguistic point about the word 'aydin', a theological inconsistency in the opponent's own position, and a contextual argument from the story of Adam and Iblis. Let's examine each one.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the source text carefully. Notice the three objections introduced by 'أيضاً' and 'وأيضاً'.
2
Understand the linguistic argument
Analyse the claim that 'aydin' is not the plural of 'yad' in the relevant sense. How does this invalidate the interpretation?
The key is the difference between 'aydin' and 'ayadi'.
3
Understand the theological argument
Consider why affirming two powers contradicts Mu'tazilite theology, which denies even one eternal attribute of power.
This is an internal inconsistency argument.
4
Understand the contextual argument
Reflect on the story of Adam and Iblis. Why does the distinction between their creations necessitate a literal interpretation of 'two hands'?
If 'yad' meant power, Iblis could claim the same honour.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد اعتل معتل بقول الله عز وجل : ( وَالسَّماءَ بنيتها بأييدي) [الذاريات : ٤٧] قالوا الأيدي القوة، فوجب أن يكون معنى قوله : بيَدَيَّ ) بقدرتي . قيل لهم : هذا التأويل فاسد من وجوه أحدها أن الأيدي ليس بجمع لليد ; لأن جمع يد التي هي نعمة أيادي وإنما قال تعالى: لِمَا خَلَقْتُ بِيَدَيَّ ) فبطل بذلك أن يكون معنى قوله : (بِيَدَيَّ ) معنى قوله : (بنيتها بأيد). وأيضاً فلو كان أراد القوة لكان معنى ذلك بقدرتي، وهذا ناقض لقول مخالفنا ، وكاسر المذهبهم ; لأنهم لا يثبتون قدرة واحدة، فكيف يثبتون قدرتين. وأيضاً فلو كان الله تعالى عنى بقوله : لِمَا خَلَقْتُ بِيَدَيَّ ) القدرة لم يكن لآدم عليه السلام على إبليس مزية في ذلك، والله تعالى أراد أن يرى فضل آدم عليه السلام عليه إذ خلقه بيديه دونه، ولو كان خالقاً لإبليس بيده كما خلق آدم عليه السلام بيديه لم يكن لتفضيله عليه بذلك وجه، وكان إبليس يقول محتجاً على ربه فقد خلقتني بيديك كما خلقت آدم عليه السلام بهما، فلما أراد الله تعالى تفضيله عليه بذلك قال له موبخاً على استكباره على آدم أن يسجد له: ﴿ مَا مَنَعَكَ أَن تَسْجُدَ لِمَا خَلَقْتُ بِيَدَى اسْتَكْبَرتَ [ ص: ٧٥] دل على أنه ليس معنى الآية القدرة إذا كان الله عــز وجـــل خـلـق الأشياء جميعاً بقدرته، وإنما أراد إثبات يدين، ولم يشارك إبليس آدم عليه السلام
And an objector argued with the statement of Allah, mighty and majestic: 'And the heaven We built it with hands (aydin)' (adh-Dhariyat 47). They said: 'al-aydin' means power, so it necessitates that the meaning of His statement 'bi-yadayya' is 'by My power'. It is said to them: This interpretation is invalid from several aspects. One of them is that 'al-aydin' is not the plural of 'yad'; because the plural of 'yad' which is grace is 'ayadi'. And He, exalted, only said: 'lima khalaqtu bi-yadayya' (for what I created with My two hands). So it is invalidated by that that the meaning of His statement (bi-yadayya) is the meaning of His statement (banaytuha bi-aydin). And also, if He meant power, then the meaning would be 'by My power', and this contradicts our opponent's statement and breaks their school; because they do not affirm one power, so how can they affirm two powers? And also, if Allah, exalted, meant by His statement 'lima khalaqtu bi-yadayya' power, then Adam, peace be upon him, would have no superiority over Iblis in that, and Allah intended to show Adam's virtue over him by creating him with His two hands without him. And if He had created Iblis with His hand as He created Adam with His hands, there would be no basis for preferring him over him in that, and Iblis would have argued against his Lord: 'You created me with Your two hands as You created Adam with them.' So when Allah intended to prefer him over him by that, He said to him, rebuking his arrogance over Adam to prostrate to him: 'What prevented you from prostrating to what I created with My two hands? Are you arrogant?' (Sad 75). This indicates that the meaning of the verse is not power, since Allah, mighty and majestic, created all things by His power, but He intended to affirm two hands, and He did not make Iblis share with Adam in that.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage refutes the interpretation that 'yad' in 'bi-yadayya' means 'quwwah' (power), based on the verse 'banaytuha bi-aydin' (I built it with power). The author gives three objections. First, linguistic: 'aydin' is not the plural of 'yad' (hand); the plural of 'yad' when meaning grace is 'ayadi', so the verse does not support them. Second, theological: if it meant power, it would imply two powers (dual form), but the opponents (Mu'tazila) deny that God has any attribute of power, so affirming two powers is even more problematic for them. Third, contextual: the verse about Adam's creation distinguishes him from Iblis; if 'yad' meant power, then Iblis was also created by God's power, removing the distinction. Therefore, the interpretation is invalid.

Key Terms
أيد (aydin)
قوة (quwwah)
قدرة (qudrah)
يدان (two hands)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some argue that 'yad' in 'bi-yadayya' means power based on the verse 'banaytuha bi-aydin'.
Correction: Linguistic analysis shows 'aydin' is not the plural of 'yad' in the sense of a hand, and the theological and contextual arguments further invalidate this interpretation.

Checkpoint
What is one of the reasons the author gives to refute interpreting 'yad' as power?
A) The plural 'aydin' matches the plural of 'yad' meaning grace, not limb.
B) The opponents affirm two powers, which is consistent with the verse.
C) Adam's creation was also by God's power like Iblis, so no distinction.
D) The verse about Adam shows no distinction between him and Iblis.

Key Takeaway
The interpretation of 'yad' as power is invalid based on linguistic plurality, theological inconsistency, and the unique honor of Adam's creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that Allah created Adam with His two hands, does your heart feel the honor and nearness, or do you file it as a theological fact? Where in your life do you treat Allah's attributes as abstract doctrines rather than realities that demand your humility and gratitude?
?
If reinterpreting Allah's attributes to fit human comfort can lead to stripping them of their intended meaning — as the Mu'tazilites did with 'yad' — then what attributes of Allah have you subtly reshaped to avoid their weight? How does that affect your worship and your sense of accountability to Him?
?
You are a descendant of Adam, who was honored by being created by Allah's own hands. Does that lineage of divine honor move you to live in a way that reflects your noble origin? Or have you forgotten that your very existence carries a trace of that direct act — and what does that demand of you today?

Linguistic Refutation: The Plural of 'Yad' is Not 'Aydin'
Ash'ari's first linguistic argument against the Mu'tazili interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ash'ari argues that the word 'aydin' in the Qur'an cannot be the plural of 'yad' meaning hand, and how this refutes the Mu'tazili interpretation of 'bi-yadayya' as power.

Core Idea
The wrong plural breaks the analogy.

The Mu'tazila try to interpret 'bi-yadayya' as 'by My power' by citing the verse about building the heaven 'bi-aydin', claiming 'aydin' means power. But Ash'ari first attacks the linguistic basis: the word 'aydin' is not the correct plural of 'yad' (hand) when it refers to an attribute of Allah. This lesson examines that opening refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage where Ash'ari presents the first aspect of his refutation. Notice how he quotes the opponent's argument first.
2
Understand the linguistic point
Ash'ari argues that 'aydin' is not the plural of 'yad' meaning hand; rather, the plural for that meaning is 'ayādin'. Thus the analogy fails.
See that he distinguishes between the plural of 'yad' as a blessing and the plural used in the heaven verse.
3
See the conclusion
He concludes that the meaning of 'bi-yadayya' cannot be equated with the meaning of 'banaytu bi-aydin'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد اعتل معتل بقول الله عز وجل: (وَالسَّمَاءَ بَنَيْنَا بِأَيْيدٍ) [الذاريات: ٤٧] قالوا الأيدي القوة، فوجب أن يكون معنى قوله: (بِيَدَيَّ) بقدرتي. قيل لهم: هذا التأويل فاسد من وجوه أحدها أن الأيدي ليس بجمع لليد؛ لأن جمع يد التي هي نعمة أيادي، وإنما قال تعالى: (لِمَا خَلَقْتُ بِيَدَيَّ) فبطل بذلك أن يكون معنى قوله: (بِيَدَيَّ) معنى قوله: (بَنَيْتُ بِأَيْيدٍ). وأيضاً فلو كان أراد القوة لكان معنى ذلك بقدرتي، وهذا ناقض لقول مخالفنا وكاسر لمذهبهم؛ لأنهم لا يثبتون قدرة واحدة، فكيف يثبتون قدرتين. وأيضاً فلو كان الله تعالى عنى بقوله: (لِمَا خَلَقْتُ بِيَدَيَّ) القدرة لم يكن لآدم عليه السلام على إبليس مزية في ذلك، والله تعالى أراد أن يرى فضل آدم عليه السلام عليه إذ خلقه بيديه دونه، ولو كان خالقاً لإبليس بيده كما خلق آدم عليه السلام بيديه لم يكن لتفضيله عليه بذلك وجه، وكان إبليس يقول محتجاً على ربه: فقد خلقتني بيديك كما خلقت آدم عليه السلام بهما، فلما أراد الله تعالى تفضيله عليه بذلك قال له موبخاً على استكباره على آدم أن يسجد له: ﴿ مَا مَنَعَكَ أَن تَسْجُدَ لِمَا خَلَقْتُ بِيَدَىَّ اسْتَكْبَرْتَ ﴾ [ص: ٧٥] دل على أنه ليس معنى الآية القدرة إذا كان الله عز وجل خلق الأشياء جميعاً بقدرته، وإنما أراد إثبات يدين، ولم يشارك إبليس آدم عليه السلام في أن خلق بهما.
And someone has argued using the saying of Allah Almighty: 'And the heaven We built with hands (aydin)' [51:47]. They said: 'al-aydi' means power, so it must be that the meaning of His saying: 'bi-yadayya' (with My two hands) is 'by My power.' It was said to them: This interpretation is invalid from several aspects: One of them is that 'al-aydi' is not a plural of 'yad' (hand); for the plural of 'yad' which is a blessing is 'ayādī', and Allah Almighty said: 'for what I created with My two hands (bi-yadayya)'. So it is invalid by that that the meaning of His saying 'bi-yadayya' is the meaning of His saying 'built with hands (aydin)'. Also, if He intended power, that would mean 'by My power', and this contradicts the statement of our opponent and breaks their doctrine; for they do not affirm a single power, so how can they affirm two powers? Also, if Allah Almighty intended by His saying 'for what I created with My two hands' (the meaning of) power, there would be no superiority for Adam, peace be upon him, over Iblis in that, and Allah Almighty intended to show the virtue of Adam, peace be upon him, over him, as He created him with His two hands without him (Iblis). And if He were the creator of Iblis with His hand as He created Adam, peace be upon him, with His two hands, there would be no aspect of preferring him over him by that, and Iblis would say, arguing against his Lord: 'You have created me with Your two hands as You created Adam, peace be upon him, with them.' So when Allah Almighty intended to prefer him over him by that, He said to him, rebuking him for his arrogance over Adam to prostrate to him: 'What prevented you from prostrating to what I created with My two hands? Are you arrogant?' [38:75]. This indicates that the meaning of the verse is not power, since Allah Almighty created all things by His power, but rather He intended to affirm two hands, and Iblis did not share with Adam, peace be upon him, in that he was created with them.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is a refutation (radd) of the Mu'tazili interpretation that the phrase 'bi-yadayya' (with My two hands) in the Qur'an means 'by My power' (qudra). The author begins by citing the opponents' argument: they analogize from the verse 'wa-al-samā'a banaynā bi-aydin' (and the heaven We built with hands/strength), claiming that 'aydin' means power/qudra, and thus 'bi-yadayya' in other verses must also mean 'by My power'. Ash'ari then refutes this with three points. First, he argues that 'aydin' is not the plural of 'yad' meaning hand; rather, the plural of 'yad' in the sense of 'hand' is 'ayādin' when it means blessing, but here it is a different word. Moreover, the verse in question is 'limā khalaqtu bi-yadayya' (for what I created with My two hands), not 'banaytu bi-aydin', so the analogy fails. Second, if the intended meaning were power, then 'bi-yadayya' would imply two powers—but the Mu'tazila do not affirm even a single power for Allah in the sense of an eternal attribute, so they cannot affirm two. This exposes an internal inconsistency in their position. Third, and most importantly, if the verse merely meant 'by My power', then Adam would have no distinction over Iblis, since Allah created all things by His power. But the Qur'an specifically rebukes Iblis for refusing to prostrate to what Allah created with His two hands, showing that a special honor is intended. Iblis could have argued that he too was created by two hands, but the rebuke indicates that he was not. Therefore, the verse necessarily affirms the reality of two hands (yadayn) as an attribute of Allah, not mere power. The author concludes that the intended meaning is to affirm two hands, and Iblis did not share with Adam in being created with them.

Key Terms
يد (yad)
أيدي (aydin)
أيادي (ayādi)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'aydin' in the Qur'an is the plural of 'yad' (hand) and thus can be used to interpret 'bi-yadayya' as power.
Correction: Ash'ari clarifies that the plural of 'yad' for an attribute is 'ayādin', and 'aydin' in the heaven verse is a different word meaning strength or power. So the analogy is invalid.

Checkpoint
What is the first reason Ash'ari gives to refute the interpretation of 'bi-yadayya' as power?
A) The Mu'tazila do not affirm any power attribute.
B) The word 'aydin' is not the plural of 'yad' meaning hand.
C) Adam would have no superiority over Iblis.
D) The verse about heaven is not about creation.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazili interpretation fails linguistically because 'aydin' is not the correct plural of 'yad' for the attribute of hand.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that Allah created with 'two hands', does something in you resist? Are you willing to submit to that literal meaning even if it troubles your mind?
?
Why are you so quick to adopt interpretations that soften or dismiss Allah's attributes? Is it because you fear what others might think, or because you trust your own logic more than His words?
?
If you encountered someone who denied the meaning of Allah's hands out of a desire to protect His transcendence, would you have the courage to correct them with the same precision Ash'ari used here? What would stop you?

Theological Refutation: Two Powers Contradict Mu'tazilism
Ash'ari's second argument: internal inconsistency of the Mu'tazili position.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second argument: that interpreting 'bi-yadayya' as power would imply two powers, which contradicts the Mu'tazilite denial of even one eternal power attribute.

Core Idea
They can't even accept one power, so two is impossible.

Ash'ari's second refutation targets the internal consistency of the Mu'tazili position. Even if the linguistic issue were resolved, interpreting 'bi-yadayya' as 'by My power' would lead to the conclusion that Allah has two powers. But the Mu'tazila deny that Allah has any power as an eternal attribute distinct from His essence. This contradiction exposes the weakness of their interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic portion where Ash'ari presents the second aspect. Notice the logical flow: if 'bi-yadayya' means power, that would be two powers, but they reject even one.
2
Understand the contradiction
Ash'ari points out that the Mu'tazila do not affirm a single power attribute for Allah, so they cannot logically affirm two. This shows their interpretation is self-defeating.
They would have to accept two powers, which is absurd to them.
3
Appreciate the rhetorical force
This argument uses the opponents' own principles to refute them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?

?
The Mu'tazila wanted to protect Allah's transcendence, but their interpretation trapped them in self-contradiction. Are you willing to accept that your best intentions can still lead to error if they are not grounded in the revealed text? What step will you take to ensure your understanding is aligned with the Salaf?

The Superiority of Adam: Special Creation with Two Hands
Ash'ari's third argument: the special honor of Adam requires literal hands.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third argument: that the verse about Adam's creation with two hands gives him special honor over Iblis, which would be meaningless if it only meant power.

Core Idea
Adam's honor proves the hands are real, not just power.

Ash'ari's strongest argument is from the context of the verse in Surah Sad. Allah rebukes Iblis for refusing to prostrate to Adam, specifically mentioning that He created Adam with His two hands. If 'bi-yadayya' meant merely 'by My power', then Iblis, who was also created by Allah's power, could claim equal honor. But the rebuke shows that Adam has a distinction, so the hands must be a special attribute unique to Adam's creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage where Ash'ari explains that if 'bi-yadayya' meant power, Iblis could argue he was created with the same power, so no distinction.
2
Understand the implication
Ash'ari argues that the Qur'anic rebuke of Iblis would be undermined if the creation of Adam was only through power, since Iblis is also a creature of power.
3
See the conclusion
Therefore, the verse must affirm two hands as a real attribute, and Iblis was not created with them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The author begins by citing the opponents' argument: they analogize from the verse 'wa-al-samā'a banaynā bi-aydin' (and the heaven We built with hands/strength), claiming that 'aydin' means power/qudra, and thus 'bi-yadayya' in other verses must also mean 'by My power'. Ash'ari then refutes this with three points. First, he argues that 'aydin' is not the plural of 'yad' meaning hand; rather, the plural of 'yad' in the sense of 'hand' is 'ayādin' when it means blessing, but here it is a different word. Moreover, the verse in question is 'limā khalaqtu bi-yadayya' (for what I created with My two hands), not 'banaytu bi-aydin', so the analogy fails. Second, if the intended meaning were power, then 'bi-yadayya' would imply two powers—but the Mu'tazila do not affirm even a single power for Allah in the sense of an eternal attribute, so they cannot affirm two. This exposes an internal inconsistency in their position. Third, and most importantly, if the verse merely meant 'by My power', then Adam would have no distinction over Iblis, since Allah created all things by His power. But the Qur'an specifically rebukes Iblis for refusing to prostrate to what Allah created with His two hands, showing that a special honor is intended. Iblis could have argued that he too was created by two hands, but the rebuke indicates that he was not. Therefore, the verse necessarily affirms the reality of two hands (yadayn) as an attribute of Allah, not mere power. The author concludes that the intended meaning is to affirm two hands, and Iblis did not share with Adam in being created with them.

Key Terms
يد (yad)
استكبرت (istakbarta)
سجود (sujud)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the phrase 'bi-yadayya' in the Adam verse can be interpreted as power without losing the distinction.
Correction: Ash'ari shows that if it meant power, Iblis could argue he was also created by power, eliminating Adam's special honor. Hence, it must be a distinct attribute.

Checkpoint
What would Iblis be able to argue if 'bi-yadayya' meant power, according to Ash'ari?
A) That he was created before Adam.
B) That he was also created by Allah's two hands.
C) That he was created by power just like Adam.
D) That Adam was not created by Allah.

Key Takeaway
The special honor of Adam in creation proves that 'bi-yadayya' refers to a real attribute of two hands, not merely power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider the story of Adam and Iblis, do you ever find yourself feeling superior to others because of a perceived unique favor from God? In what specific relationship or situation have you acted like Iblis, refusing to acknowledge God's special gift to someone else? What would genuine humility require you to do today?
?
Ash'ari warns that reinterpreting 'hands' as power could allow Iblis to argue against God. In your own spiritual life, when you reinterpret difficult verses to fit your comfort, do you ever find yourself subtly arguing with God? Identify one verse you have explained away to avoid its demand on your life. What would it mean to submit to its literal weight?
?
Adam was created directly by God's hands. Do you live as if your existence is a deliberate, personal act of God, or as if you are a product of random forces? How would your daily worship and gratitude change if you truly believed you were crafted by God's hands? What one practice can you adopt this week to remind yourself of this truth?

Classification of Possible Meanings of Allah's Hands
Ash'ari classifies four possible meanings of 'bi-yadayya' and affirms the fourth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Ash'ari uses logical division (taqsīm) to affirm the divine attribute of hands while rejecting anthropomorphic and metaphorical interpretations.

Core Idea
Allah's hands are affirmed as a real attribute, unlike any created thing.

Imam Ash'ari presents a precise logical classification of the possible meanings of the phrase 'bi-yadayya' (with My two hands) from the Quran. By systematically eliminating interpretations that imply creation-likeness or pure metaphor, he demonstrates the correct Islamic position: affirming the attribute without specifying its modality. This passage is a masterclass in the Ash'ari method of dealing with ambiguous divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice how Ash'ari uses the word 'taqsīm' (division) to structure his argument.
2
Identify the four possible meanings
The passage lists four interpretations: two blessings, two limbs, two powers, and two hands unlike any of these. Locate each one and see how they are introduced.
3
Understand why the first three are rejected
Ash'ari rejects the first meaning because it violates linguistic usage, and the third because it contradicts both his own and his opponents' positions. The second (limbs) is implicitly rejected by context. Ask why each is invalid.
The rejection of the second meaning (limbs) is not explicitly argued here but is understood from the overall context of tanzih (transcendence).
4
Grasp the affirmation of the fourth meaning
After invalidating the first three, Ash'ari affirms the fourth: two hands that are not like created hands. Note that this is not a mere negation but a positive affirmation of a real attribute whose reality is known only to Allah.
This is the classic Ash'ari position of 'tafwīd' (consigning the modality to Allah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس يخلو قوله عز وجل: (لِمَا خَلَقْتُ بِيَدَيَّ) أن يكون معنى ذلك: إثبات يدين نعمتين، أو يكون معنى ذلك إثبات يدين جارحتين، أو يكون معنى ذلك إثبات يدين قدرتين، أو يكون معنى ذلك إثبات يدين ليستا نعمتين ولا جارحتين ولا قدرتين ولا يوصفان إلا كما وصف الله عز وجل، فلا يجوز أن يكون معنى ذلك نعمتين؛ لأنه لا يجوز عند أهل اللسان أن يقول القائل: عملت بيدي وهو يعني نعمتي، ولا يجوز عندنا ولا عند خصومنا أن يعني قدرتين، وإذا فسدت الأقسام الثلاثة صح القسم الرابع؛ وهو أن معنى قوله: (بِيَدَيَّ) إثبات يدين ليستا جارحتين ولا قدرتين ولا نعمتين لا يوصفان إلا بأن يقال: إنهما يدان ليستا كالأيدي خارجتان عن سائر الوجوه الثلاثة التي سلفت.
And it is not free that His saying, the Mighty and Majestic: 'for what I created with My two hands (bi-yadayya)' is that its meaning is: affirmation of two hands as blessings (ni'matayn), or that its meaning is affirmation of two hands as limbs (jārihatayn), or that its meaning is affirmation of two hands as powers (qudratayn), or that its meaning is affirmation of two hands that are not blessings nor limbs nor powers, and they are not described except as Allah the Mighty and Majestic described them. It is not permissible that its meaning be two blessings, because it is not permissible according to the people of language for someone to say: 'I worked with my two hands' while meaning 'my two blessings.' And it is not permissible according to us nor according to our opponents that it means two powers. And when the three divisions are invalidated, the fourth division is correct; which is that the meaning of His saying 'bi-yadayya' is affirmation of two hands that are not limbs nor powers nor blessings, not described except by saying: they are two hands unlike [other] hands, exempt from all the three aspects that preceded.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is a logical classification (taqsīm) of the possible meanings of the phrase 'bi-yadayya' (with My two hands). The author enumerates four possible interpretations: 1) two hands meaning two blessings (ni'matayn), 2) two hands meaning two limbs (jārihatayn), 3) two hands meaning two powers (qudratayn), and 4) two hands that are none of the above but affirmed as Allah describes. The author then rules out the first three: The first (blessings) is rejected because it is linguistically improper—no speaker of Arabic would say 'I worked with my two hands' meaning 'my two blessings'. The second (limbs) is implicitly rejected because it implies anthropomorphism (tashbīh), though the argument here relies on the third being rejected as well. The third (powers) is rejected because neither the author (Ash'ari) nor his opponents (the Mu'tazila) affirm two distinct powers; the Mu'tazila do not affirm any eternal attribute of power, and Ash'ari affirms one power. Therefore, only the fourth division remains valid: the affirmation of two hands that are not like created hands, not limbs, not powers, not blessings, but described solely as Allah described them. The author emphasizes that these hands are 'outside the three aspects that preceded'—meaning they are unique and incomparable. This is a classic Ash'ari method of affirming divine attributes by negating false interpretations without attempting to explain modality (ta'wīl).

Key Terms
يد (yad)
نعمة (ni'mah)
جارحة (jārihah)
قدرة (qudrah)
تقسيم (taqsīm)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the fourth position is a mere negation or that it implies hands like human hands.
Correction: The fourth position is a positive affirmation of a real attribute that is unlike any created thing; its modality is unknown, but its reality is affirmed.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the first possible meaning (two hands as blessings) rejected?
A) Because it contradicts the Quran.
B) Because it is linguistically improper according to the people of language.
C) Because it implies anthropomorphism.
D) Because the Mu'tazila do not accept it.

Key Takeaway
Imam Ash'ari affirms the divine attribute of hands as a real, unique attribute unlike any created thing, by eliminating false interpretations through logical division.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that Allah has two hands unlike anything you can imagine, do you feel a sense of awe or a desire to reduce it to something your mind can grasp? What does your reaction reveal about your submission to Allah's words?
?
Are you willing to affirm attributes of Allah that seem strange to your intellect, even if they make you uncomfortable? What would it cost you to simply say 'I believe' without trying to explain how?
?
If you were to explain this lesson to someone who denies the divine attributes, would you rely on rational argument or on the sheer authority of revelation? Which approach shows more trust in Allah's description of Himself?

Refuting False Interpretations of Allah's Two Hands
Imam Ashari refutes three false interpretations of 'بيدي' and affirms the correct one.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Ashari's method of taqsim (logical division) to affirm the correct meaning of Allah's two hands as real but non-corporeal attributes.

Core Idea
Allah's hands are affirmed as real, but not as limbs, blessings, or powers.

Imam Ashari uses a powerful logical tool—taqsim—to refute three false interpretations of Allah's statement 'لِمَا خَلَقْتُ بِيَدَىَ'. By systematically eliminating impossible meanings, he isolates the only valid one: two hands that are truly Allah's but unlike any created thing. This passage demonstrates the classical Ash'ari methodology of affirming divine attributes without ta'til or tashbih.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice how Ashari lists four possible meanings before eliminating three.
The passage is a logical argument, not just a statement.
2
Understand the four categories
Identify the four meanings: blessings (نعمتين), limbs (جارحتين), powers (قدرتين), and the fourth which is none of these. Understand why the first three are invalid according to Ashari.
The refutation of 'blessings' uses a linguistic argument.
3
See the logical elimination
Recognize that after ruling out three meanings, the fourth remains by necessity. This is a classic taqsim argument.
The fourth meaning is not defined positively; it is affirmed only as what Allah described.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس يخلو قوله عز وجل : لِمَا خَلَقْتُ بِيَدَىَ أن يكون معنى ذلك : إثبات يدين نعمتين، أو يكون معنى ذلك إثبات يدين جارحتين، أو يكون معنى ذلك إثبات يدين قدرتين، أو يكون معنى ذلك إثبات يدين ليستا نعمتين ولا جارحتين ولا قدرتين ولا يوصفان إلا كما وصف الله عز وجل، فلا يجوز أن يكون معنى ذلك نعمتين؛ لأنه لا يجوز عند أهل اللسان أن يقول القائل : عملت بيدي وهو يعني نعمتي، ولا يجوز عندنا ولا عند خصومنا أن يعني قدرتين وإذا فسدت الأقسام الثلاثة صح القسم الرابع ؛ وهو أن معنى قوله : بيدي إثبات يدين ليستا جارحتين ولا قدرتين ولا نعمتين لا يوصفان إلا بأن يقال : إنهما يدان ليستا كالأيدي خارجتان عن سائر الوجوه الثلاثة التي سلفت.
And the saying of Allah Almighty: 'لِمَا خَلَقْتُ بِيَدَىَ' is not free from that its meaning is: affirmation of two hands as two blessings, or affirmation of two hands as two limbs, or affirmation of two hands as two powers, or affirmation of two hands that are neither two blessings nor two limbs nor two powers and are not described except as Allah Almighty described them. So it is not permissible that its meaning be two blessings; because it is not permissible according to the people of language that a person says: 'I did it with my hands' while meaning my two blessings. And it is not permissible according to us nor according to our opponents that it means two powers. And when the three divisions are invalidated, the fourth division is correct; and it is that the meaning of His saying 'بيدي' is affirmation of two hands that are not limbs nor powers nor blessings, not described except by saying: they are two hands not like hands, outside all the three aspects that have preceded.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of false interpretations of Allah's statement 'لِمَا خَلَقْتُ بِيَدَىَ' (what I created with My two hands). Imam Ashari begins by enumerating four possible meanings: two hands as blessings, as limbs, as powers, or as something else not any of these. He then eliminates the first three. The meaning of blessings is invalid because Arabic speakers never say 'I did it with my hands' intending 'my two blessings'. The meaning of powers is invalid because neither Ash'aris nor their opponents accept that. Since three possibilities are false, the fourth is correct: two hands that are not limbs, not blessings, not powers, described only as Allah described — hands that are unlike any created hands. The author systematically uses a logical division (taqsim) to isolate the orthodox meaning.

Key Terms
يد
نعمة
جارحة
قدرة
تقسيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'يد' must mean either a physical limb or a metaphorical blessing, ignoring the Ash'ari position of real but non-corporeal hands.
Correction: Imam Ashari shows that there is a fourth possibility: hands that are real attributes of Allah but not limbs, blessings, or powers. They are affirmed as He described, without ta'til or tashbih.

Checkpoint

B) Two blessings, two favors, two limbs, or two powers
C) Two hands, two forearms, two arms, or two powers
D) Two blessings, two limbs, two attributes, or two actions

Key Takeaway
The correct understanding of Allah's two hands is that they are affirmed as real attributes, but not as limbs, blessings, or powers; they are unlike any created thing.

Refuting the 'Blessings' Interpretation of 'بيدي'
Imam Ashari argues that interpreting 'بيدي' as blessings negates Adam's distinction over Iblis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Ashari argues that interpreting 'بيدي' as 'two blessings' would negate Adam's special honor over Iblis, based on the Quranic context.

Core Idea
Interpreting 'بيدي' as blessings makes Adam and Iblis equal in honor.

Imam Ashari presents a logical argument from the Quranic story of Adam and Iblis to refute the Mu'tazilite interpretation of the divine attribute 'yad'. By examining the consequences of interpreting 'بيدي' as blessings, he shows that this interpretation contradicts the clear purpose of the verse: to show Adam's unique distinction.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context
Recall the Quranic verse (Saad 38:75) where Allah says to Iblis: 'What prevented you from prostrating to what I created with My two hands?' (بِيَدَيَّ). The verse implies Adam's special honor.
The Mu'tazila interpreted 'yaday' metaphorically as blessings, denying the literal meaning.
2
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then the English translation. Notice the logical flow: if 'بيدي' means blessings, then Adam has no virtue over Iblis.
3
Follow the argument: two possibilities
Imam Ashari analyzes two possible meanings for 'blessings': either the body of Adam or accidents in the body. In both cases, Iblis received the same kind according to Mu'tazilite doctrine.
Bodies are one genus; accidents are similar in kind.
4
Conclude the refutation
Since the verse was meant to show Adam's superiority, but the blessings interpretation leads to equality, that interpretation must be false. 'بيدي' must mean something else (the literal hands of Allah).
This is a proof by contradiction from the context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا فلو كان معنى قوله عز وجل : بِيَدَيَّ ) نعمتي لكان لا فضيلة لآدم عليه السلام على إبليس في ذلك على مذهب مخالفينا ؛ لأن الله عز وجل قد ابتدأ إبليس على قولهم كما ابتدأ آدم عليه السلام ، وليس تخلو النعمتان أن يكونا عني بهما بدن آدم عليه السلام أو يكونا عرضين خلقا في بدن آدم عليه السلام ، فلو كان عنى بدن آدم فالأبدان عند مخالفينا من المعتزلة جنس واحد وإذا كانت الأبدان عندهم جنساً واحداً فقد حصل في جسد إبليس على مذهبهم من النعمة ما حصل في جسد آدم عليه السلام، وكذلك إن عني عرضين فليس من عرض فَعَلَهُ في بدن آدم عليه السلام من لون أو حياة أو قوة أو غير ذلك إلا وقد فعل من جنسه عندهم في بدن إبليس، وهذا يوجب أنه لا فضيلة لآدم عليه السلام على إبليس في ذلك، وإنما احتج على إبليس بذلك ليريه أن لآدم عليه السلام في ذلك فضيلة. فدل ما قلناه على أن الله عز وجل لما قال : لِمَا خَلَقْتُ بِيَدَيَّ ) لم يعن نعمتي .
And also, if the meaning of His saying Almighty: 'بِيَدَيَّ' were 'My two blessings', then there would be no virtue for Adam, peace be upon him, over Iblis in that according to the school of our opponents; because Allah Almighty had favored Iblis in their view just as He favored Adam, peace be upon him. And the two blessings are not free from being either meant as the body of Adam, peace be upon him, or being two accidents created in the body of Adam. If He meant the body of Adam, then bodies according to our opponents from the Mu'tazila are one genus, and if bodies are one genus according to them, then there occurred in Iblis's body in their school of the blessing what occurred in Adam's body. Likewise if He meant two accidents, there is no accident that He made in Adam's body of color, life, strength, or other than that except that He has made from its genus according to them in Iblis's body. This necessitates that there is no virtue for Adam over Iblis in that. And He only argued against Iblis with that to show him that Adam had a virtue in that. So what we have said indicates that Allah Almighty when He said: 'لِمَا خَلَقْتُ بِيَدَيَّ' did not mean 'My two blessings'.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is a proof (dalil) from the context of the Quranic story of Adam and Iblis. Imam Ashari argues that if 'بيدي' meant 'My two blessings', then Adam would have no special honor over Iblis, because both received blessings — bodies and accidents — of the same kind according to the Mu'tazila. Since the verse (Saad 75) is clearly meant to show Adam's distinction, 'بيدي' cannot mean blessings. The argument proceeds by analyzing two possibilities: the blessings are either the body itself or accidents in the body. In both cases, Iblis also received the same type of blessings (body and accidents). Therefore, no distinction. The conclusion directly refutes the interpretation of 'بيدي' as blessings.

Key Terms
نعمة
فضيلة
بدن
عرض
مخالفون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazilite interpretation that 'بيدي' refers to Allah's blessings is consistent with the verse's message of Adam's honor.
Correction: Imam Ashari shows that if it meant blessings, Adam would have no unique honor because Iblis received the same kind of blessings, contradicting the verse's clear implication.

Checkpoint

A) Because blessings cannot be attributed to Allah
B) Because Iblis also received the same kind of blessings, so Adam would have no virtue
C) Because the word 'يد' never means blessing in Arabic
D) Because the Mu'tazila denied that Allah has any hands

Key Takeaway
Imam Ashari shows that the 'blessings' interpretation of 'بيدي' would eliminate Adam's unique honor, contradicting the verse's purpose.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Refuting the Objection: Allah's Hands Are Not Limbs
Imam Ashari refutes the objection that non-blessing hands must be limbs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Ashari uses the principle of tanzih to refute the claim that Allah's hands must be corporeal limbs, by highlighting the inconsistency in the opponents' own method.

Core Idea
The same logic that affirms Allah's life unlike ours also allows His hands unlike limbs.

In this passage, Imam Ashari responds to an objection that if 'hands' in the Qur'an are not blessings, they must be physical limbs. He exposes the flaw in this reasoning by pointing out that the opponents themselves affirm other divine attributes that are unlike creation. This lesson will walk through his argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Read the first part of the passage where Ashari presents the opponents' claim: if 'hand' is not a blessing, it must be a limb. Notice how he frames it as a dialogue.
The opponents are likely Mu'tazila or other rationalists who reject anthropomorphism.
2
Follow the reductio ad absurdum
Ashari then applies the opponents' own method consistently: if they analogize from the witnessed world for hands, they must also for life and body. But they do not, as they affirm that Allah is a living being unlike bodies.
This exposes a contradiction in their application of qiyas.
3
See the conclusion about consistency
The argument concludes that consistency demands affirming hands that are neither blessings nor limbs, just as they affirm a wise manager unlike humans. The passage ends with a call not to deny this due to contradiction with the witnessed.
This reinforces the Ash'ari principle of affirming attributes without tashbih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقال لهم : لم أنكرتم أن يكون الله عز وجل عنى بقوله : ( يَدَيَّ ) يدين ليستا نعمتين؟ فإن قالوا: لأن اليد إذا لم تكن نعمة لم تكن إلا جارحة . قيل لهم : ولم قضيتم أن اليد إذا لم تكن نعمة لم تكن إلا جارحة؟ فإن رجعونا إلى شاهدنا أو إلى ما نجده فيما بيننا من الخلق، فقالوا اليد إذا لم تكن نعمة في الشاهد لم تكن إلا جارحة . قيل لهم : إن حملتم على الشاهد وقضيتم به على الله عز وجل، فكذلك لم نجد حياً من الخلق إلا جسماً لحماً ودماً فاقضوا بذلك على الله عز وجل - تعالى عن ذلك - وإلا كنتم لقولكم تاركين ولاعتلالكم ناقضين، وإن أثبتم حياً لا كالأحياء منا، فلم أنكرتم أن تكون اليدان اللتان أخبر الله عز وجل عنهما يدين ليستا نعمتين، ولا جارحتين، ولا كالأيدي؟ وكذلك يقال لهم : لم تجدوا مدبراً حكيماً إلا إنساناً، ثم أثبتم أن للدنيا مدبراً حكيماً ليس كالإنسان، وخالفتم الشاهد ونقضتم اعتلالكم فلا تمنعوا من إثبات يدين ليستا نعمتين ولا جارحتين من أجل أن ذلك خلاف الشاهد
And it is said to them: Why did you deny that Allah Almighty meant by His saying: 'يَدَيَّ' two hands that are not two blessings? If they say: Because the hand when it is not a blessing is nothing but a limb. It is said to them: Why did you rule that the hand when it is not a blessing is nothing but a limb? If they refer us to our witnessed [world] or to what we find among us of creation, and they say: The hand when it is not a blessing in the witnessed is nothing but a limb. It is said to them: If you rely on the witnessed and rule by it upon Allah Almighty, then likewise we do not find a living being among creation except as a body of flesh and blood, so rule by that upon Allah Almighty — exalted is He above that — otherwise you would be abandoning your statement and contradicting your argument. And if you affirm a living being not like the living beings from us, then why do you deny that the two hands which Allah Almighty informed of are two hands that are not two blessings, nor two limbs, nor like hands? And likewise it is said to them: You did not find a wise manager except a human, then you affirmed that the universe has a wise manager not like a human, and you contradicted the witnessed and violated your argument. So do not prevent affirming two hands that are neither two blessings nor two limbs because that contradicts the witnessed.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer (mas'ala) refuting the claim that if 'يد' is not a blessing, it must be a limb. Imam Ashari uses a reductio ad absurdum: the objectors apply the rule from the witnessed world (shahid) to Allah for hands, but they do not apply it for other attributes like life or management. They affirm that Allah is a living being unlike human bodies, and that He is a wise manager unlike human managers. So consistency demands they also affirm hands unlike human limbs. The argument highlights the Ash'ari principle of tanzih (transcendence) and the method of qiyas al-gha'ib 'ala ash-shahid with due consideration of dissimilarity.

Key Terms
شاهد
غائب
جارحة
نعمة
تشبيه
تنزيه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Ash'ari position is anthropomorphic because they affirm hands.
Correction: The Ash'aris affirm hands that are unlike any created hands, consistent with their principle of tanzih.

Checkpoint
How does Imam Ashari refute the objection that non-blessing hands must be limbs?
A) By arguing that the word 'يد' has many meanings
B) By pointing out that the same opponents affirm Allah's life and management while denying likeness to creation
C) By quoting a verse that says Allah's hands are not limbs
D) By saying that the Mu'tazila have no proof

Key Takeaway
Imam Ashari shows that affirming divine hands unlike creation is consistent with the Ash'ari method of affirming attributes without likeness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever unconsciously imagine Allah with qualities resembling creation, even though you know He is unlike anything? Where in your heart do you find this tendency strongest? Commit today to actively replace any such thought with the declaration 'laysa kamithlihi shay' (nothing is like Him).
?
The same logic that allows you to say 'Allah is Alive, but not like our life' also forces you to say 'Allah has Hands, but not like our hands.' Are you consistent in applying divine transcendence across all attributes, or do you secretly struggle with some? Why? What would it mean for your worship if you truly internalized that every attribute of Allah is beyond human comprehension?
?
Imagine you are standing before Allah on the Day of Judgment and He asks you about your understanding of His names and attributes. Would you be able to say that you purified your belief from any trace of anthropomorphism, or will you admit that you let your imagination paint a limited picture of Him? Take a moment to repent from any such shortcoming and resolve to learn and affirm His attributes as the Salaf did.
